Bretous)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/2c7242e4-ad54-4f63-8627-a15aa6a2ea50.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn67@2020_3/2022/03/14/08-15-06-886_50ccf56f10c400b5.webp","https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/TikTok%20Trends%20B2B%20and%20B2C%20Marketers%20Should%20Watch%20in%202022-1.jpeg?width=250&name=TikTok%20Trends%20B2B%20and%20B2C%20Marketers%20Should%20Watch%20in%202022-1.jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn90@2020_5/2022/03/14/08-15-14-896_3d1146286eb2a07c.webp","https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/TikTok%20Trends%20B2B%20and%20B2C%20Marketers%20Should%20Watch%20in%202022-4.jpeg?width=250&name=TikTok%20Trends%20B2B%20and%20B2C%20Marketers%20Should%20Watch%20in%202022-4.jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx8/cdn61@2020_5/2022/03/14/08-15-14-114_c6e8a2971d2c22ba.webp","https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/TikTok%20Trends%20B2B%20and%20B2C%20Marketers%20Should%20Watch%20in%202022-2.jpeg?width=250&name=TikTok%20Trends%20B2B%20and%20B2C%20Marketers%20Should%20Watch%20in%202022-2.jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx12/cdn68@2020_5/2022/03/14/08-15-10-011_36c6c63bc8ef1413.webp","https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/TikTok%20Trends%20B2B%20and%20B2C%20Marketers%20Should%20Watch%20in%202022-3.jpeg?width=300&name=TikTok%20Trends%20B2B%20and%20B2C%20Marketers%20Should%20Watch%20in%202022-3.jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx24/cdn45@2020_1/2022/03/14/08-15-13-585_02778552e412373d.webp","https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/TikTok%20Trends%20B2B%20and%20B2C%20Marketers%20Should%20Watch%20in%202022.jpeg?width=300&name=TikTok%20Trends%20B2B%20and%20B2C%20Marketers%20Should%20Watch%20in%202022.jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx19/cdn68@2020_5/2022/03/14/08-15-09-925_732dd4e77ae02bad.webp","https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/7a03a7b4-d90f-4c86-b845-fae9305669ea.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn30@2020_2/2022/03/14/08-15-09-790_4634eb1b7855c84c.webp","https://track.hubspot.com/__ptq.gif?a=53&k=14&r=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.hubspot.com%2Fmarketing%2Ftiktok-trends&bu=https%253A%252F%252Fblog.hubspot.com%252Fmarketing&bvt=rss":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx8/cdn97@2020_5/2022/03/14/08-15-15-799_cf392374aa95eace.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1647245705114},{"createdTime":"2022-03-14 16:15:05","updatedTime":"2022-03-14 16:15:05","title":"16 of the Best Job Interview Questions to Ask Candidates (And What to Look for in Their Answers)","link":"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/great-interview-questions","description":"<p>When you're <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/recruitment\">interviewing people to join your team</a>, you have to get creative — after all, there's only so much that questions like \"What's your biggest weakness?\" and \"Are you a team player?\" reveal about who your candidates truly are.</p> \n<p>But what are the best interview questions to ask that will help you uncover your candidate's strengths, weaknesses, and interests?</p> \n<p>To help give you some ideas for the next time you're meeting with a job candidate, here are some of the best job interview questions to ask, plus good answers to each question.</p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=9cd76457-ee12-40f6-b9d3-53674b1f7714&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; margin: 0 auto; display: block; margin-top: 20px; margin-bottom: 20px\" alt=\"Download Now: 100 Marketing Interview Questions [Free Access]\" src=\"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/9cd76457-ee12-40f6-b9d3-53674b1f7714.png\" align=\"middle\"></a></p> \n<br> \n<h3 style=\"font-weight: normal;\">Questions to Test a Candidate's Honesty and Sense of Ownership&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</h3> \n<h4>1. \"What single project or task would you consider your most significant career accomplishment to date?\"</h4> \n<p>Lou Adler, author of <em>The Essential Guide for Hiring &amp; Getting Hired</em> and <em>Hire With Your Head</em>, <a href=\"http://www.inc.com/lou-adler/best-interview-question-ever.html\">spent 10 years</a> searching for the single best interview question that will reveal whether to hire or not hire a candidate — and this was the one.</p> \n<h5>A good answer to this question:</h5> \n<p>Candidates' answers will tell you about their prior success and sense of ownership. A great answer will show they are confident in their work and professional choices while being humble enough to show they care about the <em>company's</em> success. For example, if a candidate built a sales or marketing campaign they're particularly proud of, listen for them to explain how the business benefited from it. Did it help the company sign a major client?</p> \n<h4>2. \"Is it better to be perfect and late, or good and on time?\"</h4> \n<p>If your candidate responds with \"It depends,\" hear them out — the interview question itself is phrased in such a way that candidates can sense there is a right and wrong answer, and they'll be looking for signs from you that they're heading in the right direction.</p> \n<h5>A good answer to this question:</h5> \n<p>For most companies, the correct answer is \"good and on time.\" It's important to let something be finished when it's good enough. Let's face it, every blog post, email, book, video, etc. can <em>always</em> be tweaked and improved. At some point, you've just got to ship it. Most managers don't want someone who can't hit deadlines because they're paralyzed by perfection.</p> \n<p>Try to remain neutral as they feel out their response, though. They might not be able to relate to work that's measured purely by quality and deadline, but it's important that they can express how they prioritize their tasks.</p> \n<h4>3. \"Tell me about a time you screwed up.\"</h4> \n<p>An oldie but goodie. This is a tried-and-true test for self-awareness. (Honestly, well-prepared candidates should see it coming and have an answer ready.) Someone who takes ownership of their mess-up and learns something from it is usually humble and mindful. Candidates who blame others or give a \"fake\" screw-up (something like \"I worked too hard and burned out.\") are red flags.</p> \n<h5>A good answer to this question:</h5> \n<p>A good answer to this question will do two things well:</p> \n<ul> \n <li><strong>Admit to a genuine mistake.</strong> Often candidates will dress up a mistake with a self-compliment or excuse to avoid looking weak. For example, <em>\"I was so committed to X that I overlooked Y.\"</em> On the contrary, good answers will just show that they miscalculated, plain and simple.</li> \n <li><strong>Explain what they learned from it.</strong> It's one thing to screw up, but it's another thing to take that screw-up as an opportunity to improve. Great companies learn more from failure than they do from success — candidates who do too are exactly what you need to grow.</li> \n</ul> \n<p style=\"font-weight: normal;\"></p> \n<h3 style=\"font-weight: normal;\">Questions to Test a Candidate's Work Ethic</h3> \n<h4>4. \"Tell me about a time you set difficult goals.\"</h4> \n<p>If you're looking for a candidate who is goal-oriented and results-driven — as most hiring managers are — this question will help you gauge whether they'll be able to handle the audacious goals you have in store for them. Ask follow-up questions like, \"What did you do to achieve them?\" Have the candidate walk you through the process and purpose of the goals they set out for themselves.</p> \n<h5>A good answer to this question:</h5> \n<p>A good answer to this interview question shows they understand what difficult goals are, and that they put a lot of effort into attaining their goals while maintaining a high standard of work quality. Listen for answers that describe a lofty goal and show <em>why</em> this goal challenged their normal targets. Responses that admit the candidate came up short of this goal can also indicate self-awareness and confidence despite a lack of success.</p> \n<h4>5. \"What have you done professionally that is not an experience you'd want to repeat?\"</h4> \n<p>A candidate's answer to this question will give you an idea of how they viewed work they weren't very happy with, which is bound to happen to everyone in every job at one point or another.</p> \n<h5>A good answer to this question:</h5> \n<p>HubSpot's VP of Customer Service and Support <a href=\"https://www.linkedin.com/in/mredbord\">Michael Redbord</a> says candidates' answers generally fall into a few categories:</p> \n<ol> \n <li><strong>Something menial</strong> (e.g. envelope-stuffing). Pay attention to whether they understand the value of this getting done for the business, or whether they just think they're too good for a job like that.</li> \n <li><strong>Something really hard.</strong> Why was it hard? Was it because it was poorly planned, poorly executed, or something else? Where do they put the blame on it being such an unpleasant experience?</li> \n <li><strong>Something team-related.</strong> Follow up with questions about the team, what their role on the team was, and so on.</li> \n</ol> \n<p>Even the category of what they consider an experience they wouldn't want to repeat is interesting, says Redbord. When you talk about extreme experiences that get people emotional, it can be very revealing. Keep in mind, however, that good answers don't have to fall into any one category — what's most important is if they extracted value from the experience despite their lack of interest in doing it again.</p> \n<h4>6. \"What is your definition of hard work?\"</h4> \n<p>Some organizations move at very different paces, and this question is an effective way to tell whether your candidate will be able to keep pace with the <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/how-to-build-a-marketing-team\">rest of your team and add value to your team</a>. It also helps you identify someone who is a \"hard worker in disguise,\" meaning someone who might currently be at a slow-moving organization or in a role that is not well-suited to them, but wants to work somewhere where they can really get their hands dirty.</p> \n<h5>A good answer to this question:</h5> \n<p>A good answer doesn't have to produce evidence of hard work — it should rather reveal if your candidate knows what it takes to get something done and solve the problems it was designed to solve.</p> \n<p>Answers that talk about working hard by working <em>smart</em> are great, as well. Always listen for this — putting in the work to find the <em>best way</em> of doing something is often just as important as the task itself.</p> \n<h4>7. \"Who is the smartest person you know personally? Why?\"</h4> \n<p>These questions test what the candidate values and aspires to by forcing them to think of a real person they know, and then articulate what makes that person smart.</p> \n<h5>A good answer to this question:</h5> \n<p>Ideal answers vary, but could include specific examples of the person they've chosen's ability to think ahead several steps and execute. They could also touch on the person's decision-making skills, ability to connect, desire for learning, or application of the things they learned.</p> \n<h4>8. \"What’s the biggest decision you’ve had to make in the past year? Why was it so big?\"</h4> \n<p>Here's a great way to figure out how a candidate approaches decision-making. Were they quick to make that big decision, or did it take them a long time? Did they spend most of their time reflecting on it by themselves or fleshing it out with others? How did they make a plan?</p> \n<h5>A good answer to this question:</h5> \n<p>Candidates' answers could be work-related or personal. In addition to revealing their thought process, as described above, an effective response to this interview question will also show how the candidate was able to prioritize what was most important when each possible option might have had its own advantages and disadvantages.</p> \n<p>If your candidate had hiring power in a previous position, for example, maybe they found it hard to choose between two job candidates of their own. A good answer might show that they saw immediate skill in one candidate but long-term potential in the other. Although both people had usable strengths, your candidate chose the second person because he or she offered he best return on investment.</p> \n<p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/best%20interview%20questions-1.png?width=1080&amp;name=best%20interview%20questions-1.png\" alt=\"best interview questions\" width=\"1080\" style=\"width: 1080px;\"></p> \n<h3>Questions to Test a Candidate's Interests, Passions, &amp; Working Style&nbsp;</h3> \n<h4>9. \"Tell me about the relationships you've had with the people you've worked with. How would you describe the best ones? The worst?\"</h4> \n<p>Each team is different, so this question helps you tease out whether the candidate would be happy, productive, and well liked on <em>your </em>team. Their answer will tell you how they interact with others — and which kinds of interactions they <em>want</em> to happen.</p> \n<h5>A good answer to this question:</h5> \n<p>Answers to this question don't have to focus on just professional elements of a relationship with colleagues — they can also be related to business culture. Maybe the candidate enjoyed their coworker's positivity or thought their attitude lowered morale. Good responses aren't one-sided, though. Look for answers that explain how their colleague's work style thrived (or conflicted) with their own — not simply what their colleague did that benefited or offended them.</p> \n<p>Many candidates are hesitant to bad-mouth their coworkers and bosses, so it'll be interesting for you to hear how they navigate a question about their worst working relationships.</p> \n<h4>10. \"In five minutes, could you explain something to me that is complicated but you know well?\"</h4> \n<p>This is a much better test of intelligence than a college GPA, and it's also a great gauge of a candidate's passion and charisma outside of their core job responsibilities. Candidates who are passionate and knowledgeable about something — and can convey that well — are more likely to be enthusiastic and influential at work.</p> \n<h5>A good answer to this question:</h5> \n<p>The \"something\" in this question doesn't have to be work-related — it can be a hobby, a sports team, something technical ... anything, really. Good responses will tell you how well your candidate comprehends complex subjects and that they can articulate that subject to someone who doesn't know much about it.</p> \n<p>Explanations that use analogies also make good answers, especially if it's a topic that is filled with industry jargon. This shows that the candidate can solve problems by drawing comparisons to things that are more universally understood.</p> \n<h4>11. \"If I were to poll everyone you've worked with, what percentage would not be a fan of yours?\"</h4> \n<p>At work, you can't please everyone all the time. The answer to this question will help you find out if your candidate has enough drive and conviction in their own work to have ever conflicted with one or more of their colleagues.</p> \n<p>Obviously you don't want the candidate to be an unlikable person, though, so consider asking follow-up questions to find out <em>why</em> they might have alienated these coworkers: \"If I were to interview these people, what words would they most frequently use to describe you?\"</p> \n<h5>A good answer to this question:</h5> \n<p>The follow-up question about word choice is more important than the percentage they give in the initial question. In their answers, you should be encouraged by words like \"passionate\" and concerned by words like \"lazy.\"</p> \n<p>Of course, not all negative words are red flags — while words that indicate a lack of work ethic might be a bad sign, words like \"stubborn\" could show a candidate's self-awareness — and commitment to things their coworkers would rather move on from.</p> \n<h4>12. \"What is something you'd be happy doing every single day for the rest of your career?\"</h4> \n<p>While it's important to hire for skill, it's also important to hire someone who's likely to be happy in the job for which you're hiring. A question like this one will help uncover what makes each candidate happy at work — which is a great way to gauge whether they'd enjoy their role and stay at the company for a long time.</p> \n<h5>A good answer to this question:</h5> \n<p>There's no right answer to this question — it's more of a learning opportunity for you to see what your employees most enjoy in the industry. Nonetheless, a candidate's answer to this question should align with the core responsibilities of the job for which they're applying.</p> \n<p>A sales candidate who says they could lead client kickoff meetings every day, for example, is a much better fit than a sales candidate who prefers to create lead-generating campaigns (a task that shows a bigger interest in the marketing side of things).</p> \n<h4>13. \"If you had $40,000 to build your own business, what would you do?\"</h4> \n<p>This question is a favorite of HubSpot Marketing Team Development Manager <a href=\"https://www.linkedin.com/in/ekueffner\">Emily MacIntyre</a>. First, the type of business they choose to talk about can reveal a lot about their interests, values, and how creative they are. Second, it'll give you insight into how business-savvy they are. By giving them a specific amount to work with (in this case, $40,000), they have the opportunity to parse out how they'd spend that money.</p> \n<h5>A good answer to this question:</h5> \n<p>The best answers to this question will get specific: They'll offer an overview of the business <em>and </em>get into the logistics of where that money would go, whom they'd hire first, and so on.</p> \n<h3>Questions to Test a Candidate's Knowledge or Interest in Your Specific Company</h3> \n<h4>14. \"Pitch our company to me as if I were buying our product/service.\"</h4> \n<p>This is a unique and more challenging approach to the generic \"What does our company do?\" question. It forces candidates to not only drum up the research they've done to prepare for the interview, but also show they can use this research to craft a persuasive message that would be valuable in a business situation.</p> \n<h5>A good answer to this question:</h5> \n<p>This will come more naturally to some candidates than others. Above all, good answers to this interview question are able to combine an accurate definition of your company with what it offers to your core customer that they need or can't get anywhere else.</p> \n<p>Keep in mind that someone interviewing for a sales or marketing position might find it easier than someone interviewing for a non-client facing role — and that's okay. You aren't necessarily assessing their delivery. But it'll be interesting to see how each candidate thinks through and gives their response.</p> \n<h4>15. \"What has surprised you about this interview process so far?\"</h4> \n<p>This is a question no candidate can really prepare for, and it'll give you some indication of how candidates are feeling about the whole thing. Plus, you can see how they think on their feet.</p> \n<h5>A good answer to this question:</h5> \n<p>You're looking for specifics here — something about the office space; the personality of the team; an assignment they were given to complete.</p> \n<p>Honest answers are good answers, and answers that are directed at <em>you</em> are even better, as they show the candidate is confident speaking their mind in front of decision-makers. For instance, maybe the candidate was surprised you asked them about something on their resume that they don't personally pay much attention to.</p> \n<h4>16. \"Do you have any questions for me?\"</h4> \n<p>This is another classic interview question, and like the one above, you're seeing how candidates think on their feet. The answer to this question also reveals what's important to the candidate. Are they wondering about company culture, or compensation? Are they curious about growth potential, or learning opportunities?</p> \n<h5>A good answer to this question:</h5> \n<p>There are no right or wrong answers, but personality and communication style are important factors when considering hiring someone to join your team, and you can get a sense of these factors with their answer.</p> \n<p><em><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=b15f5ee5-9381-4b6d-b503-a5f8997d6eff&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; \" alt=\"marketing questions\" src=\"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/b15f5ee5-9381-4b6d-b503-a5f8997d6eff.png\"></a></em></p> \n<p><em></em></p>  \n<img src=\"https://track.hubspot.com/__ptq.gif?a=53&amp;k=14&amp;r=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.hubspot.com%2Fmarketing%2Fgreat-interview-questions&amp;bu=https%253A%252F%252Fblog.hubspot.com%252Fmarketing&amp;bvt=rss\" alt=\"\" width=\"1\" height=\"1\" style=\"min-height:1px!important;width:1px!important;border-width:0!important;margin-top:0!important;margin-bottom:0!important;margin-right:0!important;margin-left:0!important;padding-top:0!important;padding-bottom:0!important;padding-right:0!important;padding-left:0!important; \">","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Tue, 22 Feb 2022 12:00:00 +0000","feedId":54,"bgimg":"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/9cd76457-ee12-40f6-b9d3-53674b1f7714.png","linkMd5":"6387f16bdee8fb38e290119420a2e2f8","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn7@2020_5/2022/03/14/08-15-05-651_5f40cc83585676b8.webp","destWidth":604,"destHeight":59,"sourceBytes":6896,"destBytes":9546,"author":"lkolowich@hubspot.com (Lindsay Kolowich Cox)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/9cd76457-ee12-40f6-b9d3-53674b1f7714.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn7@2020_5/2022/03/14/08-15-05-651_5f40cc83585676b8.webp","https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/best%20interview%20questions-1.png?width=1080&name=best%20interview%20questions-1.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn18@2020_4/2022/03/14/08-15-10-950_23c2f1b0f7b8a396.webp","https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/b15f5ee5-9381-4b6d-b503-a5f8997d6eff.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx8/cdn75@2020_3/2022/03/14/08-15-10-063_90aed6fd7d43f179.webp","https://track.hubspot.com/__ptq.gif?a=53&k=14&r=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.hubspot.com%2Fmarketing%2Fgreat-interview-questions&bu=https%253A%252F%252Fblog.hubspot.com%252Fmarketing&bvt=rss":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn71@2020_6/2022/03/14/08-15-10-565_a4548ece2e4ad5d2.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1647245705083},{"createdTime":"2022-03-14 16:15:05","updatedTime":"2022-03-14 16:15:05","title":"How 500 Marketers are Leveraging Instagram Shopping Tools [Data]","link":"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/instagram-shopping-data","description":"<p>Does anyone remember the days when all we saw on Instagram were poorly lit pictures our friends took and memes we didn’t want our parents to see on Facebook? Well, we’re long gone from then.</p> \n<p>The platform has evolved from a simple image-sharing social platform to a money-making content curation one. With the addition of Instagram’s shopping tools, it’s steering more toward ecommerce and less on the social aspect.</p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=9294dd33-9827-4b39-8fc2-b7fbece7fdb9&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; \" alt=\"New Data: Instagram Engagement Report [2022 Version]\" src=\"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/9294dd33-9827-4b39-8fc2-b7fbece7fdb9.png\"></a></p> \n<p>So what does that mean for brands? We surveyed over 500 marketers to learn more about their Instagram strategy. Find out below what we found out as it relates to the social platform’s shopping tools.</p> \n<h2>The Benefits and Challenges of Instagram’s Shopping Tools</h2> \n<p>When we asked marketers the biggest benefit of using Instagram’s shopping tools, their number one answer was the increased product discoverability.</p> \n<p>In the past, users had to navigate to a brand’s website to get product or service details. Today, they can learn everything they need to know about it. In addition, Instagram’s \"wishlist\" feature also allows users to save products they like to a specific folder on the app.</p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><img alt=\"lucid poll asking &quot;do consumers shop on social media?&quot; Results show that 24.5% say they have shopped on instagram. \" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20500%20Marketers%20are%20Leveraging%20Instagram%20Shopping%20Tools%20%5BData%5D.png?width=500&amp;name=How%20500%20Marketers%20are%20Leveraging%20Instagram%20Shopping%20Tools%20%5BData%5D.png\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block; width: 500px;\" title=\"lucid poll asking &quot;do consumers shop on social media?&quot; Results show that 24.5% say they have shopped on instagram. \" width=\"500\"></p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center; font-size: 12px;\"><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/do-consumers-shop-directly-on-social-media-platforms\">Image Source</a></p> \n<p>The second biggest benefit is the simplified shopping experience. Gone are the days when you need to leave the app to make the purchase. You can discover a brand and make a purchase all in the same breath. This means a more enjoyable process for consumers, which can lead to more purchases for brands.</p> \n<p>Another key advantage Instagram’s shopping tools offer is the ability to easily partner with influencers.</p> \n<p>Currently, creators can tag easily the products they’re promoting and <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/do-consumers-shop-directly-on-social-media-platforms?_ga=2.29777660.2134660075.1645397012-1770650723.1645397012\">send traffic directly to the brand’s Shop page</a>.</p> \n<p>In addition, Instagram is <a href=\"https://business.instagram.com/creators/earn-money/affiliate\">currently testing an affiliate program</a>, in which influencers have their own Shop page.</p> \n<p><img alt=\"instagram affiliate program for influencers\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20500%20Marketers%20are%20Leveraging%20Instagram%20Shopping%20Tools%20%5BData%5D-2.jpeg?width=500&amp;name=How%20500%20Marketers%20are%20Leveraging%20Instagram%20Shopping%20Tools%20%5BData%5D-2.jpeg\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block; width: 500px;\" title=\"\" width=\"500\"></p> \n<p>This allows users to easily find products recommended by their favorite influencers and make a purchase seamlessly.</p> \n<p>Now, onto the not-so-great obstacles of Instagram’s shopping tools.</p> \n<p>The biggest thing marketers surveyed complained about is supply-chain issues following many purchases. Since the pandemic, this has been a common hurdle for many businesses, as manufacturers deal with month- or year-long backlogs.</p> \n<p>Another concern marketers are facing is not generating enough revenue from utilizing <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/instagram-shopping-tools\">Instagram’s shopping tools</a> or having access to certain features.</p> \n<p>37% of marketers also complained about <a href=\"https://www.facebook.com/business/help/223030991929920?id=533228987210412\">Instagram’s selling fees</a>, which is currently 5% per shipment, or a flat fee of $0.40 for shipments of $8.00 or less. For brands, this is an additional cost that they could avoid by directing traffic to their website instead.</p> \n<p>Another big concern is the loss of user data. When Instagram serves as the end-to-end platform, brands can lose valuable data to inform future strategies.</p> \n<p>Now that you know the pros and cons of the shopping tools, let’s break down how marketers are using them.</p> \n<h2>How Marketers Leverage Instagram Shopping Tools</h2> \n<p>From the marketers we surveyed in our HubSpot Blog Research, 32% currently leverage Instagram Shops in their marketing strategy, and 48% plan to increase their investment in 2022.</p> \n<p>While some brands tried the shopping tools as soon as it was introduced, others are just now diving in. In fact, 36% of marketers will be increasing their investment in Instagram Shops <em>for the first time</em> this year.</p> \n<p>Meanwhile, 14% of marketers will be prioritizing Instagram Shops above all other features in 2022.</p> \n<p>However, one thing to note is that when compared to all the features available on Instagram, marketers say its shopping tools don’t offer a high ROI when it comes to leads. Posting content and going live offer much better results.</p> \n<p>With that said, while it may not be ideal for driving leads, it may work well for meeting other marketing goals.</p> \n<p><img alt=\"instagram shopping tools\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20500%20Marketers%20are%20Leveraging%20Instagram%20Shopping%20Tools%20%5BData%5D.jpeg?width=500&amp;name=How%20500%20Marketers%20are%20Leveraging%20Instagram%20Shopping%20Tools%20%5BData%5D.jpeg\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block; width: 500px;\" title=\"\" width=\"500\"></p> \n<p>Out of all shopping features available on Instagram (Shop tab, product tagging, guides, Live shopping), the Shop tab is the most used tool by 47% of marketers surveyed.</p> \n<p>However, in terms of ROI, it’s in the #2 spot. What’s on top? Instagram Shopping from Creators, which allows influencers to tag the products they’re using in an image or video.</p> \n<p>As for shopping tools by format: It looks like in-feed shopping, Stories shopping, and Guides shopping are used at the same rate by over one in three marketers.</p> \n<h2>How Marketers Approach Product Launches on Instagram</h2> \n<p>One of the most interesting findings from our research is that for many brands, Instagram’s shopping tools are their sole ecommerce platform.</p> \n<p>In fact, 41% of marketers surveyed said most of the brands they work with use the platform’s shopping tools exclusively. The other 59% say their brands have a presence outside of the social platform via an ecommerce website.</p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><img alt=\"instagram in-feed shoppable post\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20500%20Marketers%20are%20Leveraging%20Instagram%20Shopping%20Tools%20%5BData%5D-1.jpeg?width=250&amp;name=How%20500%20Marketers%20are%20Leveraging%20Instagram%20Shopping%20Tools%20%5BData%5D-1.jpeg\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block; width: 250px;\" title=\"\" width=\"250\"></p> \n<p>So the question is, how do Instagram’s shopping tools impact a product launch? One in four marketers says it’s much better to launch a product exclusively on the platform.</p> \n<p>In fact, 83% of marketers surveyed say they have worked with a brand that launched a product exclusively on the platform.</p> \n<p>Conversely, 15% say launching a product/service exclusively on Instagram is worse than launching elsewhere.</p> \n<p>We’ve covered <em>a lot</em> here. One fact that’s clear is that more marketers will invest in Instagram’s shopping tools than they have in the past. What works well for one brand may not work for another, based on the audience, the audience, and more.</p> \n<p>So, don’t be afraid to experiment with all the features and analyze your data to figure out what offers the best return on investment for your company.</p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=b1268983-9da6-4d67-9d3a-cfef2d9f3cff&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; \" alt=\"Improve your website with effective technical SEO. Start by conducting this  audit.&nbsp;&nbsp;\" src=\"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/b1268983-9da6-4d67-9d3a-cfef2d9f3cff.png\"></a></p> \n<p></p>  \n<img
