Bretous)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/9294dd33-9827-4b39-8fc2-b7fbece7fdb9.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn10@2020_4/2022/03/14/08-15-05-665_7e54748a32aeb250.webp","https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20500%20Marketers%20are%20Leveraging%20Instagram%20Shopping%20Tools%20%5BData%5D.png?width=500&name=How%20500%20Marketers%20are%20Leveraging%20Instagram%20Shopping%20Tools%20%5BData%5D.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn91@2020_4/2022/03/14/08-15-12-750_5b578f90899f332d.webp","https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20500%20Marketers%20are%20Leveraging%20Instagram%20Shopping%20Tools%20%5BData%5D-2.jpeg?width=500&name=How%20500%20Marketers%20are%20Leveraging%20Instagram%20Shopping%20Tools%20%5BData%5D-2.jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn31@2020_4/2022/03/14/08-15-14-591_42fc6b30c25246e6.webp","https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20500%20Marketers%20are%20Leveraging%20Instagram%20Shopping%20Tools%20%5BData%5D.jpeg?width=500&name=How%20500%20Marketers%20are%20Leveraging%20Instagram%20Shopping%20Tools%20%5BData%5D.jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn93@2020_5/2022/03/14/08-15-27-207_77682495435bbcc1.webp","https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20500%20Marketers%20are%20Leveraging%20Instagram%20Shopping%20Tools%20%5BData%5D-1.jpeg?width=250&name=How%20500%20Marketers%20are%20Leveraging%20Instagram%20Shopping%20Tools%20%5BData%5D-1.jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn80@2020_3/2022/03/14/08-15-14-680_d4c2a72a8c4bc35c.webp","https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/b1268983-9da6-4d67-9d3a-cfef2d9f3cff.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn17@2020_3/2022/03/14/08-15-10-263_a4245cc995397db3.webp","https://track.hubspot.com/__ptq.gif?a=53&k=14&r=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.hubspot.com%2Fmarketing%2Finstagram-shopping-data&bu=https%253A%252F%252Fblog.hubspot.com%252Fmarketing&bvt=rss":null},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1647245705097},{"createdTime":"2022-03-14 16:15:05","updatedTime":"2022-03-14 16:15:05","title":"How to Be an Amazing Mentor in 10 Ways, according to HubSpot Managers","link":"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/mentor-tips-positive-impact","description":"<p>Take a minute to think about the best mentor you've ever had. It could be your manager, a colleague, a parent, a friend, a coach, a college professor.</p> \n<p>Then, you reach a point in your life where you have the chance to do the same for someone else. It can be both exciting, and a little confusing.</p> \n<a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=4e634041-e1ce-4a85-8e65-aea12fc10b84&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; \" alt=\"→ Click here to download leadership lessons from HubSpot founder, Dharmesh  Shah [Free Guide].\" src=\"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/4e634041-e1ce-4a85-8e65-aea12fc10b84.png\"></a> \n<p>In this article, you’ll get tips from both mentors and mentees on what it takes to foster this successful relationship.</p> \n<p></p> \n<h2>What does it mean to be a mentor?</h2> \n<p>At its core, being a mentor is being a trusted advisor. It all boils down to making yourself available to support and advise someone when they need it, delivering that support in a way that makes sense to them, and always keeping that person's best interests in mind.</p> \n<p>So, what value does a mentor bring? It depends on who you ask.</p> \n<p>For <a href=\"https://www.linkedin.com/in/vrnda-levalley\">Vrnda LeValley,</a> customer training manager at HubSpot, it’s a shift in perspective.</p> \n<p>\"My mentor provides a perspective that isn’t riddled with the same self-doubt and stereotype sensitivities that I desperately want to avoid and handicap me,\" she says, \"and a broader view of the implications of action versus inaction because they have a better vantage point from their upstream position within the company.\"</p> \n<p>She adds that her mentor has been able to step in and correct narratives that muddy her ability to make the most strategic decisions.</p> \n<p>For Legal Specialist at HubSpot <a href=\"https://www.linkedin.com/in/ronjay77\">Jason Perry,</a> one of the benefits of mentorship is the opportunity to extend your network.</p> \n<p>\"I most value the trust and confidence they extend to me by granting me access and recommending me to their broader networks,\" he said.</p> \n<p>Beyond that, there’s a certain freedom that comes with having a mentor.</p> \n<p>\"I think it allows for an open space to be vulnerable with someone who is more senior in their career but does not have direct control over your career growth,\" said <a href=\"https://www.linkedin.com/in/chloewashington\">Chloe Washington</a>, chief of staff to the CMO at HubSpot. \"You can be more transparent and ask questions you may not feel comfortable asking your manager or another co-worker.\"</p> \n<p>With that said, the mentorship doesn’t just benefit the mentee, it’s a two-sided relationship.</p> \n<p>\"I am constantly inspired by what my mentees are doing, their ambition, and their goals,\" Washington said. \"It motivates me as I continue along my career journey. It also allows me to form relationships with people that I may have not otherwise been able to speak with as much or as often.\"</p> \n<div>\n <iframe style=\"border: none; margin: 0px auto; display: block;\" src=\"https://listen.hubspot.com/embed/v2/smallPlayer/f0d5558d\" width=\"600\" height=\"337.5\"></iframe>  \n</div> \n<p></p> \n<h3>1. Understand what you want out of the relationship.</h3> \n<p>As we’ve mentioned, mentorship isn’t a one-way relationship. This means that just like the mentee, you should know the type of relationship you’re seeking and what you want to gain.</p> \n<p><a href=\"https://www.linkedin.com/in/charlene-strain-813a5a104\">Charlene Strain</a>, marketing manager at HubSpot, serves as a mentor and suggests asking yourself these questions to get started:</p> \n<ul> \n <li>Do you view it as a two-way street, player-coach relationship where you learn from them as much as they learn from you or something else?</li> \n <li>How can you sharpen your area of expertise?</li> \n <li>Do they have connections or gaps of knowledge for you as well?</li> \n <li>How does taking on a mentorship role strengthen you as a leader in your personal and professional life?</li> \n</ul> Knowing these answers will help you frame your mentorship strategy and start with clear intentions.\n<br> \n<h3>2. Set expectations together in the very beginning.</h3> \n<p>Once you know what you want out of the relationship as a mentor, setting expectations is the next natural step.</p> \n<p>Every mentor-mentee relationship is unique. So, when you first start out, discuss expectations with your mentee and determine if you’re ready for that commitment.</p> \n<p>\"Everyone works and receives feedback differently, so it's important to understand if the relationship is a fit for both parties [based] on what they're looking for,\" said Strain.</p> \n<p>Here’s what Strain recommends discussing:</p> \n<ul> \n <li>Is there a time limit on when the mentorship ends?</li> \n <li>How often should you meet, and why?</li> \n <li>What resources can the mentor provide for the mentee to do some work on their own?</li> \n <li>What metrics are being used to measure success?</li> \n <li>How hands-on should the mentor be?</li> \n</ul> \n<p>You should come to these answers as a duo and it’s OK if it takes a little bit to figure it out. The time you put in at the beginning will pay off in the long term.</p> \n<p>Some expectations are pretty straightforward, Perry says: professionalism, punctuality, clear communication, and organization. However, some expectations will be shaped by the mentee.</p> \n<p>\"A mentee should be able to tell me as the mentor exactly what they'd like me to do for them, whether it 's to provide information, make an introduction, write a recommendation or provide advice,\" says Perry. \"The relationship is theirs to shape and build and that starts with a clear, direct ask of some sort.\"</p> \n<p>When Washington works with mentees, her first session focuses on goal setting, setting up a meeting cadence, and discussing ground rules.</p> \n<p>\"For example, if there is a big topic to discuss, I request that they give me a heads up a few days before so that I can come fully prepared to discuss my point of view and not waste their time formulating my thoughts on the fly,\" she said.</p> \n<p>From there, she creates a running agenda doc to keep track of notes and have a place they can refer back to once the mentorship ends.</p> \n<h3>3. Take a genuine interest in your mentee as a person.</h3> \n<p>A mentor/mentee relationship is a very personal one.</p> \n<p>You can give mediocre advice without really knowing a person, but to stand out as an amazing mentor, you're really going to have to get to know your mentee on a personal level.</p> \n<p>You probably have some of the more career-oriented questions down: what their working style is, their dream job, goals for their current job, and so on and so forth. But what about the stuff that makes them ... <em>them? </em></p> \n<p>Getting to know your mentee on a deeper level will help you build a strong relationship, and it'll also help you understand who they are as a person and how they interact with others, and so on.</p> \n<p>One great way to get to know someone?<a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/active-listening-guide\"> </a><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/active-listening-guide\">Become an active listener</a>. This is easier said than done: It means making a conscious effort to really, truly pay attention to what your mentee is saying, instead of thinking about what you're going to say next.</p> \n<p>\"Two<a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/mentor-traits\"> traits that are helpful for someone to be a successful mentor</a> are good listening skills and the ability to connect like-minded people,\" said Strain. \"Our professional lives are not in a silo, they're a web. So, anyway I can truly listen to a mentee's goals, their journey, and where they see themselves will help me connect them with other people or businesses with the same mission.\"</p> \n<p>You might worry that you need to come up with something helpful right away, when in fact, the best thing you can do for your mentee is to listen closely to what they're saying, ask open questions to dig deeper and act as a sounding board.</p> \n<h3>4. Build trust.</h3> \n<p>In the last section, we stressed the vulnerability that comes with mentorship. To continue fostering a safe environment in which your mentee can share their concerns and challenges, you need to build trust.</p> \n<p>That can happen in a few different ways. For Solutions Engineer at HubSpot<a href=\"https://www.linkedin.com/in/sagaille\"> Jeremy Sagaille</a>, it’s transparency.</p> \n<p>\"I feel like I can really be myself in front of my mentor and I don't feel like I have to do the typical corporate political BS,\" he said, \"which is something that I've definitely had to tiptoe through in the past and haven't done well with.\"</p> \n<p>For LeValley, it’s the ability to see beyond the circumstance to assess the core issues, challenges, and opportunities.</p> \n<p>\"Those can get cloudy when you are on the road to a destination you have never visited before,\" she says. \"It makes all the difference when avoiding pitfalls and finding solid shortcuts.\"</p> \n<p>She adds that truth-telling is another valuable trait in a mentor.</p> \n<p>\"Many people haven’t been given the hard messages required for growth, due to lack of investment or lack of courage from those around them,\" she says. \"Personally, the best thing my mentor told me was to check in with my growth mindset and read a book. Not what I wanted to hear but it was 100% what I needed to hear.\"</p> \n<p>Once you build trust with your mentee, your relationship will be able to go that much deeper.</p> \n<h3>5. Know when to give advice.</h3> \n<p>When you're mentoring someone, you might feel pressured to give them advice straight away. But not all feedback is helpful feedback, and knowing the difference is key.</p> \n<p>A good mentor knows when to hit 'pause' during a conversation, says <a href=\"https://www.linkedin.com/in/rebeccacorliss\">Rebecca Corliss</a>, former director of marketing at HubSpot.</p> \n<p>\"If you don't have the right information, experience, or emotional state to react to a scenario properly, hit 'pause,\" she said. \"That will give you a chance to get more information, talk to your resources, and come back with a clear and valuable response.\"</p> \n<p>Here’s what that might look like in a real conversation.</p> \n<p><em>\"Thanks for sharing this with me. I'm going to take some time and give this some serious thought before we continue. It's important to me that I'm giving you the best possible solution. Why don't we continue talking about it [tomorrow/next week/next time we meet]? I'll book some time.\"</em></p> \n<h3>6. Don’t assume anything about your mentee – ask.</h3> \n<p>Biases cloud our judgment whether we realize it or not. While we can work to uncover and dismantle them, some are so ingrained that they peak out without us realizing it.</p> \n<p>To combat this issue with your mentee, breakthrough common assumptions by asking questions and digging deeper. This is especially important if you're mentoring someone who's in the early stages of their career</p> \n<p>Say you're mentoring someone who's having trouble getting through to their manager. Instead of launching into a story about a time you had communication issues with a manager of yours, spend time asking questions that draw out the important details of their problem.</p> \n<p>\"Your job is to facilitate advancement and movement, not just chat,\" says LeValley. \"Your words can change their lives so you must choose them carefully.\"</p> \n<p>Only once you've gotten an honest background on a problem can you share helpful, relevant feedback – without making decisions <em>for</em> your mentee.</p> \n<h3>7. Share your journey.</h3> \n<p>Being open to sharing your own mistakes and failures is one of the best gifts a mentor can give.</p> \n<p>Not only is it helpful information for problem-solving purposes, but it also builds trust and strengthens the relationship.</p> \n<p>\"Junior employees don't always feel comfortable owning up to a mistake or admitting that they're struggling in a certain area,\" says former Managing Director at HubSpot<a href=\"https://www.linkedin.com/in/emmajsnider\"> </a><a href=\"https://www.linkedin.com/in/emmajsnider\">Emma Brudner</a>. \"If you cop to your failures and struggles, you make it OK for them to chime in and help them share with you.\"</p> \n<p>Sagaille says that before his mentor, he often thought the struggles he faced were unique. However, he was reassured by his mentor, who had experience in his exact role.</p> \n<p>\"I'm just excited that I have a window into the future a little bit because she's dealt with similar issues and she's had some setbacks because of those issues,\" he says, \"so, she's able to steer me in the direction so I can avoid those pitfalls.\"</p> \n<p><a href=\"https://www.linkedin.com/in/lesliezye\">Leslie Ye</a>, content designer at HubSpot, suggests reflecting on the roadblocks you faced when you were in your mentee’s stage in life or career.</p> \n<p>\"Hearing how someone else approached a challenge is always helpful for someone going through it for the first time,\" she says. \"Even if you don't solve problems the same way as your mentee, it's always useful to hear multiple perspectives.\"</p> \n<p>Perry echoes this sentiment.</p> \n<p>\"Take time to tap into your own story,\" he says, \"Especially for Black mentors, it's important to relate and establish an interpersonal bond that fosters real talk – be a true resource in all facets.\"</p> \n<p>He adds that adversity of any kind our response to them is a foundational way to create relatability. Strain agrees, pointing to her non-traditional tech background before transitioning to the B2B Saas space.</p> \n<p>\"I'm extremely transparent about my own journey with a mentee. As I climb up the ladder as a Black woman in tech, it's important for me to continue reaching back down and helping others up as well,\" she says. \"If it wasn't for some of my own incredible mentors throughout my career, I wouldn't be a mentor now as well.\"</p> \n<h3>8. Celebrate their achievements.</h3> \n<p>Because people often look for or call upon a mentor to help them with tough situations, many mentorship conversations revolve around the stressful stuff.</p> \n<p>When you take the time to highlight and even celebrate your mentee's successes and achievements, you're also building your mentee's confidence and keeping them motivated.</p> \n<p>\"I've worked in a lot of places in the past that were very reserved with positive feedback and very lavish with constructive or negative feedback,\" said Sagaille. \"So I think that's something my mentor does really, really well – it's a nice balance.\"</p> \n<p>Some mentees also seek approval from their mentors. Acknowledging their success is a way to satisfy that psychological need for recognition.</p> \n<p>If you’re wondering <em>how </em>to celebrate their achievements, consider asking them what their love languages are. Those aren’t just helpful for personal relationships, they also work for professional ones as well.</p> \n<p>For instance, you may want to congratulate your mentee on a win by sending them a gift. However, if they value words of affirmation more, that’s the better way to go.</p> \n<h3>9. Seek out resources to help your mentee grow.</h3> \n<p>Great mentors look for situations – and some even create situations – to help their mentees get closer to their goals.</p> \n<p>It can be anything from connecting them with someone with experience in their dream job to recommending a conference they might be interested in. Take note of the areas in which your mentee wants to grow, and always be looking for opportunities to point them in the right direction.</p> \n<p>If you work at the same company as your mentee and have some involvement in their experience, Corliss suggests introducing new projects to them over time as a way to build a strong foundation.</p> \n<p>\"First, start with something that gives context. This could be something that requires research and is genuinely valuable,\" she says. \"Then, handoff something small that you normally do for your intern or mentee to own. This will help your mentee learn how to develop ownership over something, including how to execute and reach a goal on his or her own. Then, build upon that foundation.\"</p> \n<h3>10. Be sure you have the bandwidth.</h3> \n<p>LeValley believes mentorship is best when it’s approached as a calling instead of a task. With that in mind, it’s important to consider if you have the bandwidth to take it on.</p> \n<p>\"Be honest with yourself about what extent you are willing to give of your time and expertise,\" Strain says. \"This will help you manage your own workload and personal life easier without guilt or stretching yourself too thin.\"</p> \n<p>Washington echoes this sentiment and adds that it’s OK to bow out if you realize you don’t have the bandwidth.</p> \n<p>\"The relationship needs to be mutually beneficial and if you feel like you would be burdened by taking on the relationship, then be respectful to your prospective mentee and tell them that you’re not able to take on the relationship,\" she says. \"It’s better to be upfront than to waste anyone’s time.\"</p> \n<p>At the end of the day, being a great mentor takes practice and patience. The more you work with a given mentee, the more you'll learn a lot about them: their communication style, how they process feedback, how they go about pursuing their goals.</p> \n<p>The best part? It will likely be as rewarding an experience for you as it will be for your mentees.</p> \n<p><em>Editor's Note: This post was originally published in Jan. 2016 and has been updated for comprehensiveness. </em></p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=5174aed9-1caa-4a36-b2d6-84c4d96c25fb&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; \" alt=\"New Call-to-action\" src=\"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/5174aed9-1caa-4a36-b2d6-84c4d96c25fb.png\"></a></p>  \n<img src=\"https://track.hubspot.com/__ptq.gif?a=53&amp;k=14&amp;r=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.hubspot.com%2Fmarketing%2Fmentor-tips-positive-impact&amp;bu=https%253A%252F%252Fblog.hubspot.com%252Fmarketing&amp;bvt=rss\" alt=\"\" width=\"1\" height=\"1\" style=\"min-height:1px!important;width:1px!important;border-width:0!important;margin-top:0!important;margin-bottom:0!important;margin-right:0!important;margin-left:0!important;padding-top:0!important;padding-bottom:0!important;padding-right:0!important;padding-left:0!important; \">","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Mon, 28 Feb 2022 12:00:00 +0000","feedId":54,"bgimg":"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/4e634041-e1ce-4a85-8e65-aea12fc10b84.png","linkMd5":"8062f5ce2ddfcb1333f21fa686de0223","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn72@2020_4/2022/03/14/08-15-05-691_a76d18c90cdcfa92.webp","destWidth":660,"destHeight":59,"sourceBytes":7430,"destBytes":10618,"author":"mbretous@hubspot.com (Martina Bretous)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/4e634041-e1ce-4a85-8e65-aea12fc10b84.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn72@2020_4/2022/03/14/08-15-05-691_a76d18c90cdcfa92.webp","https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/5174aed9-1caa-4a36-b2d6-84c4d96c25fb.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn2@2020_1/2022/03/14/08-15-10-491_5d7cf3090735f322.webp","https://track.hubspot.com/__ptq.gif?a=53&k=14&r=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.hubspot.com%2Fmarketing%2Fmentor-tips-positive-impact&bu=https%253A%252F%252Fblog.hubspot.com%252Fmarketing&bvt=rss":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn72@2020_3/2022/03/14/08-15-09-934_739f35be8e732354.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1647245705066},{"createdTime":"2022-03-14 16:15:05","updatedTime":"2022-03-14 16:15:05","title":"23 Simple Email Marketing Tips to Improve Your Open and Clickthrough Rates [+HubSpot Blog Data]","link":"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/make-emails-more-clickable-list","description":"<p>Practicing good inbound marketing means sending emails to people who actually <em>want</em> to hear from you.</p> \n<p>But oftentimes, your emails still end up getting lost in your customers' inbox clutter -- or worse, their spam folder. And then, when someone actually opens your email, they don't actually click through.</p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=20aa1557-f54e-4dac-ad9d-52d0af5c68e3&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; \" alt=\"Click here to download our free lookbook that's packed with our favorite email  newsletters.\" src=\"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/20aa1557-f54e-4dac-ad9d-52d0af5c68e3.png\" /></a></p> \n<p>You might think to yourself, \"Ugh, I just can't win.\"</p> \n<p>Don't worry, I've got your back. Here are 23 tips that are perfect for small and growing businesses, but anyone can embrace <em>right now</em> to improve their emails' open rates, clickthrough rates, and lead generation potential.</p> \n<div class=\"hsg-featured-snippet\"> \n <h2>Email Marketing Tips for Small Businesses</h2> \n <ol> \n  <li>Do not buy email addresses.</li> \n  <li>Abide by CAN-SPAM rules.</li> \n  <li>Ensure your opt-in process complies with GDPR.</li> \n  <li>Email new contacts within 24 hours.</li> \n  <li>Send your emails from a real person, not your company.</li> \n  <li>Pre-set the preview text.</li> \n  <li>Write clear and clickable subject lines.</li> \n  <li>Keep your emails concise.</li> \n  <li>Include one call-to-action button per email.</li> \n  <li>Add alt text to your CTA image.</li> \n  <li>Hyperlink your emails' images.</li> \n  <li>Include noticeable text links.</li> \n  <li>Place at least one clickable item above the fold.</li> \n  <li>Add alt text to all of your images.</li> \n  <li>Avoid background images.</li> \n  <li>Add social sharing buttons.</li> \n  <li>Simplify sharing with ready-made tweets.</li> \n  <li>Add an email forwarding option.</li> \n  <li>Clean up the plain text version of your emails.</li> \n  <li>Optimize your emails for mobile users.</li> \n  <li>Preview and test your emails before sending them.</li> \n  <li>Don't be afraid to 'clean up' your contact list.</li> \n  <li>Monitor each email's performance.</li> \n </ol> \n</div> \n<h3>1. Do not buy email addresses.</h3> \n<p>I know what you're thinking: In the early stages of an <a href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/products/marketing/email\">email marketing</a> newsletter, you want to do whatever it takes to kickstart the campaign and get eyeballs on your business. I get it. Whatever options you see online, however, you should resist the urge to <em>purchase</em> an email list.</p> \n<p>There are lots of ways to buy an email list, but none of them will actually benefit your campaign. Why? Since the owners of these email addresses didn't explicitly agree to receive content from you, there's no telling how interested they are -- or if they're even a fit for what you have to offer. A bought email list is also in violation of GDPR (we'll talk more about this in just a minute).</p> \n<p>Purchasing email lists is always a bad idea. Get more reasons why in <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/32892/why-purchasing-email-lists-is-always-a-bad-idea.aspx\">this blog post</a>.</p> \n<h3>2. Abide by CAN-SPAM rules.</h3> \n<p>CAN-SPAM (<strong>C</strong>ontrolling the <strong>A</strong>ssault of <strong>N</strong>on-<strong>S</strong>olicited <strong>P</strong>ornography <strong>A</strong>nd <strong>M</strong>arketing) is an act <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/what-is-can-spam-ht\">that was passed in 2003</a>. Essentially, it's a law that establishes the rules for commercial email and commercial messages, gives recipients the right to have a business stop emailing them, and outlines the penalties incurred for those who violate the law.</p> \n<p>In order to be CAN-SPAM compliant, it's important that your email messages follow these rules, which are <a href=\"https://www.ftc.gov/tips-advice/business-center/guidance/can-spam-act-compliance-guide-business\">available on the FTC's website</a>.</p> \n<p>A few highlights:</p> \n<ul> \n <li>Include your valid physical postal address in every email you send out.</li> \n <li>Give recipients a clear and obvious way to opt out (i.e., unsubscribe) of every email you send. (<strong>HubSpot customers: </strong>Don't worry -- you can't save an email template unless it includes this element.)</li> \n <li>Use clear \"From,\" \"To,\" and \"Reply to\" language that accurately reflects who you are.</li> \n <li>Avoid \"no-reply\" or similar sender names, which prevent recipients from opting out of an email newsletter if they'd like to.</li> \n <li>Avoid selling or transferring any email addresses to another list.</li> \n</ul> \n<p><strong>Note:</strong><em> Because I am not a lawyer, please do not construe the contents of this article as official legal advice. <a href=\"https://www.ftc.gov/tips-advice/business-center/guidance/can-spam-act-compliance-guide-business\">Check out the FTC's website</a> for extensive advice on this subject, and <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/30594/A-Marketer-s-Guide-to-Getting-Past-Email-Spam-Filters.aspx#sm.0000o5c3iom8gdkipdw2l236rj19q\">read this blog post</a> for more tips on improving email deliverability.</em></p> \n<div class=\"video-container-responsive\"> \n <iframe style=\"margin: 0px auto; display: block;\" src=\"http://www.youtube.com/embed/cm6Dnaqiyso\" width=\"560\" height=\"315\" frameborder=\"0\" allowfullscreen=\"\"></iframe> \n</div> \n<h3>3. Ensure your opt-in process complies with GDPR.</h3> \n<p>You've probably heard of the <a href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/data-privacy/gdpr\">General Data Protection Regulation (GDPR)</a>, a new law enacted across Europe in May 2018 to better protect internet users' personal data.</p> \n<p>We don't expect you to have this long piece of legislation memorized. However, if some of your email recipients live in Europe, there is one key guideline by which you should develop your email marketing campaigns:</p> \n<p>When your website users land on a page that solicits their personal information, tradition might tell you to include a pre-checked box that opts the user into an email campaign so they can receive updates and special offers related to your business. Today, having this box pre-checked is in violation of GDPR. <strong>So, to comply with GDPR, make sure your European users and customers are given the clear option to opt into your email newsletter themselves -- don't make the decision for them</strong>.</p> \n<p>This rule might sound like bad news for your email marketing campaign, but it can actually improve your open and clickthrough rates. Limiting your subscriber list to just those who specifically asked to join you will ensure only the most interested people are receiving your messages. This maximizes the chances that you'll convert readers to qualified leads as a result of an email send.</p> \n<h3>4. Email new contacts within 24 hours.</h3> \n<p>It's important to take advantage of the window of opportunity when your company or brand is at the top of your prospects' minds. You can really get a pulse of what future engagement will look like by what people do when you email then within 24 hours of their subscribing to your newsletter, signing up for an offer, and so on. Plus, it's a great opportunity for branding and setting expectations.</p> \n<p>If you don't have any automated email workflows set up, you're likely missing out on some major opportunities to nurture and engage your existing contacts.</p> \n<p>(<strong>HubSpot customers: </strong><a title=\"HubSpot's Workflows tool\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/products/marketing-automation\">Use HubSpot's Workflows App</a> to create personalized, automated email workflows that can get triggered in a number of different ways: when a contact gets added to a list, submits a form on your website, clicks a link in an email, views a page on your blog, clicks on one of your AdWords ads, or becomes a marketing qualified lead.)</p> \n<h3>5. Send your emails from a real person, not your company.</h3> \n<p>When you send email from a real person, your email open rate increases. Plain and simple. This is because -- based on past tests we've conducted -- recipients are typically more likely to trust a personalized sender name and email address than a generic one. People are so inundated with spam nowadays, they often hesitate to open email from unfamiliar senders -- and they're more likely to trust a personalized sender name and email address than a generic one.</p> \n<p>At HubSpot, <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/31634/A-B-Testing-in-Action-3-Real-Life-Marketing-Experiments.aspx\" title=\"we've found\">we found that </a>that emails sent from \"Maggie Georgieva, HubSpot\" perform better in terms of open <em>and </em>clickthrough rate than emails sent from just \"HubSpot.\" So, it may be best to do this ...</p> \n<ul> \n <li>Sender name: Paul Smith</li> \n <li>Sender email address: <a href=\"mailto:psmith@company.com\">psmith@company.com</a></li> \n</ul> \n<p>... instead of this:</p> \n<ul> \n <li>Sender name: Marketing Team</li> \n <li>Sender email address: <a href=\"mailto:marketing@company.com\">marketing@company.com</a></li> \n</ul> \n<p>(<strong>HubSpot customers:</strong> <a href=\"https://knowledge.hubspot.com/articles/kcs_article/email/how-do-i-personalize-the-from-name-and-address-in-an-email?_ga=1.205947027.1866822358.1456501228\">Click here</a> to learn how to personalize the \"From\" name and email address.)</p> \n<p><strong>Note:</strong> Our tests showed personalization works, but we've also found that a combination of a person's name and a company name together in the sender name works well, too. You've just got to <a href=\"https://offers.hubspot.com/an-introduction-to-ab-testing\">A/B test what works best</a> for your particular company, brand, and industry as well as what's ideal based on to whom you're sending emails.</p> \n<h3>6. Pre-set the preview text.</h3> \n<p>Email clients like the iPhone Mail app, Gmail, and Outlook will display the first few lines of text from the body of your email alongside the subject line. In other words, it's a text preview of the content inside the email. The exact amount of text shown depends on the email client and user settings.</p> \n<p>Use it to provide a short, to-the-point synopsis of what you're offering -- and keep it to 50 characters or less.</p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><img class=\"alignCenter shadow\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/email-preview-text-in-inbox.png?width=690&amp;height=54&amp;name=email-preview-text-in-inbox.png\" alt=\"email-preview-text-in-inbox.png\" width=\"690\" height=\"54\" /></p> \n<p>When you don't set the preview text, the client will automatically pull from the body of your email, which not only looks messy, but is also a wasted opportunity to engage your audience. (<strong>HubSpot customers:</strong> <a href=\"https://knowledge.hubspot.com/articles/KCS_Article/Email/What-is-the-Secondary-Content-Preview-Text-section-of-my-email\">Click here</a> to learn how to set the preview text of your emails.)</p> \n<h3>7. Write clear and clickable subject lines.</h3> \n<p>Speaking of the subject line ... your marketing emails have a lot to compete with in recipients' inboxes. The best way to stand out is to write compelling, \"can't-help-but-click-on-this\" subject lines.</p> \n<p>To entice readers to click, be sure your subject lines:</p> \n<ul> \n <li>Are super clear and understandable.</li> \n <li>Are fewer than 50 characters so they don't get cut off, particularly by mobile devices.</li> \n <li>Use language and messaging that <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/33491/Everything-Marketers-Need-to-Research-Create-Detailed-Buyer-Personas-Template.aspx\">your target buyer persona</a> is familiar with and excited about.</li> \n <li>Include verbs and action-oriented language to create a sense of urgency and excitement.</li> \n <li>Include an exclusive value proposition (like 20% off an item or a free ebook) so people know what they're getting.</li> \n <li><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/30594/A-Marketer-s-Guide-to-Getting-Past-Email-Spam-Filters.aspx#sm.0000o5c3iom8gdkipdw2l236rj19q\">Avoid spam triggers</a> like “Cash,” “Quote,” and “Save.\"</li> \n <li>Are timely, if applicable. (One of <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/best-email-subject-lines-list\">my favorite subject lines</a> came from Warby Parker and read: \"Uh-oh, your prescription is expiring\".)</li> \n <li>Include their first names sometimes (it could <a href=\"https://offers.hubspot.com/the-science-of-email-marketing\">increase clickthrough rates</a>), or even add something about their specific location. (You'll want to do this sparingly, like for your most important offers, rather than over-doing it and being repetitive or intrusive.)</li> \n</ul> \n<p><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/improve-your-email-subject-line\">Read this blog post</a> for more tips on writing clickable, delightful subject lines.</p> \n<h3>8. Keep your emails concise.</h3> \n<p>Everyone's busy and their inbox is already full. Why add to the problem with a longwinded email? People generally like short, concise emails better than long ones because concise emails have an obvious focus. Plus, when your users are scanning through all their emails in a short amount of time, they're more likely to find the overall message before deciding to take any action.</p> \n<p>Another reason to keep your emails short? Too much copy is actually a red flag for spam filters, too.</p> \n<p>To keep your emails short and compelling, write your email like you were talking to someone in real life. If your email <em>has </em>to be on the long side, break it up into multiple paragraphs to provide visual breaks. This'll make skimming it much easier on your reader. (<a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/32606/The-9-Must-Have-Components-of-Compelling-Email-Copy.aspx#sm.0000o5c3iom8gdkipdw2l236rj19q\">Read this blog post on how to write compelling emails</a> for more tips.)</p> \n<p>Here's a great example of a concise email:</p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><img class=\"alignCenter shadow\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/free-lattes-concise-email-language.png?width=647&amp;height=886&amp;name=free-lattes-concise-email-language.png\" alt=\"free-lattes-concise-email-language.png\" width=\"647\" height=\"886\" /></p> \n<h3>9. Include one call-to-action button per email.</h3> \n<p>Remember when I said a lot of your email recipients will scan your email without reading all the copy? That's why you want to have a clear call-to-action (CTA) button that's easy to spot for even the quickest of email scanners. Without a CTA button, you won't be calling on your recipients to take any action that actually benefits them -- and the growth of your business.</p> \n<p>You'll want to place your CTA in a location where it's easily visible and where it makes sense for someone to click on it. For example, you might put a CTA to download a free ebook in an email that describes new strategies for using your product.</p> \n<p>Once you've determined where you want to put your CTA, it's time to create the button itself. <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/call-to-action-templates-free-download-ht\">Click here to download 50 free CTA button templates</a> to get you started. (<strong>HubSpot customers:</strong> Learn how to add CTA buttons to emails in HubSpot <a href=\"https://knowledge.hubspot.com/cta-user-guide-v2/how-to-add-a-call-to-action-cta-to-an-email\">here</a>.)</p> \n<h3>10. Add alt text to your CTA image.</h3> \n<p>Many email clients block images -- including your CTA buttons -- by default. That means a good chunk of your audience may not see your <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/call-to-action-optimization-ht\">beautiful, optimized CTA</a>. Instead, they see this:</p> \n<p><img style=\"display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hub/53/file-388144872-png/Screen_Shot_2013-11-21_at_10.02.52_AM.png\" alt=\"\" /></p> \n<p>When you set an image's alt text, though, you let recipients who can't view images in their email know exactly where to click to complete the action:</p> \n<p><img style=\"display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;\" title=\"This is what an image with alt-text looks like.\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hub/53/file-385628288-png/Screen_Shot_2013-11-21_at_9.58.55_AM.png\" alt=\"CTA image with alt-text in an email.\" /></p> \n<p>You can either edit the alt text in your email tool's rich text editor (just right-click the image and edit away), or you can manually enter it in the HTML editor of your email tool like this:</p> \n<p><span style=\"font-size: 16px; font-family: 'courier new', courier;\"><em>&lt;a href=\"<strong>HTTP://YOURLINKHERE.COM</strong>\"&gt;&lt;img class=\"alignCenter shadow\" src=\"<strong>YOUR CTA BUTTON IMAGE SOURCE HERE.JPG</strong>\" alt-text=\"<strong>YOUR ALT-TEXT GOES HERE</strong>\"/&gt;&lt;/a&gt;</em></span></p> \n<h3>11. Hyperlink your emails' images.</h3> \n<p>Your ultimate goal in email marketing is to get people to click through to a web page. One way to increase the clickthrough rate without littering the copy with links is to hyperlink the images in your email to the webpage that corresponds with the content of the image.</p> \n<p>If you're inviting readers to download an ebook, for example, and you have a picture of the ebook included in the email, don't just hyperlink the text next to the image telling people to \"download it here.\" Hyperlink the ebook's picture, too. People are drawn to images much more commonly than text, and you want to give your email subscribers as many options to get your ebook as you can.</p> \n<p>You can simply click on the image and then use your email tool's \"Insert/Edit Link\" option, or you can link an image in the HTML editor using the following code:</p> \n<p><span style=\"font-family: 'courier new', courier; font-size: 16px;\"><em>&lt;a href=\"<strong>HTTP://YOURLINKHERE.COM</strong>\"&gt;&lt;img class=\"alignCenter shadow\" src=\"<strong>YOUR IMAGE SOURCE HERE.JPG</strong>\"/&gt;&lt;/a&gt;</em></span></p> \n<h3>12. Include noticeable text links.</h3> \n<p>In general, it's a good idea to link to your featured offer in multiple places in addition to the clear and focused call-to-action button. In addition to your main CTAs and images, consider including a noticeable text link (or two) when applicable, as having more links increases the opportunity for engagement.</p> \n<h3>13. Place at least one clickable item above the fold.</h3> \n<p>One way to make your emails more clickable? Place one or more of your clickable elements -- whether it's a CTA button, a text link, or a clickable image -- near the beginning of your email.</p> \n<p>This is especially useful for mobile users. Mobile tends to require a lot of scrolling, and sometimes squinting, pinching, and zooming. Giving a recipient something actionable that is seen upon opening can lead to more clicks in this environment.</p> \n<h3>14. Add alt text to all of your images.</h3> \n<p>Again, a lot of email clients out there block images by default. (<a href=\"https://www.campaignmonitor.com/dev-resources/will-it-work/image-blocking/\">Here's the full list</a> from Campaign Monitor.) In those cases, images won't load unless the recipient clicks a button to show them or change their default settings.</p> \n<p><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/how-to-add-alt-text-to-email-images-ht\">Adding alt text to your email images</a> helps recipients understand your message -- even if they can't see the images right away. (<strong>HubSpot customers:</strong> <a href=\"https://knowledge.hubspot.com/articles/kcs_article/cos-pages-editor/how-do-i-add-alt-text-to-my-image\">Click here</a> to learn how to add alt text to your email images in HubSpot.)</p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><img class=\"alignCenter shadow\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/add-alt-text.png?width=690&amp;height=301&amp;name=add-alt-text.png\" alt=\"add-alt-text.png\" width=\"690\" height=\"301\" /></p> \n<p>You might consider making the language in your alt text actionable, such as \"Click here to download the ultimate content creation kit.\" Actionable alt text will essentially turn every linked image into another CTA. So, even if someone doesn't see the snazzy GIF of my latest offer (or if they hover their mouse over an image that <em>does </em>show up), the alt text will beckon them to click.</p> \n<h3>15. Avoid background images.</h3> \n<p>This is especially important if your target buyers tend to use Outlook as an email client.</p> \n<p>Microsoft Outlook doesn't recognize background images, period. Given that <a href=\"https://emailclientmarketshare.com/\">Outlook is the fifth most-used email client</a> with 7% of the market share -- and that's in total; your industry might have a lot more -- it's best to avoid using background images altogether.</p> \n<p>Instead, use a background color and use images in other ways in your email, like Harry's did in their email below:</p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><img class=\"alignCenter shadow\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/harrys-email-example.png?width=580&amp;height=1630&amp;name=harrys-email-example.png\" alt=\"harrys-email-example.png\" width=\"580\" height=\"1630\" /></p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><span style=\"font-size: 12px;\"><em>Image Credit: <a href=\"http://beautiful-email-newsletters.com/emails/harrys-our-most-popular-gift-is/\">Beautiful Email Newsletters</a></em></span></p> \n<h3>16. Add social sharing buttons.</h3> \n<p>Increasing the number of people who see your link will increase the number of people who click on it. So, be sure to extend the life of your email by <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/29544/The-Ultimate-Cheat-Sheet-for-Creating-Social-Media-Buttons.aspx\">adding social sharing buttons</a>.</p> \n<p><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/29544/The-Ultimate-Cheat-Sheet-for-Creating-Social-Media-Buttons.aspx\"><img class=\"alignCenter shadow\" style=\"display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;\" title=\"Social Sharing Buttons\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hub/53/file-388230117-png/linkedin-share-button-above.png?width=300&amp;name=linkedin-share-button-above.png\" alt=\"Social Sharing Buttons\" width=\"300\" /></a></p> \n<p>Many email tools will come with templates that have built-in social sharing buttons that make it easy -- just fill in the destination URL and you're good to go. If you don't have built-in capabilities, <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/29544/The-Ultimate-Cheat-Sheet-for-Creating-Social-Media-Buttons.aspx\">here is a cheat sheet for easily creating your own social sharing buttons</a>.</p> \n<p><strong>Important Note:</strong> If you want to increase clicks, you want to add <em>sharing</em> buttons, not <em>follow</em> buttons. The former will allow your email recipients to pass along the offer URL in your email to their followers. The latter will prompt them to Like, follow, or add your company social media channels.</p> \n<h3>17. Simplify sharing with ready-made tweets.</h3> \n<p>People are far more likely to take an action if you make it really, really easy for them. For recipients out there who are too lazy to tweet the wonderful content you sent them via email, you can make it easy for them by creating what we call a \"lazy tweet.\"</p> \n<p>One simple way to do this? Using ClickToTweet, a free custom tweet link generator. First, <a href=\"https://clicktotweet.com/basic\">go to ClickToTweet's basic tweet generator</a>. Then, type in your tweet, desired (<a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/what-are-utm-tracking-codes-ht\">trackable</a>) destination URL, and hashtags:</p> \n<p><img class=\"alignCenter shadow\" style=\"display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; width: 669px;\" title=\"click-to-tweet-example.png\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/click-to-tweet-example.png?width=669&amp;name=click-to-tweet-example.png\" alt=\"click-to-tweet-example.png\" width=\"669\"><br>Click \"Generate New Link,\" and then grab that link. Then you can link it to your Twitter sharing button. Or, if you're <a href=\"https://knowledge.hubspot.com/contacts-user-guide-v2/how-lists-help-you-segment-your-contacts\">segmenting your list by attributes</a> such as \"has Twitter\" or \"topic of recent conversion: social media\" (you'll need marketing intelligence software <a href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/products/email\">like HubSpot</a> for this), you can even include it in your main email copy, like this:</br></img></p> \n<h3><img class=\"alignCenter shadow\" style=\"display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;\" title=\"Premade tweet copy example\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hub/53/file-388186477-png/Screen_Shot_2013-11-21_at_10.28.40_AM.png?width=600&amp;name=Screen_Shot_2013-11-21_at_10.28.40_AM.png\" alt=\"Premade tweet copy example\" width=\"600\" /></h3> \n<h3>18. Add an email forwarding option.</h3> \n<p>Another way to extend the clicks on your email beyond its shelf life is to prompt your audience to forward the offer. <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/why-people-forward-emails-data\">The folks at Litmus found that</a> <strong>the most forwarded emails were 13X more likely than the typical email to include “Share With Your Network” calls-to-action. </strong>By including forward-to-a-friend (or social sharing links, as we discussed above), you put it in recipients' minds to share.</p> \n<p>You can add a little post-script to the end of your email copy, such as \"Not responsible for your company's social media? Feel free to forward this ebook to a friend or colleague using social media marketing.\" Link the call-to-action to a pre-made email, complete with subject and body text. That way, all someone has to do is enter their associates' email addresses and hit \"Send.\"</p> \n<p>You can highlight text or an image and add the URL via your email tool's rich text editor and then enter a mailto:? link. Here's what this looks like:</p> \n<span style=\"font-size: 16px;\"><em><span style=\"font-family: 'trebuchet ms', geneva;\">mailto:?subject=Your%20subject%20here%20&amp;body=Your%20email%20body%20text%20here.</span></em></span> \n<p>You can also create this in your HTML editor. Here's how to attach a mailto:? link to text:</p> \n<span style=\"font-size: 16px;\"><em><span style=\"font-family: 'trebuchet ms', geneva;\">&lt;a href=\"mailto:?subject=<strong>Your%20subject%20here%20&amp;body=Your%20email%20body%20text%20here</strong>.\"&gt;</span></em></span> \n<span style=\"font-size: 16px;\"><em><span style=\"font-family: 'trebuchet ms', geneva;\">forward this ebook&lt;/a&gt;.</span></em></span> \n<p>And here's how to attach your mailto:? link to an image, such as a sleek call-to-action button that says \"Email This Offer\":</p> \n<span style=\"font-size: 16px;\"><em><span style=\"font-family: 'trebuchet ms', geneva;\">&lt;a href=\"mailto:?subject=<strong>Your%20subject%20here%20&amp;body=Your%20email%20body%20text%20here.</strong>\"&gt;&lt;img class=\"alignCenter shadow\" src=\"<strong>YOUR IMAGE SOURCE HERE.JPG</strong>\" alt-text=\"<strong>YOUR ALT-TEXT GOES HERE</strong>\"/&gt;&lt;/a&gt;</span></em></span> \n<p>Just make sure you use the \"%20\" tag to separate words! Otherwise, your message willreadlikethis (not too appealing, right?).</p> \n<h3>19. Clean up the plain-text version of your emails.</h3> \n<p>Not every recipient is going to see the beautiful, HTML, rich-text version of your email. Some clients don't support HTML-rich emails, while other times, a person may simply choose to only view messages in plain text.</p> \n<p>When you don't optimize the plain-text version of your email, this is what happens when someone views it:</p> \n<p><img class=\"alignCenter shadow\" style=\"display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;\" title=\"Plain-text email done wrong.\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hub/53/file-388686490-png/Screen_Shot_2013-11-20_at_2.12.38_PM.png?width=403&amp;name=Screen_Shot_2013-11-20_at_2.12.38_PM.png\" alt=\"Plain-text email done wrong.\" width=\"403\" /></p> \n<p>Scary, isn't it? I don't think many people are going to bother to read through this garbled mess.</p> \n<p>So, cut out the extra text, replace long tracking URLs with shortened ones, and keep the body simple. Taking the five extra minutes to <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/32643/Why-Marketers-Must-Optimize-Emails-for-HTML-AND-Plain-Text-Infographic.aspx\">optimize your email's plain-text version</a> could help you reach more of your target segment and keep you out of the spam folder.</p> \n<p><strong>Note:</strong> When you're cleaning up your plain-text emails, don't change the actual copy much at all or you'll risk it getting marked as spam.</p> \n<h3>20. Optimize your emails for mobile users.</h3> \n<p>In <a href=\"https://litmus.com/blog/mobile-rises-to-56-market-share-longest-sustained-growth-in-2016\">Litmus' analysis of over a billion email opens</a>, they reported that <strong>56% of opened emails were opened on mobile devices in April 2016. </strong>This figure represents an 8% increase in mobile opens in the past year.</p> \n<p>\"This represents a peak for mobile market share,\" they wrote, \"and the longest sustained growth we’ve seen after the holiday season.\"</p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\">&nbsp;</p> \n<img class=\"alignCenter shadow\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/mobile-email-opens-litmus.png?width=690&amp;height=420&amp;name=mobile-email-opens-litmus.png\" alt=\"mobile-email-opens-litmus.png\" width=\"690\" height=\"420\"> <p style=\"text-align: center;\"><span style=\"font-size: 12px;\"><em>Image Credit: <a href=\"https://litmus.com/blog/mobile-rises-to-56-market-share-longest-sustained-growth-in-2016\">Litmus</a></em></span></p> <p>As more and more people use their mobile devices to read email and surf the web, it's more important than ever that marketers design their emails with mobile users in mind. Otherwise, their user base will be significantly affected.</p> <p>How? Here's a visual example of what happens when images aren't optimized for mobile (first) versus when images are optimized for mobile (second):</p> <p style=\"text-align: center;\"><img class=\"alignCenter shadow\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/email-not-optimized-for-mobile.png?width=300&amp;name=email-not-optimized-for-mobile.png\" alt=\"email-not-optimized-for-mobile.png\" width=\"300\" style=\"width: 300px;\"> <img class=\"alignCenter shadow\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/email-optimized-for-mobile.png?width=300&amp;name=email-optimized-for-mobile.png\" alt=\"email-optimized-for-mobile.png\" width=\"300\" title=\"email-optimized-for-mobile.png\" style=\"width: 300px; height: 628px;\" /></img></p> <p>Isn't the second image a much better user experience?</p> <p>Here are a few ways to <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/optimize-email-mobile-list\">optimize your emails for mobile devices</a>:</p> \n <ul> \n  <li><strong>Reduce your images' file sizes</strong> to make up for mobile devices' generally slower download speeds. (HubSpot customers don't need to worry about it -- images uploaded to HubSpot's software are automatically compressed. Otherwise, tools like <a href=\"https://tinypng.com/\">TinyPNG</a> will help you reduce file size.)</li> \n  <li><strong>Ensure the CTA buttons and links are larger than 45-57 pixels </strong>for the best user experience. Why? <a href=\"http://touchlab.mit.edu/publications/2003_009.pdf\">According to an MIT study</a>, the average size of an adult index finger is 1.6-2 cm, which translates to 45-57 pixels on a mobile device.</li> \n  <li><strong>Invest in responsive email templates.</strong> Creating your own responsive template may be beyond your particular skill set or bandwidth. Sometimes, the most economical solution is to just license or buy email templates from the people who do it best.</li> \n </ul> <p><strong>HubSpot customers:</strong> HubSpot's default email templates are all optimized for mobile using responsive design. To access these templates, create a new email and look for the responsive option in the \"folders\" drop-down in the top left.</p> <p style=\"text-align: center;\"><img class=\"alignCenter shadow\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/responsive-email-1.png?width=287&amp;height=159&amp;name=responsive-email-1.png\" alt=\"responsive-email-1.png\" width=\"287\" height=\"159\" /></p> <h3>21. Preview and test your emails before sending them.</h3> <p>When you're finally ready to hit \"Send\" on your email, make a habit of double-checking one last time whether your emails look as good as you think they do. If your <a href=\"https://ecommerce-platforms.com/articles/email-marketing-services\">email marketing tool</a> lets you, go ahead and preview what your email looks like in different email clients and devices that are popular with your audience.</p> <p>(<strong>HubSpot customers:</strong> You can preview what your emails look like in 30+ email clients right in the HubSpot Email App, as well as preview what your emails will look like on any device -- including desktop, tablet, or mobile devices. <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/customers/how-to-preview-your-emails-in-30-different-inboxes\">Click here to learn how</a>.)</p> <p>You should also send out a test version of your email before you send out the real deal to ensure it's working properly for everyone on your email list. Start incorporating these as final steps in your email review process. (<strong>HubSpot customers:</strong> <a href=\"https://help.hubspot.com/articles/KCS_Article/Email/How-do-I-send-a-test-email\">Learn how to test your emails here</a>.)</p> <h3>22. Don't be afraid to 'clean up' your contact list.</h3> <p>It's tempting to keep every subscriber you win on an email campaign until they personally choose to opt out. But just because they haven't opted out of an email newsletter doesn't mean they're still interested, and subscribers who have become inactive can kill your emails' open and clickthrough rates.</p> <p>To make sure you're only sending emails to the people who want to read them, <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/26404/4-tips-to-keep-your-email-list-squeaky-clean.aspx\">clean up your email list</a> so that it excludes recipients who haven't opened a certain amount of emails in the campaign's recent history. This makes sure your emails' open and clickthrough rates reflect only your most interested readers, allowing you to collect more effective data on what is and isn't working in each email you send.</p> <p>On top of that, a good&nbsp;<a href=\"https://www.zerobounce.net/\">email list cleaning service</a> removes other email addresses that pose a risk to your inbox placement. “Invalid, abuse, and temporary emails will affect your sender reputation, so it’s best to weed them out,” says Liviu Tanase, CEO of ZeroBounce. “Your desire to grow your list is only natural, but you can’t afford to expand it at all costs. Emailing only valid and active addresses allows you to connect with people who care about your brand, and that’s what every email marketer wants,” Tanase adds.</p> <p>(<strong>HubSpot customers:</strong> Lists that add and remove members based on their email behavior are called smart or \"active\" lists. Learn how to create them in <a href=\"https://knowledge.hubspot.com/lists-user-guide/how-to-create-a-list-of-your-contacts\">HubSpot Academy</a>.)</p> <h3>23. Monitor each email's performance.</h3> <p>What's working in your email campaign this month might not work quite as well next month, and it's imperative that you check in on your emails' open and clickthrough rates for opportunities to improve your copy (to do this, of course, you'll need a tool to <a href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/products/marketing/email\">track your email analytics</a>).</p> <p>If after a month of email sends, for instance, you find 10 messages are getting double the engagement as the other 20, analyze them. What did you do differently in the higher performers? Was it the imagery? The subject line? Maybe you have more than one audience segment and one of them just isn't as interested in your current email content.</p> <p>Use your email performance data to run A/B tests that are designed to show you what your email recipients really want out of your newsletters, and steer into the trends that you see to make your email campaigns more desirable.</p> <p>Email marketing can be tough at times -- I'm right there with you. But by sending compelling offers to the right target segments and paying attention to the little details that go into an email, you can increase the opens clicks in your emails and generate more leads. (And <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/metrics-email-marketers-should-be-tracking#sm.0000o5c3iom8gdkipdw2l236rj19q\">learn more about which email marketing metrics to track -- and how -- here</a>.)</p> <p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=05a9885a-6173-4c64-8598-99503d911640&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" 7-png/Screen_Shot_2013-11-21_at_10.28.40_AM.png?width=600&name=Screen_Shot_2013-11-21_at_10.28.40_AM.png":null,"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hub/53/file-388686490-png/Screen_Shot_2013-11-20_at_2.12.38_PM.png?width=403&name=Screen_Shot_2013-11-20_at_2.12.38_PM.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn43@2020_2/2022/03/14/08-15-14-738_8c47850277fa6a01.webp","https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/mobile-email-opens-litmus.png?width=690&height=420&name=mobile-email-opens-litmus.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn45@2020_1/2022/03/14/08-15-15-350_28302fbbe185f0bd.webp","https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/email-not-optimized-for-mobile.png?width=300&name=email-not-optimized-for-mobile.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx8/cdn31@2020_2/2022/03/14/08-15-12-374_c91eae38987c421b.webp","https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/email-optimized-for-mobile.png?width=300&name=email-optimized-for-mobile.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn7@2020_4/2022/03/14/08-15-12-666_8786a3aa8d75df9f.webp","https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/responsive-email-1.png?width=287&height=159&name=responsive-email-1.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn13@2020_5/2022/03/14/08-15-13-341_2bbf6b92b8cb2c74.webp","https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/05a9885a-6173-4c64-8598-99503d911640.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn90@2020_1/2022/03/14/08-15-10-784_6b1134a74c88a32e.webp","https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/ea1cee44-acd0-476e-a42f-ca2180e4b351.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn59@2020_3/2022/03/14/08-15-14-418_d1a1c517b04c5587.webp","https://track.hubspot.com/__ptq.gif?a=53&k=14&r=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.hubspot.com%2Fmarketing%2Fmake-emails-more-clickable-list&bu=https%253A%252F%252Fblog.hubspot.com%252Fmarketing&bvt=rss":null},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1647245705119},{"createdTime":"2022-03-14 16:15:05","updatedTime":"2022-03-14 16:15:05","title":"The Ultimate Guide to Writing a Cover Letter","link":"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/cover-letter","description":"<p>Nowadays, companies have a computerized system that puts resumes through an online scanner which will automatically reject some applicants and push other applicants through depending on their qualifications.</p> \n<p>So, What does this mean for you as a job seeker? Well, the cover letter attached to your application is more important than ever.</p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=3f347702-d7e9-4e59-9fe4-be4cd7bad191&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; \" alt=\"→ Click here to access 5 free cover letter templates [Free Download]\" src=\"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/3f347702-d7e9-4e59-9fe4-be4cd7bad191.png\"></a></p> \n<p>We've crafted this ultimate guide to cover letters. You'll find out how to write one that gets read, what to include, and browse tons of templates to gain inspiration.</p> \n<p>You can dive straight in, or jump to the section you'd like to read.</p> \n<p></p> \n<p></p> \n<h2>How long should a cover letter be?</h2> \n<p>OK, so you're all fired up and ready to craft the cover letter of the hiring manager's dream. But how do you manage the fine balance between in-depth and overwhelming?</p> \n<p>A good cover letter is long enough to communicate why the recruiter should pick you but not long enough to bore them.</p> \n<p>One page is usually enough to cover everything you'll need to include, without losing the recruiter's attention. Let's go into those items in more detail:</p> \n<h3>Your Name and Address</h3> \n<p>Kick-off your cover letter by adding your name and address to the document.</p> \n<p>This step is pretty self-explanatory, but it allows the recruiter to easily connect your cover letter to your resume (especially if they're being printed).</p> \n<p>Your name and address also make it easier for the recruiter to get in touch with a job offer. And that's the aim of our letter, right?</p> \n<h3>Their Name and Address</h3> \n<p>Similarly, you should add the name and address of the company or person you're writing to.</p> \n<p>This shows you've done your research and allows the hiring manager to receive your letter if it's sent to a generic company email address.</p> \n<h3>The Date of Writing</h3> \n<p>Make it easier for the hiring manager to file your application by including the date on your cover letter.</p> \n<p>Even if you're not successful this time around, the company might store your letter and refer back to it when they're hiring for another position.</p> \n<h3>Why You're Writing the Letter</h3> \n<p>We know that the aim of a cover letter is to persuade the hiring manager you're the best fit for their job.</p> \n<p>Before you get to the good stuff, be sure to highlight the role you're applying for, as that can get lost.</p> \n<p>Something like this will usually do the trick:</p> \n<p><em>\"I'm writing to discuss the content strategist role at HubSpot.\"</em></p> \n<h3>Why You're a Perfect Fit for the Job</h3> \n<p>The next section of a cover letter structure is the fun part. It's where you'll convince the hiring manager they should hire you.</p> \n<p>In this section, answer these questions:</p> \n<ul> \n <li>Why should this company hire you?</li> \n <li>What skills do you have that will help complete the job better than anyone else?</li> \n <li>What makes you a good employee?</li> \n <li>What qualifications do you have that are relevant to the role?</li> \n</ul> \n<p>Once you've answered these, the recruiter will have a solid understanding of who you are, and (hopefully) be convinced to bring you on for an interview.</p> \n<h3>What You Can Offer the Company</h3> \n<p>Have you ever heard the advice to \"always sell yourself in a job application\"? That concept can be applied to cover letters as well.</p> \n<p>Businesses measure success in terms of results. The company looking for a new employee will want to know what they bring to the table and how you fit into their business goals. New candidates are rarely brought on board solely for the<a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/soft-skills\"> </a><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/soft-skills?_ga=2.185839593.1527963336.1644028103-1253290474.1644028103\">soft skills listed in their resume</a>.</p> \n<p>That's why this part of your cover letter structure is arguably the most important.</p> \n<p>In two paragraphs or less, show the business what you can do — and provide examples of how you've done it before.</p> \n<p>Not only does this give you the opportunity to show off your skills, but the company can picture the success you'll bring to their business by hiring you.</p> \n<h3>Your Availability</h3> \n<p>In the marketing world, we're always told the importance a call-to-action can make.</p> \n<p>Great cover letters end with a brief section on the candidate's earliest start date.</p> \n<h2>How to Format a Cover Letter</h2> \n<h3>How to Address a Cover Letter</h3> \n<p>Earlier, we mentioned the importance of addressing the hiring manager by their name and address. This proves you've done your research and ensures the cover letter lands in the right place.</p> \n<p>Personalized letters will always outperform generic ones, so including the first name of the recruiter can go a long way.</p> \n<p>But in a world where privacy is held close to our chest, you might need to do a bit of digging before finding the hiring manager's name.</p> \n<p>Luckily, you can use the power of the internet to do this.</p> \n<h4><strong>How to Find a Hiring Manager's Name</strong></h4> \n<p>Head over to LinkedIn and find the company's profile page.</p> \n<p>You can do this by entering their name into the search bar or searching for a link to their LinkedIn page on their company website.</p> \n<p>Then, click the number of employees to see all employees who are on LinkedIn:</p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><img alt=\"how to look up employer details to format cover letter\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/The%20Ultimate%20Guide%20to%20Writing%20a%20Cover%20Letter.jpeg?width=600&amp;name=The%20Ultimate%20Guide%20to%20Writing%20a%20Cover%20Letter.jpeg\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block; width: 600px;\" title=\"\" width=\"600\"></p> \n<p>You'll then see a list of all employees along with their titles. Simply work your way through this list to find the most relevant contact.</p> \n<p>Keep in mind that some employees do not have LinkedIn profiles, so you may not find them using this tactic. If you're unable to track down the hiring manager's name, a simple \"Dear Hiring Manager\" will work.</p> \n<h3>How to Open a Cover Letter</h3> \n<p>After you've addressed the cover letter to the most relevant person, you'll want to:</p> \n<ul> \n <li>Introduce yourself.</li> \n <li>List the role you're interested in.</li> \n <li>Explain your interest.</li> \n</ul> \n<p>Here's an example:</p> \n<p>\"<em>Dear Hiring Manager, </em></p> \n<p><em>As an avid reader of the HubSpot Blog for the past five years, I am thrilled to submit my application for the content strategist role. I believe that my five years of experience working for B2B SaaS companies have equipped me with the skills needed to thrive in this role.\"</em></p> \n<p>In the next two paragraphs, highlight your relevant experience and include key details from each role.</p> \n<h3>How to Close a Cover Letter</h3> \n<p>Once you've covered</p> \n<p>Here are some great options:</p> \n<ul> \n <li>Looking forward to hearing from you</li> \n <li>Sincerely</li> \n <li>Best Regards</li> \n</ul> \n<p>Then, sign the cover letter with your full name.</p> \n<h3>Should you include salary requirements?</h3> \n<p>The cover letter should focus on why you are a good fit for the role. Discussing salary requirements doesn’t fit at this stage of your application.</p> \n<p>Instead, it’s best to wait until you speak to a recruiter or someone from HR to discuss your expectations.</p> \n<h2>Are cover letters necessary?</h2> \n<p>Today, in many industries, cover letters are listed as optional. The question is, should you include one if it's optional?</p> \n<p>The answer isn’t exactly clear-cut.</p> \n<p>Some research would suggest that cover letters may not hold the same weight as they once did. However, a cover letter can help you stand out among the competition.</p> \n<p><img alt=\"Are cover letters necessary job seekers believe getting a job will be harder than in previous years\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/The%20Ultimate%20Guide%20to%20Writing%20a%20Cover%20Letter-1.jpeg?width=500&amp;name=The%20Ultimate%20Guide%20to%20Writing%20a%20Cover%20Letter-1.jpeg\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block; width: 500px;\" title=\"\" width=\"500\"></p> \n<p>In a 2021 Job Seeker Nation Report by JobVite, <a href=\"https://www.jobvite.com/lp/2021-job-seeker-nation-report/\">69% of surveyed workers</a> believed getting a job will be much harder or somewhat harder than in previous years. With this in mind, adding a cover letter to your application is a great way to stand out.</p> \n<p>Writing a cover letter will allow you to:</p> \n<ul> \n <li>Communicate with the hiring manager.</li> \n <li>Rely on more than just bullet-pointed lists in your resume.</li> \n <li>Build your personal brand.</li> \n</ul> \n<p>In short: Cover letters aren't absolutely necessary, but they do have stark advantages. If there's an option to upload one when applying for any job, do it — even if it's not required.</p> \n<h2>How to Write a Cover Letter</h2> \n<p>Writing a cover letter can be tricky. Even the best writers can struggle with communicating their skills in the right manner, but these tips will help you create a job-winning document.</p> \n<p>The structure of your cover letter is arguably the most important thing about writing one.</p> \n<p>Not only does a good structure help you to organize your points effectively, but it can help a hiring manager to quickly review the details you're sharing.</p> \n<h5 style=\"color: #666666; font-size: 18px;\"><span style=\"color: #425b76; font-weight: normal; font-style: italic;\">Featured Resource:<a href=\"https://offers.hubspot.com/cover-letter-templates?hubs_post-cta=header\"> </a><a href=\"https://offers.hubspot.com/cover-letter-templates?hubs_post-cta=header\">5 Free Cover Letter Templates</a></span></h5> \n<p><img alt=\"Cover-Letter-Templates\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/The%20Ultimate%20Guide%20to%20Writing%20a%20Cover%20Letter.png?width=250&amp;name=The%20Ultimate%20Guide%20to%20Writing%20a%20Cover%20Letter.png\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block; width: 250px;\" title=\"\" width=\"250\"></p> \n<p><a href=\"https://offers.hubspot.com/cover-letter-templates?hubs_post-cta=imagebottom\">Download these free cover letter templates</a> to write a stand-out cover letter.</p> \n<h2>7 Tips for Writing Great Cover Letters</h2> \n<p>So, you've crafted a cover letter and you're almost ready to hit send.</p> \n<p>Before attaching to your resume and hoping for the best, use these seven tips to make sure your cover letter is as great as can be.</p> \n<h3>1. Keep it succinct.</h3> \n<p>Earlier, we mentioned how the best cover letters strike the perfect balance in their length.</p> \n<p>Our best tip for writing cover letters is to avoid adding fluff that fails to add value. Every line should highlight why you're the best fit for the role.</p> \n<p>In addition, cut the jargon and corporate-speak that hiring managers have heard before.</p> \n<p>Yes, professionalism is important, but be harsh and critical when editing your cover letter. If a sentence doesn't add value, get rid of it.</p> \n<h3>2. Tailor it for the company and position you're applying for.</h3> \n<p>The one-size-fits-all approach doesn't fit well with cover letters.</p> \n<p>You're applying for different roles at various companies, but don't let a change in name and address be the only updates you make.</p> \n<p>Remember that a cover letter should explain why you should be hired for a specific role instead of anyone else. It's highly unlikely that multiple companies will hire for exactly the same position, so take some time to personalize your cover letter for every position you're applying for.</p> \n<h3>3. Don't repeat what's on your resume.</h3> \n<p>Although cover letters are submitted along with resumes, be wary of making them carbon copies of one another.</p> \n<p>Instead, use the documents to compliment each other by:</p> \n<ul> \n <li>Including new skills.</li> \n <li>Elaborating on how your qualifications would help you in the role.</li> \n <li>Sharing how specific experience gives you an advantage over other candidates.</li> \n</ul> \n<p>If you need to include the same thing in both documents, add \"as listed in my resume …\" rather than copy and pasting the same content.</p> \n<h3>4. Include data-backed examples.</h3> \n<p>When referencing experience from your resume, use your cover letter as an opportunity to explain in detail — with examples.</p> \n<p>Examples allow the company to picture the success you could bring if they hired you, rather than the person next in their resume pile. But, data-backed examples give an extra edge.</p> \n<p>Let's use an example. Which of these options is more impressive?</p> \n<ol start=\"1\"> \n <li>I increased leads for the company.</li> \n <li>I increased leads by 35% in one month through a single blog post, which became the company's highest lead driver.</li> \n</ol> \n<p>It's option B, right? That's because it's descriptive and shows results.</p> \n<h3>5. Tell a story.</h3> \n<p>Following on from the previous step, you could elaborate on your data-backed examples by telling a story.</p> \n<p>Storytelling helps with relatability and gives a hint of your personality in a cover letter. It also makes the recruiter remember your cover letter amongst a sea of other one-page documents in their review pile.</p> \n<p>However, this cover letter tip comes with a warning: Don't overdo it and make sure it's relevant.</p> \n<h3>6. Get a second pair of eyes on it.</h3> \n<p>Even the best writers make mistakes, but they can leave a negative first impression.</p> \n<p>That's why our sixth cover letter tip is to get a second pair of eyes on it.</p> \n<p>Email it to a friend or ask a family member to glance over it before you hit \"send.\" Ask them to highlight any spelling mistakes or suggestions to improve how you're communicating with the person reading it.</p> \n<p>You never get a second chance to make a first impression. Seeing as though a cover letter is one of the first documents a recruiter sees, try to make it perfect.</p> \n<h3>7. Be unique.</h3> \n<p>Finally, make your cover letter unique.</p> \n<p>If you're applying for a creative role, experiment with colors, subheadings, and layouts.</p> \n<p>If you're applying for more of a traditional role, be wary. Not everyone is a fan of bright, bold cover letters, but you can scope your limits by getting a feel of their company culture.</p> \n<p>Are they strict and professional, or does the company like to have fun? (You can usually get a feel of this from their website or social media profiles.)</p> \n<p>Testing the level of uniqueness can be a case of trial and error. If you're not getting great reactions from your cover letter, revise and try again.</p> \n<h2>Cover Letter Examples</h2> \n<p>We understand that inspiration can go a long way. That's why we've created a one-stop-shop for<a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/best-cover-letter-examples\"> </a><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/best-cover-letter-examples\">cover letter examples</a>, which are available to view here.</p> \n<p>You're also free to browse our collection of<a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/how-to-write-cover-letter-template\"> </a><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/how-to-write-cover-letter-template\">cover letter samples</a> for extra inspiration on formatting your cover letter and learning from those who've helped to land dream jobs.</p> \n<p>Now you're fully equipped to write a cover letter that will help you get your foot in the door.</p> \n<p><em>Editor's note: This post was originally published in September 2018 and has been updated for comprehensiveness.</em></p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\"
