16:15:05","updatedTime":"2022-03-14 16:15:05","title":"3 Roles Marketing Leaders Plan to Recruit in 2022 [New Research + Expert Insights]","link":"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/top-marketing-roles","description":"<p>The new year can be an exciting time to consider how you might expand your team to reach new goals in 2022.</p> \n<p>But it can also be stressful for that very same reason. With a limited budget, how can you ensure you're making the <em>right</em>&nbsp;hire?</p> \n<p>HubSpot's Blog Research uncovered the top three roles marketers are planning on hiring in 2022. Let's explore why those three roles matter, according to experts.</p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=6baeae42-e710-4ecd-beb9-ceb2fb9f0877&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; margin: 0 auto; display: block; margin-top: 20px; margin-bottom: 20px\" alt=\"Download Now: Free State of Marketing Report\" src=\"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/6baeae42-e710-4ecd-beb9-ceb2fb9f0877.png\" align=\"middle\"></a></p> \n<h2 style=\"font-weight: normal;\">The Top 3 Roles Marketing Leaders Plan to Hire in 2022</h2> \n<h3><strong>1. Creative Director </strong></h3> \n<p>Nowadays, brands are expected to create top-notch content across platforms. To successfully reach new audiences and increase sales, you'll want to have strong social media, content marketing, and video marketing strategies — to name a few.</p> \n<p>As Wistia's Creative Director, Adam Day, puts it, \"In the context of today's media landscape, the opportunity for brands to express themselves through multiple mediums is more attainable than ever — and consumers are demanding more than ever, too.\"</p> \n<p>Day adds, \"It's not just about blog posts anymore. Video consumption, alone, is <a href=\"https://wistia.com/about/state-of-video\">up 121% from 2019</a>, and in a recent survey of Wistia customers, we learned that most companies are increasing their production budgets by more than 10% this year. Businesses need someone who can oversee the creative execution of all this work while maintaining the consistency and quality it takes to have a world-class brand.\"</p> \n<p>That's all well and good. But what, exactly, does a creative director do?</p> \n<p>\"A great creative director develops a clear and engaging visual identity for your brand,\" Mark Tanner, Co-Founder and COO of <a href=\"https://qwilr.com/\">Qwilr</a>, told me. \"Visual consistency communicates professionalism, attention to detail, and builds buyer confidence in a brand's capabilities.\"</p> \n<blockquote>\n Tanner told me, \"The creative director should 'own' how a brand is represented across all visual assets, from your website to ads to product brochures to sales proposals.\"\n</blockquote> \n<p>Tanner continues, \"And if you think the impact of a creative director is limited to aesthetics, think again. According to a <a href=\"https://www.mckinsey.com/business-functions/mckinsey-design/our-insights/the-business-value-of-design\">study by McKinsey</a>, design-driven companies consistently outperform their competitors, demonstrating the ROI potential of a good design experience.\"</p> \n<p>A creative director can ultimately help your business hit its sales goals by ensuring your marketing materials are highly optimized, effective, and on-brand.&nbsp;</p> \n<p>As Tanner told me, \"<a href=\"https://pages.qwilr.com/SaaS-Buyer-Experience-Study-2021-Full-Report-tPfTLda8SiOI\">One out of three buyers</a>&nbsp;are influenced by the quality of your sales materials, and that influence can either be positive, or cause your buyer to go with your competition, instead. It's no wonder the <a href=\"https://www.bls.gov/ooh/arts-and-design/art-directors.htm\">U.S. Bureau of Labor Statistics projects creative director demand to grow by 11%</a>, faster than the average for all occupations.\"</p> \n<p>Among other things, you can expect a creative director to guide your overarching content strategy; build and manage a successful production process; lead, inspire, and nurture your creative team to drive brand direction forward; and own specific KPIs related to content marketing.</p> \n<p>Jenny Coppola, Head of Brand &amp; Communications at<a href=\"https://teamwork.com/\" style=\"color: #1e1f21; font-size: 12px;\">&nbsp;</a><a href=\"https://www.teamwork.com/\">Teamwork</a>, says, \"Creative directors should focus on ensuring that all brand touchpoints are cohesive and consistent, both visually and in terms of messaging, while also shepherding the idea of experimentation and concerted risk-taking within the team.\"</p> \n<blockquote>\n Coppola says, \"Your team's creative director should always be thinking ahead to what the future could look like for the brand and the market as a whole, which means pushing ideas further and challenging the status quo of what's expected.\"\n</blockquote> \n<p>Coppola adds, \"Equally as important, creative directors should be close to the customer, understanding what makes them tick inside and out. Knowing your target customer and being able to see the world through their eyes is the best way to build a brand that resonates with them.\"</p> \n<p>If you can only hire one new marketer in 2022, you'll want to strongly consider the importance of having a creative director if you don't already have one. Even a small but mighty team of marketers needs a creative director to nurture their strengths and guide the overarching vision.</p> \n<p>Additionally, if your business works with freelancers, agencies, or contractors, a creative director can help streamline those processes and ensure consistency across marketing channels.</p> \n<p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/adam%20day%20on%20top%20marketing%20role%20of%202022.png?width=1200&amp;name=adam%20day%20on%20top%20marketing%20role%20of%202022.png\" alt=\"adam day on top marketing role of 2022\" width=\"1200\" style=\"width: 1200px;\"></p> \n<h3><strong>2. Creative Assistant </strong></h3> \n<p>The second most-voted for role in 2022 is a creative assistant.</p> \n<p>If you already have someone in a director-level or manager-level role, it makes sense to consider how you might help alleviate some of their responsibilities by hiring an assistant.</p> \n<p>A creative assistant is an entry-level professional who will create promotional materials for your brand — those materials could include promotional videos, advertising campaigns, press releases, or social media posts.</p> \n<p>A creative assistant will also help your creative director or manager by handling the day-to-day creation of specific marketing materials — for instance, they might write copy, produce designs or infographics, or conduct market research to identify future trends and campaign ideas.</p> \n<p>A creative assistant can be a strategic, long-term play for your team. A creative assistant is an entry-level position, which means it's someone who is often new to the field of marketing.</p> \n<p>You might hire a creative assistant with impressive design skills, or a strong knowledge of the various social media platforms, and foster his or her growth on your team.</p> \n<p>Simply put, a creative assistant is a hire who will continue to grow on your team and could ultimately have a strong impact on the future of your brand's marketing strategy.&nbsp;</p> \n<h3><strong>3. Content Marketing Manager </strong></h3> \n<p>\"Let's face it,\" Dan Seavers, Talkwalker's Content Marketing Manager, told me,</p> \n<blockquote>\n \"Consumers are rapidly changing. They are savvier, smarter, and more active in their research. And they no longer want to be sold to. They want to be educated, entertained, excited, enthralled, anything … but not sold to.\"\n</blockquote> \n<p>Seavers told me that this shift in consumer behavior has led to content marketing as an essential component for any business' bottom line.</p> \n<p>And a strong <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/content-marketing\">content marketing strategy</a> needs a content marketing manager.</p> \n<p>Why? Well, as Seavers puts it, \"To do [content marketing] properly, you need content. A lot of content. We're talking blogs, videos, podcasts, tweets, reports, case studies, TikTok dances, and more — all weaved into an epic journey that leads consumers from discovery to purchase.\"</p> \n<p>Unbounce's VP of Marketing, Meg Sakakibara, agrees that a content marketing manager is vital for any marketing team.&nbsp;</p> \n<p>Sakakibara says, \"Content marketing managers are critical for brands today that need a voice that cuts through the noise, builds trust, and ensures content isn't just a pleasant accessory — it drives conversions.\"</p> \n<p>Sakakibara adds, \"After analyzing the most influential elements for conversion in 40,000 landing pages, Unbounce found that copy influenced conversion more than 2X as much as design did. Content isn't just the king/queen — it's the whole kingdom. By investing in content marketing and new technologies like<a href=\"https://unbounce.com/conversion-intelligence/\">&nbsp;Unbounce's Conversion Intelligence Platform</a>, people are using content and optimization to convert more leads, sales, and sign-ups to win in this competitive space.\"</p> \n<p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/meg%20sakakibara%20on%20top%20marketing%20role%20of%202022.png?width=1200&amp;name=meg%20sakakibara%20on%20top%20marketing%20role%20of%202022.png\" alt=\"meg sakakibara on top marketing role of 2022\" width=\"1200\" style=\"width: 1200px;\"></p> \n<p>So what should you look for in a content marketing manager?</p> \n<p>Among other things, an effective content marketing manager will execute digital content strategies across platforms, drive traffic and engagement, have a deep understanding of what types of content perform best on which channels, and consistently evaluate how each campaign performs — and shift when necessary.</p> \n<p>Additionally, Seaver told me,&nbsp;\"To be good, your content marketing manager should always have one eye on your consumers' ecosystem. <em>Where do they cluster online? What do they talk about? What are they looking for in a product? What problem do they have that you can solve? </em><a href=\"https://www.talkwalker.com/blog/content-strategy\">Their content strategy</a>&nbsp;will answer all of these questions, piece by piece. Slowly building that brand and consumer relationship from awareness — to having your consumers wonder how they can go on without you.\"</p> \n<p>Finally, a good content marketing manager needs to be a strong fit for your brand and goals. Content marketing is about delivering unique value to your intended audiences — which means your marketing manager needs to know, inside and out, who your target audience is and what they care about.</p> \n<p>As Microsoft's Group Marketing Manager Nora Xu puts it, \"It goes beyond a single touchpoint with an action to purchase your product, to a flywheel of inspirational and educational content that meets them where they are. On the <a href=\"https://ads.microsoft.com/\">Microsoft Advertising</a> brand marketing team, I look for people who can get into the mindset of our audience and create content that makes them feel seen and connected with our brand.\" &nbsp;</p> \n<p>Ultimately, <em>you</em> know what's best for your business needs. Take a careful look at your team's current strengths, and aim to identify a role that can help fill in the gaps.</p> \n<p>Once you're ready to begin the recruitment process, take a look at these <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/marketing-job-descriptions\">17 marketing job descriptions</a> to attract the right hire.&nbsp;</p> \n<p></p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" a checkbox to your workbook may sound simple but it can expand the possibilities of what you can do in <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/microsoft-excel\">Excel</a>.</p>  \n<p>From checklists to graphs, there’s so much you can do. However, it starts with the checkbox.</p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=9ff7a4fe-5293-496c-acca-566bc6e73f42&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; \" alt=\"Download 10 Excel Templates for Marketers [Free Kit]\" src=\"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/9ff7a4fe-5293-496c-acca-566bc6e73f42.png\"></a></p> \n<p>Learn everything you need to know about checkboxes below.</p> \n<h2>How to Insert a Checkbox in Excel</h2> \n<ol start=\"1\"> \n <li> <h3>Add the developer tab to your Ribbon.</h3> <img alt=\"\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20to%20Insert%20a%20Checkbox%20in%20Excel%20in%204%20Easy%20Steps-2.png?width=624&amp;name=How%20to%20Insert%20a%20Checkbox%20in%20Excel%20in%204%20Easy%20Steps-2.png\" title=\"\" width=\"624\" style=\"font-style: normal; font-variant-ligatures: normal; font-variant-caps: normal; font-weight: 400; font-size: 18px; font-family: AvenirNext, 'Helvetica Neue', Helvetica, Arial, sans-serif; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\"></li> \n <li> <h3>Navigate to the Developer tab and locate the \"Checkbox\" option.</h3> <h3 style=\"font-style: normal; font-variant-ligatures: normal; font-variant-caps: normal; font-family: AvenirNext, 'Helvetica Neue', Helvetica, Arial, sans-serif; color: #33475b;\"><img alt=\"\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20to%20Insert%20a%20Checkbox%20in%20Excel%20in%204%20Easy%20Steps.png?width=624&amp;name=How%20to%20Insert%20a%20Checkbox%20in%20Excel%20in%204%20Easy%20Steps.png\" title=\"\" width=\"624\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\"></h3> </li> \n <li> <h3>Select the cell where you want to add the checkbox control then click the checkbox.</h3> <img alt=\"\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20to%20Insert%20a%20Checkbox%20in%20Excel%20in%204%20Easy%20Steps-1.gif\" title=\"\" style=\"font-style: normal; font-variant-ligatures: normal; font-variant-caps: normal; font-weight: 400; font-size: 18px; font-family: AvenirNext, 'Helvetica Neue', Helvetica, Arial, sans-serif; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\"></li> \n <li> <h3>Right-click the checkbox to edit the text and adjust sizing.</h3> <img alt=\"\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20to%20Insert%20a%20Checkbox%20in%20Excel%20in%204%20Easy%20Steps-2.gif\" title=\"\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\"></li> \n</ol> \n<p>To do this on <strong>Windows</strong>, click File &gt; Options &gt; Customize Ribbon. Then, select the Developer checkbox and click \"save.\" On <strong>IOS</strong>, click Excel &gt; Preferences &gt; Ribbon &amp; Toolbar &gt; Main Tabs. Then, select the Developer checkbox and save.</p> \n<p>On Windows, there are a few extra steps to see the checkbox option. Under the Developer tab, click \"Insert\" and under \"Form Controls,\" click the checkbox icon.</p> \n<p><strong>Note</strong>: Currently, you cannot use checkboxes in the web version of Excel. If you upload a workbook with these controls, you’ll first have to disable them to start editing.</p> \n<h2>How to Format a Checkbox in Excel</h2> \n<ol start=\"1\"> \n <li> <h3>Open up the format control.</h3> <img alt=\"\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20to%20Insert%20a%20Checkbox%20in%20Excel%20in%204%20Easy%20Steps.jpeg\" title=\"\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\"></li> \n <li> <h3>Modify the value and cell link, then click \"OK.\"</h3> <img alt=\"\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20to%20Insert%20a%20Checkbox%20in%20Excel%20in%204%20Easy%20Steps-1.png\" title=\"\" style=\"font-style: normal; font-variant-ligatures: normal; font-variant-caps: normal; font-weight: 400; font-size: 18px; font-family: AvenirNext, 'Helvetica Neue', Helvetica, Arial, sans-serif; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\"></li> \n</ol> \n<p>To access it on Windows, right-click the checkbox and select \"Format Control.\" On IOS, navigate to the \"Format\" tab and select \"Format Control.\"</p> \n<p>With value, there are three options:</p> \n<ul> \n <li><strong>Unchecked – </strong>This displays a box that is unchecked and returns a \"FALSE\" statement.</li> \n <li><strong>Checked – </strong>This displays a box that is checked and returns a \"TRUE\" statement.</li> \n <li><strong>Mixed – </strong>This will leave the checkbox empty as neither a true or false statement until an action is taken.</li> \n</ul> \n<p>As for the cell link, this contains the checkbox status (true or false) of the cell it’s referencing.</p> \n<p><img alt=\"\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20to%20Insert%20a%20Checkbox%20in%20Excel%20in%204%20Easy%20Steps.gif?width=550&amp;name=How%20to%20Insert%20a%20Checkbox%20in%20Excel%20in%204%20Easy%20Steps.gif\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block; width: 550px;\" title=\"\" width=\"550\"></p> \n<p>Now that you have those details down, you can start fully customizing your checkbox.</p> \n<h2>How to Delete A Checkbox in Excel</h2> \n<p>Deleting a checkbox in Excel is a simple two-step process:</p> \n<ol start=\"1\"> \n <li>Right-click the checkbox.</li> \n <li>Click \"delete\" on your keyboard.</li> \n</ol> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=7912de6f-792e-4100-8215-1f2bf712a3e5&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img to%20Insert%20a%20Checkbox%20in%20Excel%20in%204%20Easy%20Steps.gif":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx19/cdn54@2020_2/2022/03/14/08-15-16-042_7fd0d48126f8af61.webp","https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/7912de6f-792e-4100-8215-1f2bf712a3e5.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn23@2020_6/2022/03/14/08-15-13-174_5cfe01436a49f100.webp","https://track.hubspot.com/__ptq.gif?a=53&k=14&r=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.hubspot.com%2Fmarketing%2Finserting-check-box-excel&bu=https%253A%252F%252Fblog.hubspot.com%252Fmarketing&bvt=rss":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx8/cdn7@2020_5/2022/03/14/08-15-11-506_4288928b1c7924af.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1647245705115},{"createdTime":"2022-03-14 16:15:05","updatedTime":"2022-03-14 16:15:05","title":"How to Do A/B Testing: 15 Steps for the Perfect Split Test","link":"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/how-to-do-a-b-testing","description":"<p>When marketers like us create<a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/best-landing-page-builder\"> landing pages</a>, write email copy, or design call-to-action buttons, it can be tempting to use our intuition to predict what will make people click and connect.</p>  \n<p>However, you’re much better off conducting A/B testing than basing marketing decisions off of a “feeling”, as this can be detrimental to your results.</p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=5d42eade-1de3-4ff1-adba-6b1521e6cbde&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; margin: 0 auto; display: block; margin-top: 20px; margin-bottom: 20px\" alt=\"Free Download: A/B Testing Guide and Kit\" src=\"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/5d42eade-1de3-4ff1-adba-6b1521e6cbde.png\" align=\"middle\"></a></p> \n<p>Keep reading to learn how to conduct the entire A/B testing process before, during, and after data collection so you can make the best decisions from your results.</p> \n<a></a> \n<p></p> \n<p></p> \n<p>A/B testing can be valuable because different audiences behave, well, differently. Something that works for one company may not necessarily work for another. <span>In fact, conversion rate optimization (CRO) experts hate the term \"best practices\" because it may not actually be the best practice for&nbsp;</span><em>you</em><i>. </i>But, this kind of testing can be complex if you’re not careful.</p> \n<p>Let’s go over how A/B testing works to ensure that you don’t make incorrect assumptions about what your audience likes.</p> \n<h2>How does A/B testing Work?</h2> \n<p>To run an A/B test, you need to create two different versions of one piece of content, with changes to a single <strong>variable</strong>. Then, you'll show these two versions to two similarly sized audiences and analyze which one performed better over a specific period of time (long enough to make accurate conclusions about your results).</p> \n<p><img class=\"alignCenter shadow\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/a-b-testing-explanation.jpg?width=650&amp;name=a-b-testing-explanation.jpg\" alt=\"Explanation of what a/b testing is\" title=\"explanation of what a/b testing is\" width=\"650\" style=\"display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; width: 650px;\"></p> \n<p style=\"font-size: 12px; text-align: center;\"><a href=\"https://cxl.com/blog/ab-testing-guide/\"><em>Image Source</em></a></p> \n<p>A/B testing helps marketers observe how one version of a piece of marketing content performs alongside another. Here are two types of A/B tests you might conduct in an effort to increase your website's conversion rate:</p> \n<h3>Example 1: User Experience Test</h3> \n<p>Perhaps you want to see if moving a certain call-to-action (CTA) button to the top of your homepage instead of keeping it in the sidebar will improve its click-through rate.</p> \n<p>To A/B test this theory, you'd create another, alternative web page that uses the new CTA placement. The existing design with the sidebar CTA — or the \"<strong>control</strong>\" — is Version A. Version B with the CTA at the top is the \"<strong>challenger</strong>.\" Then, you'd test these two versions by showing each of them to a predetermined percentage of site visitors. Ideally, the percentage of visitors seeing either version is the same.</p> \n<p>Learn how to easily A/B test a component of your website with <a href=\"https://knowledge.hubspot.com/articles/kcs_article/cos-pages-editor/a/b-test-a-page\">HubSpot's Marketing Hub</a>.</p> \n<h3>Example 2: Design Test</h3> \n<p>Perhaps you want to find out if changing the color of your call-to-action (CTA) button can increase its click-through rate.</p> \n<p>To A/B test this theory, you'd design an alternative CTA button with a different button color that leads to the <em>same</em> landing page as the control. If you usually use a red call-to-action button in your marketing content, and the green variation receives more clicks after your A/B test, this could merit changing the default color of your call-to-action buttons to green from now on.</p> \n<p><a href=\"https://offers.hubspot.com/ab-testing-kit?hubs_post-cta=pillar_allphrase\" style=\"font-style: italic;\">To learn more about A/B testing, download our free introductory guide here.</a></p> \n<a></a> \n<h2>A/B Testing in Marketing</h2> \n<p>A/B testing has a multitude of benefits to a marketing team, depending on what it is you decide to test. Above all, though, these tests are valuable to a business because they're low in cost but high in reward.</p> \n<p>Let's say you employ a content creator with a salary of $50,000/year. This content creator publishes five articles per week for the company blog, totaling 260 articles per year. If the average post on the company's blog generates 10 leads, you could say it costs just over $192 to generate 10 leads for the business ($50,000 salary ÷ 260 articles = $192 per article). That's a solid chunk of change.</p> \n<p>Now, if you ask this content creator to spend two days developing an A/B test on <em>one</em> article, instead of writing <em>two</em> articles in that time period, you might burn $192 because you're publishing one fewer article. But if that A/B test finds you can increase each article's conversion rate from 10 to 20 leads, you just spent $192 to potentially double the number of customers your business gets from your blog.</p> \n<p>If the test fails, of course, you lost $192 — but now you can make your <em>next</em> A/B test even more educated. If that second test succeeds in doubling your blog's conversion rate, you ultimately spent $384 to potentially double your company's revenue. No matter how many times your A/B test fails, its eventual success will almost always outweigh the cost to conduct it.</p> \n<p></p> \n<p>There are many types of split tests you can run to make the experiment worth it in the end. Here are some common goals marketers have for their business when A/B testing:</p> \n<ul> \n <li><strong>Increased Website Traffic:</strong> Testing different blog post titles or webpage titles can change the number of people who click on that hyperlinked title to get to your website. This can increase website traffic as a result.</li> \n <li><strong>Higher Conversion Rate:</strong> Testing different locations, colors, or even anchor text on your CTAs can change the number of people who click these CTAs to get to a landing page. This can <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/a-b-test-landing-page-form-copy\">increase the number of people who fill out forms on your website</a>, submit their contact info to you, and \"convert\" into a lead.</li> \n <li><strong>Lower Bounce Rate:</strong> If your website visitors leave (or \"bounce\") quickly after visiting your website, testing different blog post introductions, fonts, or featured images can reduce this bounce rate and retain more visitors.</li> \n <li><strong>Lower Cart Abandonment:</strong> Ecommerce businesses see an average of <a href=\"https://baymard.com/lists/cart-abandonment-rate\">70% of customers leave their website with items in their shopping cart</a>. This is known as \"shopping cart abandonment\" and is, of course, detrimental to any online store. Testing different product photos, check-out page designs, and even where shipping costs are displayed can lower this abandonment rate.</li> \n</ul> \n<p>Now, let's walk through the checklist for setting up, running, and measuring an A/B test.</p> \n<a></a> \n<h2>How to Conduct A/B Testing<a href=\"https://offers.hubspot.com/ab-testing-kit?hubs_post-cta=imagebody&amp;_ga=2.4361779.1667640274.1563800435-1307414301.1541080541\"></a></h2> \n<p><a href=\"https://offers.hubspot.com/ab-testing-kit?hubs_post-cta=imagebody&amp;_ga=2.4361779.1667640274.1563800435-1307414301.1541080541\"><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/kissmetrics_Abtestkit_headerimage.png?width=650&amp;name=kissmetrics_Abtestkit_headerimage.png\" alt=\"ab test graphic\" width=\"650\" style=\"width: 650px; display: block; margin: 0px auto;\"></a></p> \n<p><a href=\"https://offers.hubspot.com/ab-testing-kit?hubs_post-cta=imagebody&amp;_ga=2.4361779.1667640274.1563800435-1307414301.1541080541\"></a><a href=\"https://offers.hubspot.com/ab-testing-kit?hubs_post-cta=pillar_allphrase\" style=\"font-weight: normal;\"></a><a href=\"https://offers.hubspot.com/ab-testing-kit?hubs_post-cta=pillar_allphrase\"><em>Follow along with our free A/B testing kit with everything you need to run A/B testing including a test tracking template, a how-to guide for instruction and inspiration, and a statistical significance calculator to see if your tests were wins, losses, or inconclusive.</em></a><a href=\"https://offers.hubspot.com/ab-testing-kit?hubs_post-cta=imagebody&amp;_ga=2.4361779.1667640274.1563800435-1307414301.1541080541\"></a></p> \n<a></a> \n<h3>Before the A/B Test</h3> \n<p>Let's cover the steps to take before you start your A/B test.</p> \n<h4>1. Pick one variable to test.</h4> \n<p>As you optimize your web pages and emails, you might find <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/26785/20-variables-every-marketer-should-be-testing.aspx\">there are a number of variables you want to test</a>. But to evaluate how effective a change is, you'll want to isolate one \"<strong>independent variable</strong>\" and measure its performance. Otherwise, you can't be sure which variable was responsible for changes in performance.</p> \n<p>You can test more than one variable for a single web page or email — just be sure you're testing them one at a time.</p> \n<p>To determine your variable, look at the elements in your marketing resources and their possible alternatives for design, wording, and layout. Other things you might test include email subject lines, sender names, and different ways to personalize your emails.</p> \n<p>Keep in mind that even simple changes, like changing the image in your email <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/call-to-action-ab-testing-ht\">or the words on your call-to-action button</a>, can drive big improvements. In fact, these sorts of changes are usually easier to measure than the bigger ones.</p> \n<p><strong>Note: </strong>There are some times when it makes more sense to test multiple variables rather than a single variable. This is a process called multivariate testing. If you're wondering whether you should run an A/B test versus a multivariate test, <a href=\"https://www.optimizely.com/resources/multivariate-test-vs-ab-test/\">here's a helpful article from Optimizely</a> that compares the two processes.</p> \n<h4>2. Identify your goal.</h4> \n<p>Although you'll measure several metrics during any one test, choose a primary metric to focus on <em>before</em> you run the test. In fact, do it before you even set up the second variation. This is your \"<strong>dependent variable</strong>,\" which changes based on how you manipulate the independent variable.</p> \n<p>Think about where you want this dependent variable to be at the end of the split test. You might even state an official <strong>hypothesis</strong> and examine your results based on this prediction.</p> \n<p>If you wait until afterward to think about which metrics are important to you, what your goals are, and how the changes you're proposing might affect user behavior, then you might not set up the test in the most effective way.</p> \n<h4>3. Create a 'control' and a 'challenger.'</h4> \n<p>You now have your independent variable, your dependent variable, and your desired outcome. Use this information to set up the unaltered version of whatever you're testing as your control scenario. If you're testing a web page, this is the unaltered page as it exists already. If you're testing a landing page, this would be the landing page design and copy you would normally use.</p> \n<p>From there, build a challenger — the altered website, landing page, or email that you’ll test against your control. For example, if you're wondering whether <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/social-proof-examples-landing-pages\">adding a testimonial to a landing page</a> would make a difference in conversions, set up your control page with no testimonials. Then, create your challenger with a testimonial.</p> \n<h4>4. Split your sample groups equally and randomly.</h4> \n<p>For tests where you have more control over the audience — like with emails — you need to test with two or more audiences that are equal in order to have conclusive results.</p> \n<p>How you do this will vary depending on the A/B testing tool you use. If you're a <a href=\"https://knowledge.hubspot.com/email-user-guide-v2/how-to-utilize-ab-testing-in-email\">HubSpot Enterprise customer conducting an A/B test on an email</a>, for example, HubSpot will automatically split traffic to your variations so that each variation gets a random sampling of visitors.</p> \n<h4>5. Determine your sample size (if applicable).</h4> \n<p>How you <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/email-a-b-test-sample-size-testing-time\">determine your sample size</a> will also vary depending on your A/B testing tool, as well as the type of A/B test you're running.</p> \n<p>If you're A/B testing an email, you'll probably want to send an A/B test to a subset of your list that is large enough to achieve statistically significant results. Eventually, you'll pick a winner and send the winning variation on to the rest of the list. (See \"The Science of Split Testing\" ebook at the end of this article for more on calculating your sample size.)</p> \n<p>If you're a HubSpot Enterprise customer, you'll have some help determining the size of your sample group using a slider. It'll let you do a 50/50 A/B test of any sample size — although all other sample splits require a list of at least 1,000 recipients.</p> \n<p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/how-to-do-a-b-testing-2.png?width=650&amp;name=how-to-do-a-b-testing-2.png\" alt=\"ab testing sample size settings in hubspot\" width=\"650\" style=\"width: 650px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\"></p> \n<p>If you're testing something that <em>doesn't</em> have a finite audience, like a web page, then how long you keep your test running will directly affect your sample size. You'll need to let your test run long enough to obtain a substantial number of views. Otherwise, it will be hard to tell whether there was a statistically significant difference between variations.</p> \n<h4>6. Decide how significant your results need to be.</h4> \n<p>Once you've picked your goal metric, think about how significant your results need to be to justify choosing one variation over another. Statistical significance is a super important part of the A/B testing process that's often misunderstood. If you need a refresher, I recommend <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/marketers-guide-understanding-statistical-significance\">reading this blog post on statistical significance from a marketing standpoint</a>.</p> \n<p>The higher the percentage of your confidence level, the more sure you can be about your results. In most cases, you'll want a confidence level of 95% minimum — preferably even 98% — especially if it was a time-intensive experiment to set up. However, sometimes it makes sense to use a lower confidence rate if you don't need the test to be as stringent.</p> \n<p><a href=\"https://www.linkedin.com/in/matthew-rheault-322b051b\">Matt Rheault</a>, a senior software engineer at HubSpot, likes to think of statistical significance like placing a bet. What odds are you comfortable placing a bet on? Saying \"I'm 80% sure this is the right design and I'm willing to bet everything on it\" is similar to running an A/B test to 80% significance and then declaring a winner.</p> \n<p>Rheault also says you’ll likely want a higher confidence threshold when testing for something that only slightly improves conversion rate. Why? Because random variance is more likely to play a bigger role.</p> \n<p>\"An example where we could feel safer lowering our confidence threshold is an experiment that will likely improve conversion rate by 10% or more, such as a redesigned hero section,\" he explained.</p> \n<p>\"The takeaway here is that the more radical the change, the less scientific we need to be process-wise. The more specific the change (button color, microcopy, etc.), the more scientific we should be because the change is less likely to have a large and noticeable impact on conversion rate.\"</p> \n<h4>7. Make sure you're only running one test at a time on any campaign.</h4> \n<p>Testing more than one thing for a single campaign — even if it's not on the same exact asset — can complicate results. For example, if you A/B test an email campaign that directs to a landing page at the same time that you’re A/B testing that landing page, how can you know which change caused the increase in leads?</p> \n<a></a> \n<h3>During the A/B Test</h3> \n<p>Let's cover the steps to take during your A/B test.</p> \n<h4>8. Use an A/B testing tool.</h4> \n<p>To do an A/B test on your website or in an email, you'll need to use an A/B testing tool. If you're a HubSpot Enterprise customer, the HubSpot software has features that let you A/B test emails (<a href=\"https://knowledge.hubspot.com/email-user-guide-v2/how-to-utilize-ab-testing-in-email\">learn how here</a>), calls-to-action (<a href=\"https://knowledge.hubspot.com/cta-user-guide-v2/how-to-create-an-a-b-variation-test-for-calls-to-action\">learn how here</a>), and landing pages (<a href=\"https://knowledge.hubspot.com/landing-page-user-guide-v2/how-to-ab-test-landing-pages\">learn how here</a>).</p> \n<p>For non-HubSpot Enterprise customers, other options include <a href=\"http://www.google.com/analytics\">Google Analytics</a>, which lets you A/B test up to 10 full versions of a single web page and compare their performance using a random sample of users.</p> \n<h4>9. Test both variations simultaneously.</h4> \n<p>Timing plays a significant role in your marketing campaign’s results, whether it's time of day, day of the week, or month of the year. If you were to run Version A during one month and Version B a month later, how would you know whether the performance change was caused by the different design or the different month?</p> \n<p>When you run A/B tests, you'll need to run the two variations at the same time, otherwise you may be left second-guessing your results.</p> \n<p>The only exception here is if you're testing timing itself, like finding the optimal times for sending out emails. This is a great thing to test because depending on what your business offers and who your subscribers are, the optimal time for subscriber engagement can vary significantly by industry and target market.</p> \n<h4>10. Give the A/B test enough time to produce useful data.</h4> \n<p>Again, you'll want to make sure that you let your test run long enough to obtain a substantial sample size. Otherwise, it'll be hard to tell whether there was a statistically significant difference between the two variations.</p> \n<p>How long is long enough? Depending on your company and how you execute the A/B test, getting statistically significant results could happen in hours ... or days ... or weeks. A big part of how long it takes to get statistically significant results is how much traffic you get — so if your business doesn't get a lot of traffic to your website, it'll take much longer for you to run an A/B test.</p> \n<p><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/email-a-b-test-sample-size-testing-time\">Read this blog post to learn more about sample size and timing</a>.</p> \n<h4>11. Ask for feedback from real users.</h4> \n<p>A/B testing has a lot to do with quantitative data ... but that won't necessarily help you understand <em>why</em> people take certain actions over others. While you're running your A/B test, why not collect qualitative feedback from real users?</p> \n<p>One of the best ways to ask people for their opinions is <a href=\"https://offers.hubspot.com/art-asking-survey-questions\">through a survey or poll</a>. You might add an exit survey on your site that asks visitors why they didn't click on a certain CTA, or one on your thank-you pages that asks visitors why they clicked a button or filled out a form.</p> \n<p>You might find, for example, that a lot of people clicked on a call-to-action leading them to an ebook, but once they saw the price, they didn't convert. That kind of information will give you a lot of insight into why your users are behaving in certain ways.</p> \n<a></a> \n<h3>After the A/B Test</h3> \n<p>Finally, let's cover the steps to take after your A/B test.</p> \n<h4>12. Focus on your goal metric.</h4> \n<p>Again, although you'll be measuring multiple metrics, keep your focus on that primary goal metric when you do your analysis.</p> \n<p>For example, if you tested two variations of an email and chose leads as your primary metric, don’t get caught up on open rate or click-through rate. You might see a high click-through rate and poor conversion rates, in which case you might end up choosing the variation that had a lower click-through rate in the end.</p> \n<h4>13. Measure the significance of your results using our A/B testing calculator.</h4> \n<p>Now that you've determined which variation performs the best, it's time to determine whether your results are statistically significant. In other words, are they enough to justify a change?</p> \n<p>To find out, you'll need to conduct a test of statistical significance. You could do that manually ... or you could just plug in the results from your experiment to <a href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/ab-test-calculator\">our free A/B testing calculator</a>.</p> \n<p>For each variation you tested, you'll be prompted to input the total number of tries, like emails sent or impressions seen. Then, enter the number of goals it completed — generally you'll look at clicks, but this could also be other types of conversions.</p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><img class=\"alignCenter shadow\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/hubspot-a-b-testing-calculator.png?width=1500&amp;name=hubspot-a-b-testing-calculator.png\" alt=\"hubspot ab testing calculator\" title=\"hubspot-a-b-testing-calculator.png\" width=\"1500\" style=\"width: 1500px; margin: 0px auto;\"></p> \n<p>The calculator will spit out the confidence level your data produces for the winning variation. Then, measure that number against the value you chose to determine statistical significance.</p> \n<h4>14. Take action based on your results.</h4> \n<p>If one variation is statistically better than the other, you have a winner. Complete your test by disabling the losing variation in your A/B testing tool.</p> \n<p>If neither variation is statistically better, you've just learned that the variable you tested didn't impact results, and you'll have to mark the test as inconclusive. In this case, stick with the original variation, or run another test. You can use the failed data to help you figure out a new iteration on your new test.</p> \n<p>While A/B tests help you impact results on a case-by-case basis, you can also apply the lessons you learn from each test and apply it to future efforts.</p> \n<p>For example, if you've conducted A/B tests in your email marketing and have repeatedly found that using numbers in email subject lines generates better clickthrough rates, you might want to consider using that tactic in more of your emails.</p> \n<h4>15. Plan your next A/B test.</h4> \n<p>The A/B test you just finished may have helped you discover a new way to make your marketing content more effective — but don't stop there. There’s always room for more optimization.</p> \n<p>You can even try conducting an A/B test on another feature of the same web page or email you just did a test on. For example, if you just tested a headline on a landing page, why not do a new test on body copy? Or a color scheme? Or images? Always keep an eye out for opportunities to increase conversion rates and leads.</p> \n<p>You can use HubSpot’s A/B Test Tracking Kit to plan and organize your experiments.</p> \n<p><a href=\"https://offers.hubspot.com/ab-testing-kit\"><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/ab%20test%20tracking.png?width=1410&amp;name=ab%20test%20tracking.png\" alt=\"ab test tracking\" width=\"1410\" style=\"width: 1410px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\"></a></p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><a href=\"https://offers.hubspot.com/ab-testing-kit?_ga=2.268392270.1136205898.1644610869-1937536568.1644610869\">Download This Template Now</a></p> \n<h2>How to Read A/B Testing Results</h2> \n<p>As a marketer, you know the value of automation. Given this, you likely use software that handles the A/B test calculations for you — a huge help. But, after the calculations are done, you need to know how to read your results. Let’s go over how.</p> \n<h3>1. Check your goal metric.</h3> \n<p>The first step in reading your A/B test results is looking at your goal metric, which is usually conversion rate. After you’ve plugged your results into your A/B testing calculator, you’ll get two results for each version you’re testing. You’ll also get a significant result for each of your variations.</p> \n<h3>2. Compare your conversion rates.</h3> \n<p>By looking at your results, you’ll likely be able to tell if one of your variations performed better than the other. However, the true test of success is whether the results you have are statistically significant. This means that one variation performed better than the other at a significant level because, say, the CTA text was more compelling.</p> \n<p>Say, for example, Variation A had a 16.04% conversion rate and variation B had a 16.02% conversion rate, and your confidence interval of statistical significance is 95%. Variation A has a higher conversion rate, but the results are not statistically significant, meaning that Variation A won’t significantly improve your overall conversion rate.</p> \n<h3>3. Segment your audiences for further insights.</h3> \n<p>Regardless of significance, it's valuable to break down your results by audience segment to understand how each key area responded to your variations. Common variables for segmenting audiences are:</p> \n<ul> \n <li>Visitor type, or which version performed best for new visitors versus repeat visitors.</li> \n <li>Device type, or which version performed best on mobile versus desktop.</li> \n <li>Traffic source, or which version performed best based on where traffic to your two variations originated.</li> \n</ul> \n<p>Let’s go over some examples of A/B experiments you could run for your business.</p> \n<a></a> \n<h2>A/B Testing Examples</h2> \n<p>We’ve discussed how A/B tests are used in marketing and how to conduct one — but how do they actually look in practice?</p> \n<p>As you might guess, we run many A/B tests to increase engagement and drive conversions across our platform. Here are five examples of A/B tests to inspire your own experiments.</p> \n<h3>1. Site Search</h3> \n<p>Site search bars help users quickly find what they’re after on a particular website. HubSpot found from previous analysis that visitors who interacted with its site search bar were more likely to convert on a blog post. So, we ran an A/B test in an attempt to increase engagement with the search bar.</p> \n<p>In this test, search bar functionality was the independent variable and views on the content offer thank you page was the dependent variable. We used one control condition and three challenger conditions in the experiment.</p> \n<p>In the control condition (variant A), the search bar remained unchanged.</p> \n<p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/how-to-do-a-b-testing-search-bar-control.png?width=530&amp;name=how-to-do-a-b-testing-search-bar-control.png\" alt=\"control condition in the hubspot search bar A B test\" width=\"530\" style=\"width: 530px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\"></p> \n<p>In variant B, the search bar was made larger and more visually prominent, and the placeholder text was set to “search by topic.”</p> \n<p><img src=\"https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/ViXecYg9kH0cxCiinUo2MEC_o5Ou7k0ki1H2w-iuxEvK4DVLNWVFcGApFkFN4lxWuKgS0gYd0AQM90ZhdVuGILOJbhPtiDkpQD1GDPuudRacQWOtLrjlexJZnU2IHOb-ewbP1-4P\" width=\"400\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block; width: 400px;\" alt=\"variant b of the hubspot search bar AB test\"></p> \n<p>Variant C appeared identical to variant B, but only searched the HubSpot Blog rather than the entire website.</p> \n<p>In variant D, the search bar was made larger but the placeholder text was set to “search the blog.” This variant also searched only the HubSpot Blog</p> \n<p><img src=\"https://lh3.googleusercontent.com/v6MZzCEA1LPhNPyF584H6dUQ83SPGRgYAi-7d3oA_zNmYA5yuuRbnIHKg3pc2MUj1YQ9j8km9lNpgUSWS7ENVJTQeJfgmQSkFiwIxp8ZjHe5QRnxXshmfUYXfSgb0gy8jwdRKH4F\" width=\"350\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block; width: 350px;\" alt=\"variant c of the hubspot search bar AB test\"></p> \n<p>We found variant D to be the most effective: It increased conversions by 3.4% over the control and increased the percentage of users who used the search bar by 6.5%.</p> \n<h3>2. Mobile CTAs</h3> \n<p>HubSpot uses several CTAs for content offers in our blog posts, including ones in the body of posts as well as at the bottom of the page. <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/ab-testing-ctas\">We test these CTAs extensively</a> for optimize their performance.</p> \n<p>For our mobile users, we ran an A/B test to see which type of bottom-of-page CTA converted best. For our independent variable, we altered the design of the CTA bar. Specifically, we used one control and three challengers in our test. For our dependent variables, we used pageviews on the CTA thank you page and CTA clicks.</p> \n<p>The control condition included our normal placement of CTAs at the bottom of posts. In variant B, the CTA had no close or minimize option.</p> \n<p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/how-to-do-an-a-b-test-mobile-cta-variant-b-2.png?width=300&amp;name=how-to-do-an-a-b-test-mobile-cta-variant-b-2.png\" alt=\"variant B of the hubspot mobile CTA AB test\" width=\"300\" style=\"width: 300px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\">In variant C, mobile readers could close the CTA by tapping an X icon. Once it was closed out, it wouldn’t reappear.</p> \n<p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/how-to-do-an-a-b-test-mobile-cta-variant-c-2.png?width=300&amp;name=how-to-do-an-a-b-test-mobile-cta-variant-c-2.png\" alt=\"variant C of the hubspot mobile CTA AB test\" width=\"300\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; width: 300px;\"></p> \n<p>In variant D, we included an option to minimize the CTA with an up/down caret.</p> \n<p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/how-to-do-an-a-b-test-mobile-cta-variant-d-2.jpg?width=600&amp;name=how-to-do-an-a-b-test-mobile-cta-variant-d-2.jpg\" alt=\"variant d of hubspot's mobile cta A B test\" width=\"600\" style=\"width: 600px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\"></p> \n<p>Our tests found all variants to be successful. Variant D was the most successful, with a 14.6% increase in conversions over the control. This was followed by variant C with an 11.4% increase and variant B with a 7.9% increase.</p> \n<h3>3. Author CTAs</h3> \n<p>In another CTA experiment, HubSpot tested whether adding the word “free” and other descriptive language to author CTAs at the top of blog posts would increase content leads. Past research suggested that using “free” in CTA text would drive more conversions and that text specifying the type of content offered would be helpful for SEO and accessibility.</p> \n<p>In the test, the independent variable was CTA text and the main dependent variable was conversion rate on the content offer form.</p> \n<p>In the control condition, author CTA text was unchanged (see the orange button in the image below).</p> \n<p><img src=\"https://lh6.googleusercontent.com/n1OzWBuiCbJaR4e1VRrsyvuUHCLSuZc2xkYC-ovXP5DBPkYODIuK2A62Svs1IzuBWaeo3QN4dzkHyLRpU7sY4OLi6eOPm5U1WY7CM4SPjL-_rDx9q_RLB9e0twfcWn0Q-YK87c9K\" width=\"650\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block; width: 650px;\" alt=\"variant A of the author CTA AB test\"></p> \n<p>In variant B, the word “free” was added to the CTA text.</p> \n<p><img src=\"https://lh3.googleusercontent.com/GFVdnuSnm1W6pD64fPCw5D9bCrYtFbevTczl4wluvIxNOv-Qm_9G4FRfd5dYZubqdZDuHA7A3lLw2-oZO9SWvLx5JVPKhkDQdm-llrX3cW41bqeh-73z1kkEBZF1VP8FTXOqQMK3\" width=\"650\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block; width: 650px;\" alt=\"variant B of the author CTA AB test\"></p> \n<p>In variant C, descriptive wording was added to the CTA text in addition to “free.”</p> \n<p><img src=\"https://lh6.googleusercontent.com/QeqWmdjj84siDfYVc1eucUicRHouXKgN5MkeeFFMQiwiwhKz-6DUCP90rF1hFRl0rRq41F2Ffon4C5kLnz-8IqoaFeT0BFdXardJQDE7RGp_BXH4K3u8obwZHPpYlO6-dDDkSyy1\" width=\"650\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block; width: 650px;\" alt=\"variant C of the author CTA AB test\"></p> \n<p>Interestingly, variant B saw a loss in form submissions, down by 14% compared to the control. This was unexpected, since including \"free\" in content offer text is widely considered a best practice.</p> \n<p>Meanwhile, form submissions in variant C outperformed the control by 4%. It was concluded that adding descriptive text to the author CTA helped users understand the offer and thus made them more likely to download.</p> \n<h3>4. Blog Table of Contents</h3> \n<p>To help users better navigate the blog, HubSpot tested a new Table of Contents (TOC) module. The goal was to improve user experience by presenting readers with their desired content more quickly. We also tested whether adding a CTA to this TOC module would increase conversions.</p> \n<p>The independent variable of this A/B test was the inclusion and type of TOC module in blog posts, and the dependent variables were conversion rate on content offer form submissions and clicks on the CTA inside the TOC module.</p> \n<p>The control condition did not include the new TOC module —control posts either had no table of contents, or a simple bulleted list of anchor links within the body of the post near the top of the article (pictured below).</p> \n<p><img src=\"https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/cVNqdOuWN_4G96kpE7W5pyjhWr8-zIh5iRjIDH7wDh6pOXXarbPbxzuzm6fQyubShTcuQzmLjFhy3-eclMEj-aKIfcfp3_Sj_SA8hNXoXIQt2NW29tIIDhy3QLV9NPS2eZhdcJHS\" width=\"650\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block; width: 650px;\" alt=\"variant A of the hubspot blog chapter module AB test\"></p> \n<p>In variant B, the new TOC module was added to blog posts. This module was sticky, meaning it remained onscreen as users scrolled down the page. Variant B also included a content offer CTA at the bottom of the module.</p> \n<p><img src=\"https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/s8XFuXNaFnWSuzevJwaFUyPyJtkSnUs93qMYZU9RHUnK0u3h9vVdFlXti1_rAVZTU1hFYK14P9iUR2AfSgXGXKH-4aDe_r5D4fDC3K8dUcWmmBLBhfAJWN0QPza1DlUS1qHvvZJZ\" width=\"650\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block; width: 650px;\" alt=\"variant B of the hubspot blog chapter module AB test\"></p> \n<p>Variant C included an identical module to variant B but with the CTA removed.</p> \n<p><img src=\"https://lh3.googleusercontent.com/4HFWXYjCae6K8X-R4Q0nbPMbe_OI5m5-gNna6UISmZVQRoKQnFvXU5_rruzPmpCoKHgdYhunW_WVrUKqpzfQTGgJqSjz1UyAWHBGWxvwHtcwsxIcrEQx9V2nCvZufSTZ96LK4mXR\" width=\"650\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block; width: 650px;\" alt=\"variant C of the hubspot blog chapter module AB test\"></p> \n<p>Both variants B and C did not increase the conversion rate on blog posts. The control condition outperformed variant B by 7% and performed equally with variant C. Also, few users interacted with the new TOC module or the CTA inside the module.</p> \n<h3>5. Review Notifications</h3> \n<p>To determine the best way of gathering customer reviews, we ran a split test of email notifications versus in-app notifications. Here, the independent variable was the type of notification and the dependent variable was the percentage of those who left a review out of all those who opened the notification.</p> \n<p>In the control, HubSpot sent a plain text email notification asking users to leave a review. In variant B, HubSpot sent an email with a certificate image including the user’s name.</p> \n<p><img src=\"https://lh3.googleusercontent.com/1uBsYglIwFmXp-L0b_zQsSq5-lTYVSnN1B0-ewKYiRz9uZrXttvE8h38jEOFl9Q0GDD7s3x60WUknh7BxJEPMGIRuTCk7sMrPshNnxzyEkP935SLHiWrJrhNUPDh5Bf6JKu4kmMf\" width=\"500\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block; width: 500px;\" alt=\"variant B of the hubspot notification AB test\"></p> \n<p>For variant C, HubSpot sent users an in app-notification.</p> \n<p><img src=\"https://lh4.googleusercontent.com/Uaesq2m_BCCmf8leXIo30qCSQcQ7-8aadq4wtiyYUw73FG31jU1oD36OD52zDcLdRqbzpK_JovaJTKZYfvfbKdthSwnY8DEICqnUMSwayGKMFX0VsRddFnKexXHPYvahohwIa_HU\" width=\"500\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block; width: 500px;\" alt=\"variant C of the hubspot notification AB test\"></p> \n<p>Ultimately, both emails performed similarly and outperformed the in-app notifications. About 25% of users who opened an email left a review versus the 10.3% who opened in-app notifications. Emails were also more often opened by users.</p> \n<h2>Start A/B Testing Today</h2> \n<p>A/B testing allows you to get to the truth of what content and marketing your audience wants to see. Learn how to best carry out some of the steps above using the free e-book below.</p> \n<p><em>Editor's note: This post was originally published in May 2016 and has been updated for comprehensiveness.</em></p> \n<p><em></em></p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" 16:15:05","updatedTime":"2022-03-14 16:15:05","title":"5 Reasons Why Brands Lose Followers on Instagram [HubSpot Blog Data]","link":"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/losing-followers-instagram","description":"<p>According to <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/hubspot-blog-social-media-marketing-report\">HubSpot Blog Research</a>, 14% of <a href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/instagram-marketing\">Instagram marketers</a> report losing followers from 2020 to 2021.</p> \n<p>If you’re a part of that 14%, you may be panicking trying to figure out what’s causing the decline.</p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=9294dd33-9827-4b39-8fc2-b7fbece7fdb9&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; \" alt=\"New Data: Instagram Engagement Report [2022 Version]\" src=\"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/9294dd33-9827-4b39-8fc2-b7fbece7fdb9.png\"></a></p> \n<p>Don’t fret – we’ve got you covered. Below, we’re covering the top reasons why brands lose followers on Instagram and <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/gain-instagram-followers\">how to regain them</a>.</p> \n<h2>Why am I losing so many followers on Instagram?</h2> \n<h3>1. You’re not posting often enough or posting too much.</h3> \n<p>When <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/hubspot-blog-social-media-marketing-report\">we surveyed Instagram marketers</a>, 40% said that not posting enough is the number one reason why brands lose followers.</p> \n<p>Meanwhile, 33% said posting too much can have the same impact.</p> \n<p>When it comes to posting, it’s all about striking the right balance. You want to post enough to make sure you’re reaching your target audience and not disappearing in a sea of posts.</p> \n<p>However, you don’t want to post too much that your audience is getting flooded with your posts all over their timeline.</p> \n<p>Here are a few guidelines: First, post at least once a day on the platform – whether it’s on Instagram Stories, Reels, or in-feed. If you have to choose, Stories is probably the best option as marketers surveyed say it’s the second-best way to gain followers behind going live.</p> \n<p>Second, share an in-feed post two to three times a week. You can increase this cadence based on how your audience responds but you probably shouldn’t lower it.</p> \n<h3>2. You’re being too sales-y.</h3> \n<p>The second most popular reason why your brand is losing followers is that your content is too focused on selling, according to 39% of Instagram marketers surveyed.</p> \n<p>Our survey found that content centered around a brand’s products/services is leveraged by 39% of IG marketers and has the second-highest ROI.</p> \n<p>However, if it’s the only type of content you post, you might alienate your audience.</p> \n<p>Again, balance is the keyword here.</p> \n<p>In addition to posts that highlight your products and/or services, you should also post content that:</p> \n<ul> \n <li>Reflects your brand values.</li> \n <li>Invites conversation.</li> \n <li>Builds community.</li> \n</ul> \n<p>Another effective content strategy? Make your audience laugh.</p> \n<p>Our survey revealed that funny content is the most effective for getting followers, shares, and engagement on Instagram.</p> \n<h3>3. You had bot followers.</h3> \n<p>If you <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/buy-instagram-followers\">purchased bot followers</a>, you’ll be in for a rude awakening when they all disappear and your follower list tanks.</p> \n<p>39% of Instagram marketers surveyed say this is the third most popular reason why brands lose followers.</p> \n<p>While it’s tempting to buy bots to give the semblance of a strong follower base, this practice will only hurt you in the long run.</p> \n<p>Instead, focus on building a follower list organically through a consistent posting schedule, sharing valuable content, following trends, and listening to your data.</p> \n<p>It doesn’t have to take long either. Only 1% of marketers we surveyed say it took over a year to grow their followers by 1K. Most marketers (65%) said it took anywhere from one to six months.</p> \n<p>And 13% actually did it in less than a month.</p> \n<p>This is all to say that see this loss in followers as an opportunity to rebuild your Instagram page and get more reliable data on your audience.</p> \n<div>\n <iframe style=\"border: none; margin: 0px auto; display: block;\" src=\"https://listen.hubspot.com/embed/v2/smallPlayer/d40176e3\" width=\"560\" height=\"315\"></iframe>  \n</div> \n<h3>4. You don’t have a consistent aesthetic and voice.</h3> \n<p>One thing audiences love is consistency.</p> \n<p>Consistency in your branding and your creative assets is key in building strong brand recognition. In addition, consistency also helps build a visually appealing profile.</p> \n<p>If a user visits your profile and every post looks like it was created by a different brand, they’ll have a hard time understanding what your brand is all about and choose to unfollow you.</p> \n<p>Personally, if I’m scrolling and I notice a brand I don’t recognize on my timeline, I’ll visit their profile and if I don’t recognize their last few posts, I’ll likely unfollow them. I imagine many users behave the same way.</p> \n<p>With this in mind, figure out what your <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/agency/develop-brand-identity\">brand identity </a>and visual aesthetic are early on in your <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/branding\">branding</a> process.</p> \n<p>From there, you can leverage tools like Canva to build a visual profile that stays consistent across all platforms.</p> \n<h3>5. Your audience has evolved and you’re not keeping up.</h3> \n<p>It would be so easy to market to our audiences if their interests and behaviors always stayed the same.</p> \n<p>Unfortunately, that isn’t the case.</p> \n<p>This requires marketers to stay on top of what attracts and retains their audiences. One of the most effective ways to do this is by relying on your data. What is it telling you?</p> \n<p>Say you’re HubSpot and our feed consists of customer success stories, product highlights, company values, and industry trends.</p> \n<p>Perhaps content surrounding industry trends used to perform very well but you’ve noticed a slow decline over the past six months. Perhaps your audience is not as interested in this content or the format in which it’s being presented.</p> \n<p>Maybe if you used to leverage images, you should consider switching to video.</p> \n<p>Your Instagram strategy should be steered by what your data is telling you. If you don’t use it, you will quickly lose touch with your audience and slowly see your follower list decrease.</p> \n<p>Losing Instagram followers can be a scary reality to face. However, once you identify the reason behind the decline, you can address it and regain them.</p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=b1268983-9da6-4d67-9d3a-cfef2d9f3cff&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; \" alt=\"Improve your website with effective technical SEO. Start by conducting this  audit.&nbsp;&nbsp;\" src=\"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/b1268983-9da6-4d67-9d3a-cfef2d9f3cff.png\"></a></p> \n<p></p>  \n<img src=\"https://track.hubspot.com/__ptq.gif?a=53&amp;k=14&amp;r=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.hubspot.com%2Fmarketing%2Flosing-followers-instagram&amp;bu=https%253A%252F%252Fblog.hubspot.com%252Fmarketing&amp;bvt=rss\" alt=\"\" width=\"1\" height=\"1\" style=\"min-height:1px!important;width:1px!important;border-width:0!important;margin-top:0!important;margin-bottom:0!important;margin-right:0!important;margin-left:0!important;padding-top:0!important;padding-bottom:0!important;padding-right:0!important;padding-left:0!important; However, it can also be a source of negativity.</p>  \n<p>At its best, it can build community and at its worst, it can harm your brand and distract viewers from your content.</p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=b33cfd44-133a-49e3-a943-086c5679d485&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; \" alt=\"→ Free Templates: How to Use YouTube for Business [Download Now]\" src=\"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/b33cfd44-133a-49e3-a943-086c5679d485.png\"></a></p> \n<p>With this in mind, it’s important to know how to manage your comments. Discover how to delete and disable comments plus troubleshoot a common problem.</p> \n<h2>How to Turn on Comments on YouTube</h2> \n<p>When it comes to comments on a video-level, there are four main settings you can have:</p> \n<ul> \n <li><strong>Allow all comments</strong> – This allows user comments to be immediately visible.</li> \n <li><strong>Hold all comments for review – </strong>This requires you to approve every comment before it will show in the comment section. It will stay in the review tab for up to 60 days</li> \n <li><strong>Hold some comments for review – </strong>If some comments are flagged as potentially inappropriate by YouTube’s system, they will be hidden and held for review. You can also create a blocked words list that will hold comments containing or closely matching these terms.</li> \n <li><strong>Turn off comments – </strong>This prevents any user from leaving comments under your video.</li> \n</ul> \n<p>When you start a channel on YouTube, the default comment setting is to hold inappropriate comments for review and allow all other comments to show immediately under the video.</p> \n<p>If you had changed your settings and now want videos on your channel to display comments, you can do so by following these steps:</p> \n<ol start=\"1\"> \n <li> <h3>Access your Studio dashboard and click on \"Settings.\"</h3> <img alt=\"how to turn on comments on YouTube step 1\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20to%20Manage%20YouTube%20Comments.jpeg?width=250&amp;name=How%20to%20Manage%20YouTube%20Comments.jpeg\" title=\"\" width=\"250\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\"></li> \n <li> <h3>Navigate to the \"Advanced Settings\" tab.</h3> <img alt=\"how to turn on comments on YouTube step 3\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20to%20Manage%20YouTube%20Comments-1.jpeg?width=450&amp;name=How%20to%20Manage%20YouTube%20Comments-1.jpeg\" title=\"\" width=\"450\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block; width: 450px;\"></li> \n <li> <h3>Scroll down to the \"Comments\" section and select \"Allow all comments.\"</h3> <img alt=\"how to turn on comments on YouTube step 4\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20to%20Manage%20YouTube%20Comments-3.jpeg?width=450&amp;name=How%20to%20Manage%20YouTube%20Comments-3.jpeg\" title=\"\" width=\"450\" style=\"margin-left: auto; width: 303px; margin-right: auto; display: block;\" title=\"\" width=\"303\"></p> \n<h2>How to Delete YouTube Comments</h2> \n<p>When it comes to deleting YouTube comments, the rule of thumb is to use it with intention.</p> \n<p>It’s not sustainable or effective to delete every comment your brand disagrees with.</p> \n<p>You might ask, \"<em>Well, what if a comment says something false or damaging about our brand?</em>\" In this case, responding to the comment may be a more effective strategy. This way, you address the comment and can redirect viewers.</p> \n<p>To save time, focus on deleting comments that are hateful, explicit, or spammy.</p> \n<ol start=\"1\"> \n <li> <h3>Open YouTube Studio.</h3> </li> \n <li> <h3>Select \"Comments\" from the sidebar.</h3> </li> \n <li> <h3>Sift through your published comments.</h3> </li> \n <li> <h3>Tap \"More\" to see the option to remove the comment.</h3> </li> \n <li> <h3>Delete and return to the \"Comments\" dashboard.</h3> </li> \n</ol> \n<h2>How to Turn Off Comments on YouTube</h2> \n<p><img alt=\"youtube comment section turned off\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20to%20Manage%20YouTube%20Comments-Feb-03-2022-05-25-26-29-AM.jpeg\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\" title=\"youtube comment section turned off\"></p> \n<p>There are two ways to turn off comments on YouTube: at the channel-level and at the video-level.</p> \n<p>Here’s how it works at the channel level:</p> \n<ol start=\"1\"> \n <li> <h3>Access your Studio dashboard and click on \"Settings.\"</h3> <img alt=\"how to turn off comments on youtube step 1\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20to%20Manage%20YouTube%20Comments.jpeg?width=250&amp;name=How%20to%20Manage%20YouTube%20Comments.jpeg\" title=\"\" width=\"250\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block; width: 250px;\"></li> \n <li> <h3>Select \"Upload defaults.\"</h3> <img alt=\"how to turn off comments on youtube step 2\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20to%20Manage%20YouTube%20Comments-1.jpeg?width=450&amp;name=How%20to%20Manage%20YouTube%20Comments-1.jpeg\" title=\"\" width=\"450\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block; width: 450px;\"></li> \n <li> <h3>Navigate to the \"Advanced Settings\" tab.</h3> </li> \n</ol> \n<p><img alt=\"how to turn off comments on youtube step 3\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20to%20Manage%20YouTube%20Comments-3.jpeg?width=450&amp;name=How%20to%20Manage%20YouTube%20Comments-3.jpeg\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block; width: 450px;\" title=\"\" width=\"450\"></p> \n<h3>4. Scroll down to the Comments section.</h3> \n<img alt=\"how to turn off comments on youtube step 4\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20to%20Manage%20YouTube%20Comments-Feb-03-2022-05-25-25-95-AM.jpeg?width=450&amp;name=How%20to%20Manage%20YouTube%20Comments-Feb-03-2022-05-25-25-95-AM.jpeg\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block; width: 450px;\" title=\"\" width=\"450\"> \n<h3>5. Select \"Disable comments\" and click \"Save.\"</h3> \n<p><img alt=\"how to turn off comments on youtube step 5\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20to%20Manage%20YouTube%20Comments-4.jpeg?width=450&amp;name=How%20to%20Manage%20YouTube%20Comments-4.jpeg\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block; width: 450px;\" title=\"\" width=\"450\"></p> \n<p>To turn off comments on a specific video, you can do this during the uploading process.</p> \n<ol start=\"1\"> \n <li> <h3>In the \"Details\" tab of the upload, scroll all the way down to \"Show more.\"</h3> <img alt=\"turn off comments on a specific video step 1\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20to%20Manage%20YouTube%20Comments-Feb-03-2022-05-25-26-98-AM.jpeg\" title=\"\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\"></li> \n <li> <h3>Under \"Comments and Ratings,\" choose \"Disable comments.\"</h3> </li> \n</ol> \n<p><img alt=\"turn off comments on a specific video step 2\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20to%20Manage%20YouTube%20Comments-2.jpeg?width=415&amp;name=How%20to%20Manage%20YouTube%20Comments-2.jpeg\" style=\"margin-left: auto; width: 415px; margin-right: auto; display: block;\" title=\"\" width=\"415\"></p> \n<p>Note that you can change this setting later after uploading your video.</p> \n<h2>Troubleshooting: Youtube Comments Not Loading</h2> \n<p>If your YouTube comments aren’t loading, there’s a good chance it’s your internet connection. If your connection is slow and unreliable, the comment section may not load properly.</p> \n<p>Another reason why your comments may not load is if you’re using a different viewport. While on the web app, YouTube comments load automatically when you scroll, on the mobile app, you must tap to see the comments section.</p> \n<p>Lastly, certain browser extensions may affect how elements load on a page. As such, test disabling your browser extensions if your comments are not loading.</p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=7e8681b3-9162-45a4-b6a1-f33ff244a78a&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; \"
