16:15:05","updatedTime":"2022-03-14 16:15:05","title":"YouTube vs. Vimeo: Which Video Platform is Best for Your Business? [New Data]","link":"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/youtube-vs-vimeo","description":"<p>While YouTube is obviously the <a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/yt/about/press/\" style=\"color: #0091ae;\"><span>largest video hosting platform</span></a> on the web, it might not be the best choice for every business.</p>  \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=b33cfd44-133a-49e3-a943-086c5679d485&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; margin: 0 auto; display: block; margin-top: 20px; margin-bottom: 20px\" alt=\"→ Free Templates: How to Use YouTube for Business [Download Now]\" src=\"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/b33cfd44-133a-49e3-a943-086c5679d485.png\" align=\"middle\"></a></p> \n<p>There are other factors to consider when choosing a home for your video marketing — such as cost, tech support, and video and audio quality — to name a few.&nbsp;</p> \n<p>To help you find the best fit for your company's unique needs, we compared YouTube directly against the smaller, more niche platform Vimeo across a number of factors. Read on to see the results, and decide for yourself.</p> \n<p class=\"p1\"></p> \n<h3>Number of Users</h3> \n<p><strong>Winner: YouTube</strong></p> \n<p><span style=\"color: #33475b;\">There's no real competition here. YouTube commands an audience of </span><a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/yt/about/press/\" style=\"color: #0091ae;\"><span>over two billion monthly users</span></a><span style=\"color: #33475b;\"> — almost half of the entire internet-using population. Vimeo's </span><a href=\"https://expandedramblings.com/index.php/vimeo-statistics/\" style=\"color: #0091ae;\"><span>230 million monthly viewers and 1.9 million </span></a><span style=\"color: #33475b;\">paid subscribers seem insignificant in contrast. For maximum reach, choose YouTube.</span></p> \n<h3>Search Optimization</h3> \n<p><strong>Winner: YouTube</strong></p> \n<p>YouTube leaves Vimeo in the dust here. YouTube is <a href=\"https://www.alexa.com/topsites\">the second largest search engine on the internet</a>, right after parent company Google. If you're planning to create a video tailored to a specific search query, (e.g., <em>how to pick a font for your website</em>), your video belongs on YouTube. Not only will it appear in search results directly on YouTube, but Google also <a href=\"https://www.wsj.com/articles/google-steers-users-to-youtube-over-rivals-11594745232\">seems to favor</a> videos from YouTube over those posted on other platforms.</p> \n<h3>Mobile</h3> \n<p><strong>Winner: YouTube</strong></p> \n<p><a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/intl/en-GB/about/press/\">70% of all YouTube views come from mobile</a>, and the YouTube mobile app is absolutely <a href=\"https://www.digitalinformationworld.com/2020/02/youtube-dominates-all-the-major-apps-takes-away-most-streaming-time-on-smartphones.html\">dominating the mobile streaming space</a> — outranking even formidable competitors like Netflix, Hulu, and Twitch.</p> \n<p>Videos uploaded to Vimeo and YouTube are both optimized automatically for mobile, but YouTube offers more opportunities for mobile discovery and reach.</p> \n<h3>Cost</h3> \n<p><strong>Winner: YouTube</strong></p> \n<p>YouTube is free — even for businesses. But you might be wondering if Vimeo is as well.</p> \n<h4>Is Vimeo free to use?</h4> \n<p><span style=\"color: #33475b;\">Vimeo operates on a tiered pricing model, </span><a href=\"https://vimeo.com/upgrade\" style=\"color: #0091ae;\"><span>ranging from a free basic plan to a $75/month package </span></a><span style=\"color: #33475b;\">that includes unlimited live streaming.</span></p> \n<h4>Vimeo Pro vs YouTube</h4> \n<p>While Vimeo does have a free basic plan, it limits you to 500MB maximum storage per week.</p> \n<p>If you're okay with paying some money, you can get a Vimeo Pro plan. With Vimeo Pro, you'll have access to support, advanced analytics, and professional privacy.</p> \n<p>On the other hand, you can have unlimited storage for free on YouTube.</p> \n<h3>Support</h3> \n<p><strong>Winner: Vimeo</strong></p> \n<p>With their paid packages, Vimeo <a href=\"https://vimeo.com/upgrade\" style=\"color: #0091ae;\"><span>offers several levels of technical support</span></a> that could be a game-changer for businesses with little video expertise. YouTube offers plenty of <a href=\"https://support.google.com/youtube?__hstc=20629287.6ac66382cd6445e9a532bf78e26b2936.1629761983054.1644432577944.1644443037198.247&amp;__hssc=20629287.5.1644443037198&amp;__hsfp=2104872287#topic=7505892\" style=\"color: #0091ae;\"><span>free help documentation</span></a> and access to a (rather crowded) <a href=\"https://productforums.google.com/forum/?__hstc=20629287.6ac66382cd6445e9a532bf78e26b2936.1629761983054.1644432577944.1644443037198.247&amp;__hssc=20629287.5.1644443037198&amp;__hsfp=2104872287#!forum/youtube\" style=\"color: #0091ae;\"><span>support community</span></a>. Still, if you're seeking higher-touch, personalized support on-demand, a paid Vimeo account is the better option.</p> \n<h3>Storage</h3> \n<p><strong>Winner: YouTube</strong></p> \n<p>YouTube offers unlimited, free storage for all accounts, while Vimeo <a href=\"https://vimeo.com/upgrade\" style=\"color: #0091ae;\"><span>charges for storage on a tiered basis</span></a>. The basic, free Vimeo account option gives you 500MB of storage per week. With their highest level, $75/month package, you can store 7TB total with no weekly limits.</p> \n<h3>No Pre-Roll Ads</h3> \n<p><strong>Winner: Vimeo</strong></p> \n<p>If you upload your videos to YouTube, there's a good chance a pre-roll ad will play before it, which has the potential to deter some viewers from sticking around. Vimeo currently doesn't allow ads, and it doesn't look like they'll be changing this policy anytime soon.</p> \n<h3>Running Ad Campaigns</h3> \n<p><strong>Winner: YouTube</strong></p> \n<p>If you're thinking of running your own ads on a video platform, you can't beat YouTube (You also <a href=\"https://help.vimeo.com/hc/en-us/articles/224968628-Vimeo-PRO\">can't</a><a href=\"https://help.vimeo.com/hc/en-us/articles/224968628-Vimeo-PRO\"> purchase ad space on Vimeo</a>, even if you wanted to, because they don't allow it.)</p> \n<p>YouTube <a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/yt/advertise/\">offers an advanced, user-friendly ads platform</a>, as well as personalized support from a \"YouTube Advertising Expert\" when you spend $10 a day on ads.</p> \n<h3>Community</h3> \n<p><strong>Winner: Vimeo</strong></p> \n<p>User numbers don't tell the entire story. With such a massive audience on YouTube, the environment is naturally more competitive. It's easier for your video to get drowned out by thousands of others if you aren't planning to feature it somewhere off YouTube. Vimeo's smaller, more community-driven platform might be a better option if you're hoping to tap into an existing creative niche, or get featured on their <a href=\"https://vimeo.com/channels/staffpicks\">hand-curated staff picks page</a>.</p> \n<h3>Advanced Privacy Options</h3> \n<p><strong>Winner: Vimeo</strong></p> \n<p>Both YouTube and Vimeo give you the option to set videos to private or public (the default setting on YouTube is public), but Vimeo offers a handful of more nuanced, specific privacy options if that serves your interests. You can add a password protection option to videos, share a video only with people who follow your account, or even hide it from the Vimeo community — which could be useful if you plan on embedding the video on your website and want it to be viewable in only one place.</p> \n<h3>Customizable Player</h3> \n<p><strong>Winner: Vimeo</strong></p> \n<p>Vimeo's sleek embedded player <a href=\"https://help.vimeo.com/hc/en-us/articles/224972808-Customizing-the-embedded-player\">offers a number of useful customization options</a> that YouTube can't match, including hex color customization and the ability to include a custom player logo (on Business and PRO accounts). Plus, when you change the default customization options on your account, all previously embedded videos will update to reflect the changes automatically, with no need to go back and tinker with any code.</p> \n<h3>Analytics</h3> \n<p><strong>Winner: YouTube </strong></p> \n<p>YouTube takes the win here because <a href=\"https://support.google.com/youtube/answer/1714323?hl=en&amp;__hstc=20629287.6ac66382cd6445e9a532bf78e26b2936.1629761983054.1644432577944.1644443037198.247&amp;__hssc=20629287.5.1644443037198&amp;__hsfp=2104872287\" style=\"color: #0091ae;\"><span>all their analytics</span></a> — ranging from basic statistics like views to more advanced options — are completely free. Vimeo also offers <a href=\"https://vimeo.com/stats\" style=\"color: #0091ae;\"><span>powerful analytics tools</span></a> to evaluate performance, but you'll have to pay to access everything but basic stats.</p> \n<h3>Video Quality</h3> \n<p style=\"font-weight: bold;\">Winner: Vimeo</p> \n<p>When it comes to video quality, Vimeo beats out YouTube. In a test done by <a href=\"https://medium.com/@GreatUX/vimeo-vs-youtube-video-quality-18e51f83f916\">Medium</a>, Vimeo's video quality was crisp, clean, and easier to read. On the other hand, the same video on YouTube was blurry, making it much harder to follow.</p> \n<h3>Audio Quality</h3> \n<p style=\"font-weight: bold;\">Winner: Vimeo</p> \n<p>Again, when it comes to quality, Vimeo comes out on top. Sound quality is higher on Vimeo because the platform supports 320Kbps. However, to enjoy higher-quality videos and audio, you'll need to be subscribed to one of the paid plans.</p> \n<h3>Live Streaming</h3> \n<p style=\"font-weight: bold;\">Winner: YouTube</p> \n<p>Both Vimeo and YouTube have live streaming options, however, YouTube is the clear winner here because it's free. Vimeo offers live streaming with a paid plan. However, with Vimeo, you can upload new versions of the video and keep on using the same URL and upload higher quality recorded versions of a live stream, which you can edit before posting.</p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Imported%20sitepage%20images/youtube-vs-vimeo-mini-infographic-market-motive.jpg?width=790&amp;name=youtube-vs-vimeo-mini-infographic-market-motive.jpg\" alt=\"YouTube vs. Vimeo infographic\" width=\"790\" style=\"width: 790px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\"><span style=\"font-size: 12px;\"><a href=\"https://www.marketmotive.com/blog/online-marketing/vimeo-vs-youtube-which-should-you-be-using\" style=\"font-style: italic;\">Image Source</a></span></p> \n<h3>So which one should you choose?</h3> \n<p>It depends on what exactly you want to accomplish with your videos. If you're looking for a creative community where you can connect with other video creators and gain some exposure in a specific niche, Vimeo is a better place to start sharing your content. If you have business goals that revolve heavily around search optimization and ads, YouTube is your best bet.</p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=7e8681b3-9162-45a4-b6a1-f33ff244a78a&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; \" alt=\"New call-to-action\" src=\"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/7e8681b3-9162-45a4-b6a1-f33ff244a78a.png\"></a></p> \n<p></p>  \n<img src=\"https://track.hubspot.com/__ptq.gif?a=53&amp;k=14&amp;r=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.hubspot.com%2Fmarketing%2Fyoutube-vs-vimeo&amp;bu=https%253A%252F%252Fblog.hubspot.com%252Fmarketing&amp;bvt=rss\" alt=\"\" width=\"1\" height=\"1\" style=\"min-height:1px!important;width:1px!important;border-width:0!important;margin-top:0!important;margin-bottom:0!important;margin-right:0!important;margin-left:0!important;padding-top:0!important;padding-bottom:0!important;padding-right:0!important;padding-left:0!important; \">","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Tue, 08 Mar 2022 12:00:00 +0000","feedId":54,"bgimg":"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/b33cfd44-133a-49e3-a943-086c5679d485.png","linkMd5":"be7dafc5977404caa82c10b938b1410d","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx5oss/cdn64@2020_4/2022/03/14/08-15-05-875_cf13f3171c1652e5.webp","destWidth":625,"destHeight":59,"sourceBytes":6230,"destBytes":9478,"author":"kcook@hubspot.com (Karla Hesterberg)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/b33cfd44-133a-49e3-a943-086c5679d485.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx5oss/cdn64@2020_4/2022/03/14/08-15-05-875_cf13f3171c1652e5.webp","https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Imported%20sitepage%20images/youtube-vs-vimeo-mini-infographic-market-motive.jpg?width=790&name=youtube-vs-vimeo-mini-infographic-market-motive.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn56@2020_2/2022/03/14/08-15-12-999_5c49f26b5a0d36be.webp","https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/7e8681b3-9162-45a4-b6a1-f33ff244a78a.png":null,"https://track.hubspot.com/__ptq.gif?a=53&k=14&r=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.hubspot.com%2Fmarketing%2Fyoutube-vs-vimeo&bu=https%253A%252F%252Fblog.hubspot.com%252Fmarketing&bvt=rss":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn76@2020_6/2022/03/14/08-15-13-353_4ad67a02c3a430ec.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1647245705115},{"createdTime":"2022-03-14 16:15:05","updatedTime":"2022-03-14 16:15:05","title":"Mastering Facebook Ads In 2022 Through Incrementality","link":"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/facebook-ads-incrementality","description":"<p>There are many resources out there telling you how to optimize your Facebook ads to scale your business's growth. And while I'm sure they can help in some aspects, you're probably optimizing your campaigns based on the wrong metrics.</p> \n<p>In 2022, Facebook has <a href=\"https://zephoria.com/top-15-valuable-facebook-statistics/\">1.79 billion daily users</a>. There are plenty of opportunities to create Facebook ads that will drive impressions, link clicks, leads, and more. However, these metrics only scratch the surface of how much impact your Facebook ads can truly have on your business.</p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=ed40e380-bf04-4fea-b0c3-257696630e08&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; margin: 0 auto; display: block; margin-top: 20px; margin-bottom: 20px\" alt=\"Sign Up for HubSpot Academy's Free Facebook Ads Training Course\" src=\"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/ed40e380-bf04-4fea-b0c3-257696630e08.png\" align=\"middle\"></a></p> \n<p>As more industry experts focus their media buying on incremental gains, marketers can better measure their Facebook ads' positive, negative, or neutral impact on their business.</p> \n<h2>What is incrementality in Facebook Ads?</h2> \n<p>Incrementality allows marketers to understand how Facebook ads impact their business. Often, advertisers make optimizations to campaigns based on certain metrics, which can dramatically affect the end goal.</p> \n<p>It's crucial for businesses to identify what's working and what isn't — especially since Facebook's ad revenue worldwide was <a href=\"https://www.statista.com/statistics/277963/facebooks-quarterly-global-revenue-by-segment/\"><strong>$84.2 billion</strong> in 2020</a>. Whether you have a large or small Facebook advertising budget, you want to make sure it's generating results.</p> \n<p>Advertisers can measure incrementality by using control tests and comparing the results from those exposed to an ad versus those who have not. Once the tests have been completed, the results can help your business make smarter decisions on your Facebook ads and optimize your campaigns accordingly.</p> \n<h2>Why should marketers track incremental return on ad spend (iROAS)?</h2> \n<p>One minute you're a marketer, and the next, you're a data analyst. All jokes aside, information overload is very real in 2022. With all of this data available, there’s the assumption that it should be easy for marketers to pinpoint the best audience to target, understand what point they are at in the Facebook sales funnel, and the best methods to convert them.</p> \n<p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Facebook-Sales-Funnel.png?width=1104&amp;name=Facebook-Sales-Funnel.png\" alt=\"Facebook Sales Funnel\" width=\"1104\" style=\"width: 1104px;\"></p> \n<p>However, data dumps and compiling all of this information is incredibly time-consuming. And as digital marketing continues to expand, time is not always on our side. Businesses need to refocus their efforts from heavy reliance on data collection to doubling down on finding the <em>right</em> data—that can assist in smart optimizations and <a href=\"https://vistasocial.com/social-media-analytics/\">actionable insights</a> to fuel your Facebook campaign's bottom line.</p> \n<h2>How to Calculate Incremental Return on Ad Spend</h2> \n<p>The method for calculating iROAS is different for every publisher. The most methodical approach is by applying a <a href=\"https://www.facebook.com/business/help/1915029282150425\">holdout</a> to your Facebook campaign. The holdout on your campaign will act as a control group for Facebook users that will not see your ads. The remaining group of users will be the test audience for your Facebook campaign.</p> \n<p>After the test is complete, marketers can compare the results from the test group to the control group. The difference in the results will be your conversion lift, representing the incremental impacts on your conversions.</p> \n<p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/ROAS-Formula.png?width=760&amp;name=ROAS-Formula.png\" alt=\"How to calculate return on ad spend ROAS\" width=\"760\" style=\"width: 760px;\">iROAS is calculated similarly to <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/return-on-ad-spend?_ga=2.189840235.1519769113.1645056446-1004475094.1645056446\">ROAS</a>, which is revenue divided by cost. However, this measurement allows your business to understand which Facebook campaigns are working and which aren't. The calculation for iROAS is Incremental Revenue / Ad Spend = iROAS.</p> \n<p>In the YouTube video below, HubSpot details how to determine ad spend by understanding the bidding system used by ad networks.</p> \n<div class=\"hs-embed-wrapper\" style=\"position: relative; overflow: hidden; width: 100%; height: auto; padding: 0; max-width: 560px; max-height: 315px; min-width: 256px; display: block; margin: auto;\">\n <div class=\"hs-embed-content-wrapper\">\n  <div style=\"position: relative; overflow: hidden; max-width: 100%; padding-bottom: 56.25%; margin: 0px;\">\n   <iframe width=\"560\" height=\"315\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/JtwEBXoMa80\" frameborder=\"0\" allowfullscreen style=\"position: absolute; top: 0px; left: 0px; width: 100%; height: 100%; border: none;\"></iframe>\n  </div>\n </div>\n</div> \n<h2>3 Simple Ways to Increase Your Facebook's Ads Incrementality in 2022</h2> \n<p>Frequently data dumps fail due to the sheer amount of information available. Marketers may find many valid insights, but the delivery of this information can get lost in translation — especially if there is no clear direction. Brands looking to increase their Facebook ads incrementality should work with a <a href=\"https://agencyvista.com/\">leading marketing agency</a> with proven experience.</p> \n<p>However, if you're looking to get started on your own, below we'll walk you through the top three ways to increase your Facebook ad's incrementality to exceed your 2022 growth goals.</p> \n<h3>1. Audience Targeting</h3> \n<p>Facebook users at the top of the funnel versus the bottom will yield very different incrementality results. For example, you will see very different results if you're using a 5% lookalike audience of customers who purchased in the last month vs. remarketing to customers who purchased in the last few years.</p> \n<p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Facebook-Ad-Targeting.jpg?width=1600&amp;name=Facebook-Ad-Targeting.jpg\" alt=\"Creating audience for Facebook Ad targeting\" width=\"1600\" style=\"width: 1600px;\">Targeting new customers should be your most incremental audience segment since they would not have converted and made the purchase had it not been for your Facebook ad.</p> \n<p>This can also affect your bid strategies and budgets for remarketing audiences. For example, a customer who has purchased from you recently may not need a Facebook ad to prompt another purchase — this will depend on your product or service buying situation.</p> \n<h4><strong>Three Class of Buying Situations:</strong></h4> \n<ul> \n <li><strong>Routine decision-making: </strong>involves purchases that require very little thought after the original decision has been made. Such as gum, a chocolate bar, or a soft drink.</li> \n <li><strong>Limited decision-making: </strong>involves purchasing products that require a moderate amount of time and effort to compare models and brands before making a choice. This could be comparing which phone you are planning to upgrade to.</li> \n <li><strong>Extensive decision-making: </strong>involves an extensive consumer decision regarding whether or not to purchase a product. Examples include cars, homes, and education.</li> \n</ul> \n<h3>2. Ad Creative</h3> \n<p>I'm sure every marketer has heard about the study that found that the average attention span has decreased from 12 seconds to 8 seconds—while a goldfish holds a 9-second attention span. There is so much noise and clutter on social media that often, consumers will scroll right past your ad.</p> \n<p>Advertisers need to create Facebook ads that grab the viewers' attention and drive action. Facebook ad creative is one of the top ways to increase your incrementality.</p> \n<p>Learn from the best! We've collected the 50 best Facebook ads to inspire your next campaign. <a href=\"https://offers.hubspot.com/facebook-ad-examples?hubs_post-cta=body&amp;hubs_post=blog.hubspot.com/marketing/the-facebook-ad-types&amp;_ga=2.189840235.1519769113.1645056446-1004475094.1645056446\">Check out this exclusive lookbook</a> to get a head start on crafting the perfect ad to drive incremental revenue.</p> \n<h3>3. Facebook Placements</h3> \n<p>There are several placements for advertisers across Facebook, Instagram, Messenger, and Audience Network. But, not every placement works with every type of campaign.</p> \n<p>For example, an ad on audience network may spark brand awareness or interest but not drive an immediate conversion. The same goes for device targeting, often people are in discovery mode on mobile but complete the transaction on desktop.</p> \n<p>Most advertisers still recommend combining placements to maximize the results, but it is beneficial to understand where your most incremental audience is.</p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=4f0eef09-2c33-43c7-9dee-7dde3ae4071e&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; \" Place","link":"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/marketing-operations","description":"<p>One of my favorite movies is \"<a href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/School_of_Rock\">School of Rock</a>,\" which also happens to be one of 2003's best films. In the movie, Jack Black poses as a substitute teacher at a private school, and, after noticing the students are musically talented, he turns the 10-year-olds into a fully-fledged rock band.</p>  \n<p>When assigning roles to the students, he approaches the class president and deems her band manager because she had the organizational skills needed to help the band run smoothly. \"Summer,\" he says, \"You're in charge of the whole thing.\"</p> \n<p>When I think about marketing operations, I think of this quote — without a team, businesses that depend on technology would have a less-than-seamless experience carrying out their duties. In this post, you’ll learn more about marketing operations and why these teams are essential to a business.</p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"></p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=34155d81-37a6-4910-a596-3a77b9e5a99f&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; margin: 0 auto; display: block; margin-top: 20px; margin-bottom: 20px\" alt=\"Access Now: The State of Marketing Ops Professionals\" src=\"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/34155d81-37a6-4910-a596-3a77b9e5a99f.png\" align=\"middle\"></a></p> \n<a></a> \n<p></p> \n<p>The people involved in marketing operations build a foundation that reinforces and supports marketing efforts. It makes it easier to achieve goals by implementing systems to ensure marketers are best equipped to succeed at their jobs.</p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><img alt=\"what is marketing operations\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/Everything%20You%20Need%20to%20Know%20About%20Marketing%20Operations%20in%20One%20Place.png?width=624&amp;height=624&amp;name=Everything%20You%20Need%20to%20Know%20About%20Marketing%20Operations%20in%20One%20Place.png\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\" title=\"\" width=\"624\" height=\"624\"></p> \n<a></a> \n<h3 style=\"font-weight: bold;\">Why is marketing operations important?</h3> \n<p><a href=\"https://www.b2bmarketing.net/en/resources/articles/our-survey-stats-revealed-93-b2b-marketers-says-marketing-operations-function\">93% of B2B marketers</a> say the marketing operation’s function is important or critical to delivering digital transformation. After all, without marketing operations, it would be tough for marketing teams to complete essential activities effectively because they enable other marketing departments to bring cohesion to campaigns and processes.</p> \n<p>For example, as technology is necessary to carry out most marketing tasks, a team to manage the complexity of that technology and ensure it works as it should is also necessary — <em>which is exactly what MOps is</em>.</p> \n<p>Here are some examples of situations that can be rectified by having a marketing operations team:</p> \n<table> \n <tbody> \n  <tr> \n   <td>Problem</td> \n   <td>MOps Solution</td> \n  </tr> \n  <tr> \n   <td>Your investments in marketing technology don’t provide the solutions you thought they would.</td> \n   <td>MOps ensure that teams are enabled by technology solutions and eliminate tech debt.</td> \n  </tr> \n  <tr> \n   <td>You want to streamline data reporting and metrics tracking to understand ROI.</td> \n   <td>MOps focus on processes and systems for data reporting to enable teams.</td> \n  </tr> \n  <tr> \n   <td>Strategy execution is a timely process, and you want to lower the amount of time it takes from start to finish.</td> \n   <td>MOps helps team improve processes to become more efficient.</td> \n  </tr> \n </tbody> \n</table> \n<p>At HubSpot, the marketing ops team is responsible for supporting the systems and processes that enable the marketing team to perform optimally in their roles. This includes everything from permissions, conversational marketing, user data, forms, and email operations.</p> \n<p>An essential function of how well a marketing ops team works is proper management.</p> \n<p></p> \n<p>As a point of reference, marketing operations is the process of strategizing and optimizing, while marketing ops management defines how that strategizing and optimizing will happen.</p> \n<p>Since marketing operations management aims to increase efficiency, ops teams often have a hand in content planning and campaign analysis.</p> \n<a></a> \n<h3 style=\"font-weight: bold;\">Role of Marketing Operations</h3> \n<p>Marketing operations is a combination of different processes that contribute to marketing team success. The role of marketing ops encompasses:</p> \n<ul> \n <li>Project management</li> \n <li>Strategic planning</li> \n <li>Organization benchmarking</li> \n <li>Workflow process development and documentation</li> \n <li>Customer, market, and competitive intelligence research</li> \n <li>Performance measurement</li> \n <li>Campaign analysis and reporting</li> \n <li>Data management</li> \n <li>Process development and implementation</li> \n</ul> \n<p>Much of the role of marketing operations comes down to strategic decision making for key <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/digital-strategy-guide\">marketing strategies</a>, and seeing those projects through to completion based on analyzed data.</p> \n<a></a> \n<h2>Marketing Operations Strategy</h2> \n<p>Marketing ops team members need to have an expansive skillset. Some of the typical activities this department deals with are email operations, systems analysis, customer data and marketing, user operations, and lead rotation.</p> \n<p>All of these roles come together to align the process and platforms needed to carry out marketing tasks for the greater marketing team.</p> \n<p>When thinking about a marketing ops strategy, consider the problems the marketing ops team needs to solve, taking into account the needs of customers, stakeholders, and the employees of your company.</p> \n<a></a> \n<p></p> \n<h3 style=\"font-weight: bold;\">1. Identify what you want your operations strategy to accomplish for stakeholders.</h3> \n<p>Firstly, you need to effectively communicate and involve your stakeholder(s) when trying to create your marketing operations strategy. By doing so, you can better align the team and work toward solving high-level needs and priorities that may not be explicitly clear beforehand.</p> \n<p>This is where the importance of internal <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/34212/how-to-create-a-service-level-agreement-sla-for-better-sales-marketing-alignment.aspx\">service level agreements (SLAs)</a> come in. These contracts establish a set of deliverables to another party that sets clear expectations and mitigates issues that may arise.</p> \n<p>For instance, key stakeholders might want to make email marketing a more valuable process. The marketing ops team would then be responsible for the processes and systems that support this endeavor, ensuring that:</p> \n<ul> \n <li>The organization has effective email marketing technology</li> \n <li>The marketing team is enabled to send emails and create improved content offers</li> \n <li>The sales team is enabled and empowered to source quality leads</li> \n <li>All parties have what they need and are communicating effectively during each step of the process</li> \n</ul> \n<h3 style=\"font-weight: bold;\">2. Figure out a measurable metric to determine the success of your strategy.</h3> \n<p>The next step in strategizing is to identify how the team would <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/service/customer-success-metrics\">measure the success</a> of the project. When you figure out a measurable metric, you'll be able to keep track of the strategy's success as your team works through the plan. The metric will remind your team of the goal you want to accomplish and what stakeholders want to see as a result of your plan.</p> \n<p>In this example, the team might conclude, \"Click-through rate and total number of clicks are how we want to measure the value that email marketing brings to the business. We will calculate the click-through rate by dividing the number of clicks in a month by the number of unique email recipient impressions in a month and multiply it by 100 for the percentage.\"</p> \n<h3 style=\"font-weight: bold;\">3. Define your goal(s) using the SMART format.</h3> \n<p>With your metrics identified, the next step in defining a marketing ops strategy is outlining significant <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/how-to-write-a-smart-goal-template\">SMART goals</a>. This format is important because it gives your team a better sense of direction and organization in strategy execution.</p> \n<p>An example of an effective SMART goal is, “We will increase total clicks from email by 25% in one year.” because it’s:</p> \n<ul> \n <li><strong>Specific</strong>: It’s not a broad goal; it’s focused on email marketing.</li> \n <li><strong>Measurable</strong>: It can be measured by a concrete metric (total clicks).</li> \n <li><strong>Attainable</strong>: It’s possible to see this level of change in the business.</li> \n <li><strong>Realistic</strong>: The team is capable of working toward 25% of improvement.</li> \n <li><strong>Time-bound</strong>: This goal has a set duration of one year.</li> \n</ul> \n<h3 style=\"font-weight: bold;\">4. If needed, communicate how colleagues can take part in refining your strategy.</h3> \n<p>With the goal and metrics identified, your next step is to outline what this change would mean for affected colleagues, such as the team members who create and distribute email marketing messages.</p> \n<p>The team might conclude that \"Marketers can expect an easier email guideline process, a more effective format, and to receive a form to offer input about how to make that happen.\"</p> \n<h3 style=\"font-weight: bold;\">5. Determine actionable steps in your plan that will help you reach your goals.</h3> \n<p>Determining actionable steps will help your marketing ops team figure out what needs to be done, identify the resources required to see success, and stay organized as they work through their tasks.</p> \n<p>A marketing ops professional will need to run these steps by the stakeholders who actually influence the plan. For instance, they would be communicating steps to reach the previously stated SMART goal like:</p> \n<ul> \n <li>Switching to a more efficient email technology provider.</li> \n <li>Ensuring that the data being used to measure these goals is clean and accurate.</li> \n <li>Enabling the marketing team to source more quality leads.</li> \n <li>Enabling the sales team with better templates or sales enablement resources.</li> \n</ul> \n<p>With these steps communicated, stakeholders can provide assistance or suggestions where it’s needed, and the marketing ops team can get closer to execution.</p> \n<h3 style=\"font-weight: bold;\">6. Assign team members to specific tasks that will contribute to the completion of your goals.</h3> \n<p>Having that set in place, what's next for the marketing ops team is to assign team members specific tasks to help them achieve their goals. For instance, one team member might be in charge of redefining email marketing contact lists. Another might be in charge of auditing the current workflows in place for email marketing.</p> \n<p>As team members complete these tasks, they would check them off in a centralized space so the entire team can stay updated on the project’s status.</p> \n<p>Marketing operations teams are equally effective with their strategies and management capabilities as Summer's character in \"School of Rock.\" With her processes, the group was able to obtain their own rehearsal space and offer music classes.</p> \n<h2>Align and Optimize Your Marketing Operations</h2> \n<p>Marketing ops can come up with ways to increase customer satisfaction and ease the job of marketers. Their strategies make marketing activities and duties accessible to all, and because of that, are an essential part of a business.</p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=2f598dfb-38e3-4e7b-a962-57cf6aebd7d7&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; \">","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Wed, 09 Mar 2022 12:00:00 +0000","feedId":54,"bgimg":"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/34155d81-37a6-4910-a596-3a77b9e5a99f.png","linkMd5":"0aa7014dbe6c5f0e4050c8dfa3994b13","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn79@2020_4/2022/03/14/08-15-05-697_d4993499845f294a.webp","destWidth":492,"destHeight":59,"sourceBytes":5749,"destBytes":7772,"author":"Kayla Carmicheal","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/34155d81-37a6-4910-a596-3a77b9e5a99f.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn79@2020_4/2022/03/14/08-15-05-697_d4993499845f294a.webp","https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/Everything%20You%20Need%20to%20Know%20About%20Marketing%20Operations%20in%20One%20Place.png?width=624&height=624&name=Everything%20You%20Need%20to%20Know%20About%20Marketing%20Operations%20in%20One%20Place.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx29/cdn11@2020_2/2022/03/14/08-15-09-605_dce62d7bc9c727c2.webp","https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/2f598dfb-38e3-4e7b-a962-57cf6aebd7d7.png":null,"https://track.hubspot.com/__ptq.gif?a=53&k=14&r=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.hubspot.com%2Fmarketing%2Fmarketing-operations&bu=https%253A%252F%252Fblog.hubspot.com%252Fmarketing&bvt=rss":null},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1647245705115},{"createdTime":"2022-03-14 16:15:05","updatedTime":"2022-03-14 16:15:05","title":"What is a Media Mix & The Most Effective Types [HubSpot Blog Data]","link":"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/media-mix","description":"<p>I’m willing to bet that today, the typical campaign at any brand uses a media mix.</p>  \n<p>This refers to the process of using multiple channels to meet marketing goals. The question is, how exactly does it help brands better plan campaigns?</p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=a145a75e-59f6-4b51-a482-4f3ea486e740&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; margin: 0 auto; display: block; margin-top: 20px; margin-bottom: 20px\" alt=\"Free Resource: Content Marketing Planning Template\" src=\"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/a145a75e-59f6-4b51-a482-4f3ea486e740.png\" align=\"middle\"></a></p> \n<p>Let’s dive into how it works, review some stats, and see some brand examples.</p> \n<p></p> \n<p>A media mix is another term for an overview of the channels businesses choose to execute their marketing strategies on. Ultimately, media mix optimization is the process of analyzing the performance of those channels.</p> \n<p>Think about the last campaign you saw from one of your favorite brands. What did they do differently that really clicked with you? By incorporating a media mix into your yearly planning, you can narrow down what resonates with your audience.</p> \n<h2>Media Mix Example</h2> \n<p>To see how a media mix works for a campaign, let’s use makeup brand <a href=\"https://thelipbar.com/\">The Lip Bar</a>’s latest campaign: \"Something BAWSE is coming.\"</p> \n<p>To build anticipation around its latest product launch and celebrate its 10-year company anniversary, The Lip Bar launched a multi-channel campaign that reached audiences both online and offline.</p> \n<p>First up, website.</p> \n<p><img alt=\"media mix example showing makeup brand's campaign on their website\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/What%20is%20a%20Media%20Mix%20%26%20The%20Most%20Effective%20Types%20%5BHubSpot%20Blog%20Data%5D-1.jpeg?width=600&amp;name=What%20is%20a%20Media%20Mix%20%26%20The%20Most%20Effective%20Types%20%5BHubSpot%20Blog%20Data%5D-1.jpeg\" title=\"\" width=\"600\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block; width: 600px;\"></p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center; font-size: 12px;\"><a href=\"https://thelipbar.com/\">Image Source</a></p> \n<p>When you land on the brand’s homepage, you’ll see an image of the CEO with the following sentence \"Shark Tank said no, 12,000 5-star reviews later, 100% that bawse.\"</p> \n<p>Upon clicking on the image, you’ll arrive at a landing page that has a timeline of the brand. From launching in 2012, to opening its flagship store in 2019, then expanding to 1500+ stores in 2021. Once you get to 2022, you see the tagline \"Something Bawse is Coming.\"</p> \n<p>As you continue scrolling, you reach a section that offers a launch date and time for the brand’s newest product.</p> \n<p>The second digital channel the brand leveraged for this campaign is YouTube, publishing a 45-second video showing the CEO’s journey over the last 10 years.</p> \n<div class=\"hs-responsive-embed-wrapper hs-responsive-embed\" style=\"width: 100%; height: auto; position: relative; overflow: hidden; padding: 0; max-width: 853px; max-height: 480px; min-width: 256px; margin: 0px auto; display: block;\"> \n <div class=\"hs-responsive-embed-inner-wrapper\" style=\"position: relative; overflow: hidden; max-width: 100%; padding-bottom: 56.27%; margin: 0;\">\n  <iframe class=\"hs-responsive-embed-iframe\" style=\"position: absolute; top: 0; left: 0; width: 100%; height: 100%; border: none;\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/0BfxeqsaYLE\" width=\"853\" height=\"480\" frameborder=\"0\" allowfullscreen></iframe>\n </div> \n</div> \n<p>Moving offline, the brand also published billboards in five cities to continue the campaign.</p> \n<p>Note how the billboard didn’t use the tagline we saw on social media platforms.</p> \n<p><img alt=\"media mix example showing makeup brand's billboard campaign\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/What%20is%20a%20Media%20Mix%20%26%20The%20Most%20Effective%20Types%20%5BHubSpot%20Blog%20Data%5D.jpeg?width=600&amp;name=What%20is%20a%20Media%20Mix%20%26%20The%20Most%20Effective%20Types%20%5BHubSpot%20Blog%20Data%5D.jpeg\" title=\"\" width=\"600\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block; width: 600px;\"></p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center; font-size: 12px;\"><a href=\"https://www.instagram.com/p/CZwiA_ILpBj/\">Image Source</a></p> \n<p>The benefit of using a media mix is to leverage different strategies to see which tactics work and lead to better conversions.</p> \n<p>The Lip Bar’s latest campaign is a great example of how any brand can leverage channels differently to reach the same marketing goal.</p> \n<h2>Media Mix Stats in 2022</h2> \n<p>In January 2022, we surveyed over 600 <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/media-planning\">media planners</a> to discover their strategies, goals, and challenges. Here are some interesting findings:</p> \n<ul> \n <li>84% of media planners surveyed leverage a mix of organic and paid media.</li> \n <li>Email marketing is the most leveraged media channel, used by 1 in 2 media planners.</li> \n <li>41% of media planners surveyed will change their media mix in 2022, while 45% will keep it the same.</li> \n <li>14% of media planners currently leverage non-fungible tokens (NFTs) while 16% plan to use them for the first time in 2022.</li> \n <li>39% of those who use NFTs in their media planning say they have the best ROI of any channel in their media mix.</li> \n <li>39% of marketers surveyed say determining the most effective media mix is the biggest challenge of media planning.</li> \n</ul> \n<h2>Media Mix Optimization</h2> \n<p>Media mix optimization provides businesses with an understanding of how their messages are coming across to customers. It allows a brand to invest more time and money into marketing strategies that are best suited for their audiences.</p> \n<p>Marketers might consider optimizing their media mix if they want to gain some helpful insight into what time and capital is needed to target their audience in a way that gives customers a personalized experience.</p> \n<p>But, while media mix optimization is a powerful opportunity for methodizing data collection online, it's not the best strategy for marketers who employ a lot of traditional marketing techniques, since you can't really measure the success of a billboard or newspaper ad.</p> \n<p>However, to make guided decisions such as what font to use in creative design, when to publish social media posts on various channels, or where to invest resources, this method can be helpful.</p> \n<p>Optimizing a media mix means looking at the analytics and ROI of various marketing strategies. This can be anything from engagement data of social media platforms to views on the newest commercial.</p> \n<p>That's where media mix modeling comes in. If media mix optimization is the \"what,\" modeling is the \"how.\" Every model can (and should) look different, depending on your marketing and broader business goal.</p> \n<p></p> \n<p>Media mix models can be used to analyze the relationship between a dependent variable and an independent variable.</p> \n<p>For instance, let's say a business has a question like, \"How did paying for a sponsored tweet affect overall blog traffic?\" The business's media mix model should then accurately depict how a dependent variable – like overall blog traffic – relates to an independent variable, such as investing in Twitter.</p> \n<p>For businesses still deciding if a media mix optimization is a good idea for them, we've put together key tips to guide you when creating a media mix model. Let's explore those, next.</p> \n<h2>Tips for Optimizing Your Media Mix</h2> \n<h3>1. Collect personal level data.</h3> \n<p>The goal here is to find and focus on analytics that will help provide an accurate picture of how customers engage with your media mix.</p> \n<p>Analytics software is expansive and offers an array of tools for use. If you're in the market for one, the <a href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/products/marketing\">HubSpot Marketing Hub</a> is a great place to go.</p> \n<p>Having too many metrics can be confusing and lead to inaccurate data. The best plan is to have an idea of which metrics need to be tracked so they can be right at the beginning.</p> \n<p>A normal media mix optimization process can take anywhere from a few months to a year. So, collecting the right information at the beginning contributes to getting the most accurate information overall.</p> \n<h3>2. Have a robust reporting process.</h3> \n<p>When using a media mix, you often combine online and offline strategies. With this in mind, it can be more difficult to measure the impact of a billboard compared to a paid social ad.</p> \n<p>That means you’ll have to think outside of the box when evaluating your media mix. For instance, while an online ad will have clear conversion rates you can find, a billboard may require some creative tracking.</p> \n<p>Perhaps, you can track the uptick in branded search volume or improved brand recall.</p> \n<p>This requires having a robust reporting process that accounts for the events you’ll be tracking – both online and offline.</p> \n<h3>3. Choose the right platform.</h3> \n<p>Marketing teams that use CMS or analytics software are already ahead of the game. Software like this is essential to optimizing a media mix because it can give you numbers that would otherwise take some time to figure out manually.</p> \n<p>A brand can analyze its media mix with the use of platforms that collect engagement data in real-time and compile that data into tracking reports.</p> \n<p>Look for a platform that can give a holistic view of results across the board, so results will maintain consistency. It's also good to choose software that specializes in the marketing channels being used at the time.</p> \n<p>Because optimizing is measuring a lot of different data at once, stick to as few systems as possible.</p> \n<p>For businesses that are in the market for a CMS,<a href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/products/marketing/content-management-system?_ga=2.32061246.1093091538.1581343599-940436819.1565181751\"> </a><a href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/products/marketing/content-management-system?_ga=2.32061246.1093091538.1581343599-940436819.1565181751\">HubSpot offers tools</a> that are easy to use for brands of any size.</p> \n<h3>4. Analyze the data.</h3> \n<p>We've been talking a lot about the kind of data and analyzing that needs to be done in a media mix optimization, but another important factor is being able to interpret and understand that data.</p> \n<p>It's no secret that in the marketing world, there is an abundance of processes and acronyms floating around. While first getting into the groove of understanding them and what they mean can be intimidating, it's important to know the data being collected and how to use it to your advantage.</p> \n<p>For instance, if a marketing team had especially high click-to-open rates for weekly newsletters, that's useful information to infer that the next campaign could benefit greatly from an email-marketing rollout. Alternatively, if a marketing team has no idea what a click-to-open rate is, those numbers aren't going to be helpful — just a little confusing.</p> \n<p>Reading data to understand its usefulness is just as important as collecting it.</p> \n<h3>5. Consider public perception.</h3> \n<p>Knowing how the public perceives your brand can help fill in some interpretation gaps during the modeling process. In the media mix model, think about how to fit in customer opinion. That way, the numbers will have some customer opinions to define them.</p> \n<p>There are a couple of ways to do this.</p> \n<p>To better understand your brand perception, monitor your brand mentions on social media. Take note of the positives, the negatives, and the questions. You can also create a survey to know how your customers feel about your company and its services and use a net promoter score.</p> \n<p>An NPS asks customers how likely they are to recommend a business to a friend. Knowing this will aid in figuring out how a business fares among the competition in the market. It will also assist in future marketing endeavors.</p> \n<p>For instance, if customers fill out your survey and ask for more personalized Instagram stories, your team could take that knowledge and include it in your next campaign.</p> \n<p>This method ultimately gives the media mix optimization reigns to the customer.</p> \n<p>Media mix optimization can help your marketing team figure out which distribution channels will best promote an upcoming campaign, and can ultimately help strengthen your marketing strategy as a whole.</p> \n<p><em>Editor's Note: This post was originally published in Feb. 2020 and has been updated for comprehensiveness. </em></p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" Carmicheal","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/a145a75e-59f6-4b51-a482-4f3ea486e740.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn84@2020_3/2022/03/14/08-15-05-896_f8c910eb1e0201f6.webp","https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/What%20is%20a%20Media%20Mix%20%26%20The%20Most%20Effective%20Types%20%5BHubSpot%20Blog%20Data%5D-1.jpeg?width=600&name=What%20is%20a%20Media%20Mix%20%26%20The%20Most%20Effective%20Types%20%5BHubSpot%20Blog%20Data%5D-1.jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx5oss/cdn6@2020_6/2022/03/14/08-15-11-092_f224b3a7c8b4a7c9.webp","https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/What%20is%20a%20Media%20Mix%20%26%20The%20Most%20Effective%20Types%20%5BHubSpot%20Blog%20Data%5D.jpeg?width=600&name=What%20is%20a%20Media%20Mix%20%26%20The%20Most%20Effective%20Types%20%5BHubSpot%20Blog%20Data%5D.jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn2@2020_1/2022/03/14/08-15-15-518_9d0ddf4316cdfe18.webp","https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/dc23c777-516f-4c62-b371-70b180c87a3e.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx19/cdn24@2020_5/2022/03/14/08-15-12-685_d198dce450120884.webp","https://track.hubspot.com/__ptq.gif?a=53&k=14&r=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.hubspot.com%2Fmarketing%2Fmedia-mix&bu=https%253A%252F%252Fblog.hubspot.com%252Fmarketing&bvt=rss":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx19/cdn72@2020_1/2022/03/14/08-15-14-644_e7ff58d00b36a57b.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1647245705033},{"createdTime":"2022-03-14 16:15:05","updatedTime":"2022-03-14 16:15:05","title":"How Market Intelligence Will Make Your Marketing Team More Agile","link":"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/market-intelligence","description":"<p>When I was younger, my dream was to open a cheese store with my family. My mom, brother, sister, and I — we're all obsessed with cheese.</p>  \n<p>So anytime I see a cheese store, I'll go in and sample everything … for research, obviously.</p> \n<p>Although I'd never thought about it this way before, I was already thinking in terms of market intelligence and market research (two different concepts, but more on that below).</p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=6ba52ce7-bb69-4b63-965b-4ea21ba905da&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; margin: 0 auto; display: block; margin-top: 20px; margin-bottom: 20px\" alt=\"→ Download Now: Market Research Templates [Free Kit]\" src=\"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/6ba52ce7-bb69-4b63-965b-4ea21ba905da.png\" align=\"middle\"></a></p> \n<p>I was thinking about the product and its competitors.</p> \n<p>As a marketer, market intelligence is important because it can help you understand your position in the market, evaluate your product, know your target audience, and conduct competitive analysis.</p> \n<p>With this information, your marketing team will be better equipped to position your company in the marketplace. For companies that prioritize intelligence data, decision-making can be <a href=\"https://techjury.net/blog/business-intelligence-statistics/#gref\">five times faster</a>.</p> \n<p>Feeling hesitant to rely on intelligence data? <a href=\"https://www.gartner.com/smarterwithgartner/gartner-top-10-trends-in-data-and-analytics-for-2020\">Gartner reports</a> over one-third of organizations will rely on decision intelligence by 2023, making data intelligence a must for remaining competitive.</p> \n<p>Below, let's review what market intelligence is, how it's different from market research, and the intel tools that can facilitate the process.</p> \n<p>Market intelligence is used to learn about the existing market, customers, problems, <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/competitive-intelligence-competitive-advantage\">competition</a>, and growth potential. Businesses can gather this information through internal and external sources such as sales logs, surveys, social media, news websites, manufacturers, clients, or distributors.</p> \n<p>For instance, companies can gather general demographics and spending habits of their consumers to write better, more targeted <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/social-media-marketing?_ga=2.89808924.622785003.1614973949-456434430.1614973949\">social media ads</a>. Additionally, market intelligence can help a company make decisions on product development and establish a stronger brand.</p> \n<h2>How to Gather Market Intelligence</h2> \n<p>So, what type of information should you collect? Generally, market intelligence can be divided into four main categories of information:</p> \n<h3>Competitor Intelligence</h3> \n<p>This is the process of <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/competitive-intelligence-competitive-advantage\">learning more about your competitors</a>. To do this, you might conduct a <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/swot-analysis\">SWOT analysis</a>, so you can look at the competition's strengths and weaknesses. The goal is to uncover why customers would choose competitors over your product or service.</p> \n<h3>Product Intelligence</h3> \n<p>Once you've analyzed how you compare to your competitors, look inward at your own product or service. The goal is to learn about its quality and performance and identify opportunities for improvement.</p> \n<p>If you have a physical product, you should also analyze your manufacturing process. Are you building your product in the most efficient way? This information should help you improve the user experience and improve your product.</p> \n<h3>Market Understanding</h3> \n<p>To truly understand how your product is performing, you'll have to look at the various markets where it's available. Could you <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/market-development-strategy\">expand your product </a>to other markets? Are there other markets that could benefit from your product or service?</p> \n<p>Ultimately, this information should help you understand where your audience is and what gaps exist, so you can fill them.</p> \n<h3>Customer Understanding</h3> \n<p>Understanding your customer helps to increase your product or service life cycle. That's because it's usually more expensive to gain a new customer than to keep an existing one.<a href=\"https://www.invespcro.com/blog/customer-acquisition-retention/\"></a></p> \n<p>For this reason — and many others — you have to know your audience. Why do your customers buy from you? What challenges do you help them resolve? The goal here is to gather the information that can help your marketing team come up with targeted campaigns.</p> \n<p>Overall, gathering market intelligence should answer questions like:</p> \n<ul> \n <li>Where should we devote more resources?</li> \n <li>What markets can we enter next?</li> \n <li>What are our customers purchasing patterns?</li> \n <li>What audiences should we market to?</li> \n</ul> \n<p>Now, you might be wondering, <em>\"How do I gather this information?\"</em></p> \n<p>To conduct market intelligence, you'll use internal and external sources of data, such as:</p> \n<ul> \n <li>Surveys</li> \n <li>Polls</li> \n <li>Forms</li> \n <li>Focus groups</li> \n <li>Interviews</li> \n <li>Observation</li> \n <li>A/B tests</li> \n <li>Competitor tracking analytics</li> \n</ul> \n<p>Depending on the analytics you have available, a lot of this information can be found on your <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/7969/what-is-a-cms-and-why-should-you-care.aspx\">content management system </a>(CMS) or <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/sales/how-to-use-crm\">customer relationship management </a>(CRM).</p> \n<p>However, before we jump into the software you can use to find this information, I know you're probably thinking, <em>\"How is this different from market research?\" </em>Let's dive into that below.</p> \n<p>Alternatively to market intelligence, market research focuses on learning more about the buyer's research process and what influences their buying decisions.</p> \n<h2>Example of Market Intelligence</h2> \n<p>Let’s walk through an example of how a fictional company could use market intelligence to create a competitive advantage.</p> \n<p>JKL Podcasting Co offers online software podcasters can use to record, edit, and distribute their podcast to major streaming platforms. As marketers at JKL look to expand the company’s user base, they performed an in-depth analysis of the market for podcast recording software.</p> \n<p>In this analysis, they covered four areas:</p> \n<ol> \n <li>Competitor landscape — They identified the top-ranking podcast recording software companies to understand their product features, pricing model, sales funnel, marketing tactics, and customer demographics.</li> \n <li>Product — After gathering competitor information, they worked with their product team to gain a deep understanding of their own product including key features, how it was like competitor products, and what differentiated it from competitor products. They also learned about up-and-coming features launching later in the year.</li> \n <li>Market analysis — Next, the team did research to understand the overall valuation and growth potential of the podcast recording software market. They learned podcast listenership has <a href=\"https://www.insiderintelligence.com/insights/the-podcast-industry-report-statistics/\"><span>grown over the past decade</span></a> and is expected to grow more in coming years, which could lead to more podcasts being produced. With seeing growth and investment in the podcasting space, along with increased interest in people wanting to start podcasts, marketers at JKL learn there is a potential market for new, or up-and-coming podcasters who want easy-to-use software.</li> \n <li>Customer base — Finally, the JKL marketing team reached out to a focus group of their current customers to understand their relationship to the product. The customers walk them through their podcast production workflow using JKL software and share what features they love, along with what new features or changes they would like to see.</li> \n</ol> \n<p>After going through this exercise, JKL has gained valuable insight into their competitive landscape, product features to highlight, market growth opportunities, and ways to keep their current customer base engaged and using the platform.</p> \n<p>You're probably wondering, <em>\"How do I gather this information?\" </em>Below, let's review what tools and software you can use.</p> \n<h2>Market Intelligence Tools</h2> \n<p>For market intelligence to be useful, companies need to conduct research and sort through their collected data for analysis. A lot of this can be done through your <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/sales/how-to-use-crm\">CRM software</a>.</p> \n<p>To start, many CRMs allow you to create competitor profiles in which you will track your competitors' products, price points, organizational updates, social media activity, and more.</p> \n<p>You'll likely also find <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/sales/battle-cards\">battle card templates </a>in your CRM, making it easy for your sales reps to access the information they need during their calls to combat objections and persuade prospects.</p> \n<p>In addition, you can conduct regular <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/sales/questions-to-ask-win-loss-review\">win/loss analysis </a>with your sales team to determine strengths and weaknesses in your sales and/or marketing strategy. You'll want to know:</p> \n<ul> \n <li>What factors are contributing to your wins and losses?</li> \n <li>What other company was the prospect considering for the sale? Why?</li> \n <li>Which competitors are you beating and which ones you are losing to?</li> \n</ul> \n<p>If you don't already have a CRM, there are many out there that cater to businesses ranging from small to enterprise-level. Pricing is usually structured on a monthly basis and can range anywhere from $20/month to $1200+.</p> \n<p>If your team would rather focus on specific tools, there are several online options to help you achieve your goals. Below are a few we recommend, divided into sections depending on your goals. Additionally, if you're a HubSpot user, many of these tools integrate with <a href=\"https://ecosystem.hubspot.com/marketplace/apps/all-categories?eco_search=market%20intelligence\"></a><a href=\"https://ecosystem.hubspot.com/marketplace/apps/all-categories?eco_search=market%20intelligence\">HubSpot</a>.</p> \n<h3>Competitor Intelligence</h3> \n<h4>1. <a href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/products/marketing\">HubSpot's Marketing Hub</a></h4> \n<img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/HubSpot-homepage.jpg?width=600&amp;name=HubSpot-homepage.jpg\" alt=\"Market-Intelligence-Marketing-Hub\" width=\"600\" style=\"width: 600px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\"> \n<p style=\"text-align: center; font-size: 12px;\"><a href=\"http://Hubspot.com\">Image Source</a></p> \n<p>HubSpot's Marketing Hub has extensive tools to help marketing teams manage, track and scale their efforts. The platform offers both free and premium subscription plans ranging from $45 to $3,200 a month.</p> \n<h4>2. <a href=\"https://www.crayon.co/\">Crayon</a></h4> \n<p><img alt=\"Market-Intelligence-Crayon-Homepage\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/%5BUpdate%5D%20How%20Market%20Intelligence%20Will%20Make%20Your%20Marketing%20Team%20More%20Agile.jpeg?width=600&amp;name=%5BUpdate%5D%20How%20Market%20Intelligence%20Will%20Make%20Your%20Marketing%20Team%20More%20Agile.jpeg\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block; width: 600px;\" title=\"\" width=\"600\"></p> \n<p style=\"font-size: 12px; text-align: center;\"><a href=\"http://Crayon.co\">Image Source</a></p> \n<p>Crayon is one of the leading competitive intelligence (CI) tools in the industry. Its software can fetch and categorize data from over 300 million sources.</p> \n<p>The platform also makes it easy for sales and marketing teams to find the intel they need, through battle cards, email digests, and a centralized dashboard.</p> \n<p>For pricing information, you must contact the company.</p> \n<h4>3. <a href=\"https://www.semrush.com/\">SEMrush</a></h4> \n<p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/SEMrush-homepage.jpg?width=600&amp;name=SEMrush-homepage.jpg\" alt=\"Market-Intelligence-SEMrush-homepage\" width=\"600\" style=\"width: 600px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\"></p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><span style=\"font-size: 12px;\"><a href=\"http://Semrush.com\">Image Source</a></span></p> \n<p>If you want to track your competitors' SEO performance, SEMrush is a great place to start. The platform has extensive tools, including keyword research, domain overview, and keyword difficulty. This will give you more insight into your competitors' strategies and how their efforts are performing.</p> \n<p>Similar to HubSpot, SEMrush offers a free version of its platform. It also offers premium subscription plans ranging from $119 to $449 a month.</p> \n<h3>Product Intelligence</h3> \n<h4>1. <a href=\"https://ecosystem.hubspot.com/marketplace/apps/customer-success/survey/surveymonkey\">SurveyMonkey</a></h4> \n<p><img alt=\"Market intelligence Survey Monkey homepage\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/%5BUpdate%5D%20How%20Market%20Intelligence%20Will%20Make%20Your%20Marketing%20Team%20More%20Agile-1.jpeg?width=600&amp;name=%5BUpdate%5D%20How%20Market%20Intelligence%20Will%20Make%20Your%20Marketing%20Team%20More%20Agile-1.jpeg\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block; width: 600px;\" title=\"\" width=\"600\"></p> \n<p style=\"font-size: 12px; text-align: center;\"><a href=\"https://www.surveymonkey.com/\">Image Source</a></p> \n<p>Surveys are one of the best ways to learn more about how customers are responding to your products. Survey Monkey allows you to customize your survey to get the insights you need. Beyond a wide range of survey features like advanced survey logic and pagination, the platform also has tools to promote team collaboration.</p> \n<p>Access to <a href=\"https://www.surveymonkey.com/\">Survey Monkey </a>starts at no cost, but their premium versions begin at $25/month.</p> \n<h4>2. <a href=\"https://inmoment.com/\"><span>InMoment</span></a></h4> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><img src=\"https://lh6.googleusercontent.com/VEBz4QjG_mC2Cy0dKSXRQu1VDeAMlGvQkOByf1L9GfyjXDLJMjKfLW44cfEnj4P0_1Fezf7r1dmxVPME7qYH-A9QSX0Y-4uEl1hsmbrZ2OUCv57pRqTFHIF_BKWeNnvrKNG0-nFY\" width=\"624\" height=\"373\"></p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center; font-size: 12px;\"><a href=\"https://inmoment.com/roles/market-research-insights/\"><span>Image Source</span></a></p> \n<p>InMoment, formerly Wootric, an analytics platform that helps you learn more about customer sentiment. You can gather real-time analytics, which arms your team to make decisions quickly.</p> \n<p>The platform also has many integrations for easy team collaboration, including <a href=\"https://slack.com/\">Slack</a>, <a href=\"https://zapier.com/\">Zapier</a>, and <a href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/\">HubSpot</a>.</p> \n<p>For pricing details, you must contact the company.</p> \n<h4>3. <a href=\"https://ecosystem.hubspot.com/marketplace/apps/marketing/marketing-automation/metadata\">Metadata</a></h4> \n<img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Metadata.io-homepage.jpg?width=600&amp;name=Metadata.io-homepage.jpg\" alt=\"Metadata.io Homepage\" width=\"600\" style=\"width: 600px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\"> \n<p style=\"font-size: 12px; text-align: center;\"><a href=\"http://metadata.io\">Image Source</a></p> \n<p><a href=\"http://metadata.io\">Metadata </a>is a SaaS company that helps B2B brands generate demand for their products and/or services. On the platform, you can identify audiences, conduct experiments, and track the full sales journey.</p> \n<p>Pricing starts at $3,950 for growing companies, with custom plans available for enterprise-level businesses.</p> \n<h3>Customer Understanding</h3> \n<h4>1. <a href=\"https://www.google.com/forms/about/\">Google Forms</a></h4> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google-Forms.jpg?width=600&amp;name=Google-Forms.jpg\" alt=\"Google Forms homepage\" width=\"600\" style=\"width: 600px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\"><span style=\"font-size: 12px;\"><a href=\"https://www.google.com/forms/about/\">Image Source</a></span></p> \n<p>The stand-out feature on Google Forms is the simple and easy-to-use interface. In just a few minutes, you can have a survey ready to send out to your audience to collect data. You can receive alerts every time someone answers your survey and add collaborators.</p> \n<p>The best part? It's free for individuals and included in your plan if you have a Google Business account.</p> \n<h4>2. <a href=\"https://ecosystem.hubspot.com/marketplace/apps/marketing/marketing-automation/calltrackingmetrics\">CallTrackingMetrics</a></h4> \n<p><img alt=\"CallTrackingMetrics homepage\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/%5BUpdate%5D%20How%20Market%20Intelligence%20Will%20Make%20Your%20Marketing%20Team%20More%20Agile-3.jpeg?width=600&amp;name=%5BUpdate%5D%20How%20Market%20Intelligence%20Will%20Make%20Your%20Marketing%20Team%20More%20Agile-3.jpeg\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block; width: 600px;\" title=\"\" width=\"600\"></p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><span style=\"font-size: 12px;\"><a href=\"https://www.calltrackingmetrics.com/\">Image Source</a></span></p> \n<p>Too often, there's a disconnect between sales and marketing teams – <a href=\"https://www.calltrackingmetrics.com/\">CallTrackingMetrics </a>helps solve that. The platform offers a robust analytics tool that can identify which marketing campaigns are driving conversions, automate call processes for smoother interactions, and provide analytics — all in one place.</p> \n<p>Pricing ranges from $39/month to $299/month, with custom plans available.</p> \n<h4>3. <a href=\"https://analytics.google.com/\">Google Analytics</a></h4> \n<img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google-Analytics-homepage.jpg?width=600&amp;name=Google-Analytics-homepage.jpg\" alt=\"Google Analytics homepage\" width=\"600\" style=\"width: 600px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\"> \n<p style=\"text-align: center; font-size: 12px;\"><a href=\"http://analytics.google.com/\">Image Source</a></p> \n<p>Google Analytics is a website analytics tool with powerful reporting capabilities to understand how users are behaving on your site. It's a great software for brands that are already using other Google products, such as Google Ads or Google Business, as they work together seamlessly.</p> \n<p>On the platform, you can get detailed reports by goal: acquisition, retention, engagement, and monetization. The visual dashboard also allows you to get a snapshot of your site is performing.</p> \n<p>The standard version is free and ideal for small to medium-sized companies. Entreprise-level businesses must contact sales for pricing.</p> \n<h2>How To Leverage Market Intelligence Data</h2> \n<p>Once you start collecting data, unpacking it is the next step.</p> \n<p>But before you dive in head-first, come back to your goal. What do you want to learn and why? Use that to steer your approach.</p> \n<p>Having a clear direction is essential during this stage to narrow down what data to focus on. You'll be compiling a lot of data, and not all of it will be relevant to your main objective. Knowing which will be most impactful will save you so much time and allow you to use your resources efficiently.</p> \n<p>Now that you know what to focus on, start organizing and reviewing your data. You'll want to look for patterns. During this step, keep an open mind. Confirmation bias (the tendency to interpret information to support a pre-existing idea or belief) can greatly impact how you interpret data, so it's important to consider all perspectives.</p> \n<p>Once you identify a theme or trend, dive deeper to answer the 5Ws. <strong>When </strong>did it start? <strong>Who </strong>or <strong>what </strong>is influencing this? <strong>Why </strong>is it happening? <strong>Where </strong>else is this trend identified?</p> \n<p>From there, it's time to strategize. Based on what your data is telling you, you can develop an action plan and make recommendations to key stakeholders.</p> \n<p>For instance, let's say your latest intel revealed that consumers are unaware of a key feature in your product line, which is steering them toward your competitors. Your recommendation could be to launch a marketing campaign that highlights that feature, create stronger messaging on your website product pages, and adjust the sales team's scripts to place more emphasis on this feature and how it's better suited for your customers than a competitor's.</p> \n<p>The formula is easy: collect, organize, identify, and recommend. Understanding your market is key to entering the market and maintaining your place in it. But if you want to stand out among your competition, you'll need to leverage market intel.</p> \n<p>Market intelligence can give you a holistic view of the market, improve customer retention, boost your efficiency, and give you a competitive advantage. So, I'm not being hyperbolic when I say market intelligence is vital for your company to succeed.</p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\"
