d%20on%20Another%20Cell%20Range%20step%205-jpg.jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn60@2020_6/2022/03/14/08-15-10-446_d33e7d15bdf4d6ae.webp","https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20to%20Set%20Conditional%20Formatting%20Based%20on%20Another%20Cell%20in%20Google%20Sheets-1.jpeg?width=600&name=How%20to%20Set%20Conditional%20Formatting%20Based%20on%20Another%20Cell%20in%20Google%20Sheets-1.jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn36@2020_2/2022/03/14/08-15-09-626_402ee58d2eb69843.webp","https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/How%20to%20Set%20Conditional%20Formatting%20Based%20on%20Another%20Cell%20in%20Google%20Sheets-2.png?width=200&name=How%20to%20Set%20Conditional%20Formatting%20Based%20on%20Another%20Cell%20in%20Google%20Sheets-2.png":null,"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/0cedc81d-d358-4517-bd55-4a26f49c5a4e.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx8/cdn31@2020_4/2022/03/14/08-15-09-864_9fb0d0da7b424675.webp","https://track.hubspot.com/__ptq.gif?a=53&k=14&r=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.hubspot.com%2Fmarketing%2Fconditional-formatting-google-sheets&bu=https%253A%252F%252Fblog.hubspot.com%252Fmarketing&bvt=rss":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn28@2020_2/2022/03/14/08-15-12-469_acb658ea0689b868.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1647245705029},{"createdTime":"2022-03-14 16:15:05","updatedTime":"2022-03-14 16:15:05","title":"Everything You Need to Know About Brand Experience","link":"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/brand-experience","description":"<p>Online sales are reaching all-time highs as buyers become more comfortable with digital transactions — in 2021, for example, consumers spent a collective <a href=\"https://www.forbes.com/sites/shelleykohan/2021/11/27/online-sales-for-thanksgiving-and-black-friday-reach-14-billion/\">$14 billion online</a> across Black Friday and Cyber Monday.</p> \n<p>For businesses, the shift to online-first purchasing offers substantive potential, but also underpins prospective problems: As the number of digital product offerings ramps up, competition for customer conversions is also on the rise.</p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=814dd420-0d49-40e0-b59c-f01066e186c1&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; margin: 0 auto; display: block; margin-top: 20px; margin-bottom: 20px\" alt=\"Download Now: Free Brand Building Guide\" src=\"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/814dd420-0d49-40e0-b59c-f01066e186c1.png\" align=\"middle\"></a></p> \n<p>The result? A battlefield for brand experience. If companies can create a lasting positive impression among potential customers, they can drive sales and set the stage for long-term loyalty. But what exactly is brand experience? What does effective design require and what does it look like in practice? Most importantly, how do brands create experience strategies that deliver reliable results over time?</p> \n<p></p> \n<p>Brand experience describes the tangible and emotional experience consumers have while interacting with your brand. Think of it as a holistic approach that combines elements of user experience, customer experience, and <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/agency/develop-brand-identity\">brand identity</a> all in one.</p> \n<p>Brand experience encompasses all the feelings consumers have before, during, and after interacting with your brand. Take <a href=\"https://www.nestle.com/brands/allbrands/toll-house\">Nestlé Toll House</a> for example. When most people think of them, they think of cookies. You may even remember baking cookies using Toll House chocolate chips, the smell as they baked, and finally, savoring every last bite. You may even associate the brand with moments of bonding with family as you baked cookies together.</p> \n<p>In this case, the Toll House brand experience has moved beyond just the consumption of chocolate chips. It’s an emotional connection built over time with consumers and how their products integrate into the lives of the people who buy them.</p> \n<p>While brand experience is similar to user experience, it encompasses a broader perception of your brand at large. Where user experience speaks to the takeaways — positive or negative — of a user when they interact with your website or social media profiles, brand experience refers to the impression of your brand as a whole. Not surprisingly, positive user experiences inform better brand experiences (and vice versa) but the two are distinct concepts.</p> \n<p>It’s also important to understand that brand experience is subjective. While it’s possible to create experiences that produce reactions along a generalized spectrum, individual users will have different reactions to your efforts. In practice, this means that no matter how carefully you curate brand experience efforts, there will always be customers who come away with a negative reaction. As a result, the goal isn’t to create a universal experience but rather to create one that resonates positively with the largest number of target customers.</p> \n<h2>Breaking Down Brand Experience Design</h2> \n<p>Just <a href=\"https://www.forbes.com/sites/sap/2021/04/26/brand-experience-what-does-it-mean-and-how-can-it-be-your-differentiator/\">39%</a> of business decision-makers say their brand effectively resonates with prospective buyers. This is a problem: If customers don’t connect your brand with positive thoughts, feelings, and reactions, they’re less likely to remember your products and services when it comes time to make a purchase.</p> \n<p>Worth noting? Neutrality isn’t enough. While negative impressions of your brand can drive customers away from your site, neutral impressions are just as problematic — even if consumers see your brand listed in search engine results or advertised online, the absence of a positive brand impression means they won’t seek you out over companies that offer better connective messaging.</p> \n<p>So what does effective brand experience design look like? Four components are critical:</p> \n<p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Everything%20You%20Need%20to%20Know%20about%20Brand%20Experience.jpg?width=650&amp;name=Everything%20You%20Need%20to%20Know%20about%20Brand%20Experience.jpg\" alt=\"Brand Experience vs. Customer Experience\" width=\"650\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block; width: 650px;\"></p> \n<h3>Perception</h3> \n<p>Perception forms a key part of the experience. This includes audio, visual, and tactical interactions that allow customers to connect a specific sense to advertising campaigns. In much the same way that particular smells can bring back memories of childhood experiences, brands that successfully merge senses with marketing can create connections that drive sales.</p> \n<h3>Participation</h3> \n<p>It’s also more likely that customers will walk away with a positive brand experience if they’re able to participate in some way rather than simply watch. This might include the ability to submit suggestions online or interact in real-time online question forums, or it could feature the use of physical installations that allow consumers to touch your product or provide direct feedback.</p> \n<h3>Personalization</h3> \n<p>Generic marketing campaigns can produce steady returns, but personalization can help encourage connection across different customer segments. By leveraging both user-provided data (with their consent) along with social media interactions and other engagement data, it’s possible to create more personalized efforts that help create connections between consumer needs and current product offerings.</p> \n<h3>Prioritization</h3> \n<p>Brand experience can’t be all things to all people. Attempts to capture every consumer in every circumstance actually undermine experience-driven efforts — as a result, it’s worth selecting specific brand metrics such as positive social mentions or repeat purchases to prioritize.</p> \n<h2>Creating a Brand Experience Strategy</h2> \n<p>So how do you build an effective brand experience strategy?</p> \n<h3>1. Assess whether or not you’re meeting customer expectations.</h3> \n<p>First up is identifying areas where your current experience isn’t meeting customer expectations. Social media interactions and customer service calls can help pinpoint potential problems — if consistent concerns around brand interaction or reaction arise, this can help frame the foundation of brand experience strategy.</p> \n<h3>2. Identify areas for improvement.</h3> \n<p>Next is targeting an area for improvement. While there may be more than one aspect of brand experience that could use a refresh or redesign, attempting to do everything at once can spread strategy efforts too thin and deliver less-than-ideal results. For example, you might choose to increase positive social mentions across specific channels such as Facebook or Instagram. While the eventual goal could be a larger social impact from initial contact to eventual conversion, easily-accessible social platforms provide an ideal starting point.</p> \n<h3>3. Measure your results.</h3> \n<p>Effective measurement follows to ensure efforts are bearing fruit. In the case of our social media example above, this means tracking user views, reactions, and responses to social media posts along with the sentiment — positive, negative, or neutral — that goes along with them. This is also the time to explore and innovate by testing multiple strategies to see which one sticks. From video campaigns to personalized storytelling to marketing efforts all designed to elicit specific emotions, it’s worth finding that resonates with your customer base and then fine-tuning your efforts to deliver ideal outcomes.</p> \n<p></p> \n<p>It’s one thing to talk about brand experience building, but it’s another to see it in action. Here’s a look at five brand experiences efforts that offer effective in-practice examples.</p> \n<h3>1. <a href=\"https://www.apple.com/\">Apple</a></h3> \n<a class=\"hs-embed-content-wrapper\"></a>\n<a style=\"position: relative; overflow: hidden; max-width: 100%; padding-bottom: 56.5%; margin: 0px;\"> \n <div class=\"hs-responsive-embed-wrapper hs-responsive-embed\" style=\"position: relative; top: 0px; left: 0px; width: 100%; height: auto; border: none; overflow: hidden; padding: 0; max-width: 650px; max-height: 367px; min-width: 256px; margin: 0px auto; display: block;\"> \n  <div class=\"hs-responsive-embed-inner-wrapper\" style=\"position: relative; overflow: hidden; max-width: 100%; padding-bottom: 56.46%; margin: 0;\">\n   <iframe class=\"hs-responsive-embed-iframe\" style=\"position: absolute; top: 0; left: 0; width: 100%; height: 100%; border: none;\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/pJIKPzZTJXM?feature=oembed\" width=\"650\" height=\"367\" frameborder=\"0\" allowfullscreen></iframe>\n  </div> \n </div> </a> \n<p>One of the reasons Apple has such a devoted customer base is because of the brand experience they’ve created. From ads to Apple stores to the packaging of their products — all touch points work together to create a cohesive brand experience that highlights innovation, style, and functionality.</p> \n<p>Their products are cool, sleek, and user-friendly, all attributes highly coveted by Apple’s fans. Even their product announcements have become anticipated events. Apple is a pro at conquering the four \"Ps\" of brand experience (perception, participation, personalization, and prioritization) and incorporating them in all messaging. This helps Apple stay top of mind for consumers whether they’re in the market to buy or not. It’s not a smart phone, it’s an iPhone. It’s not a laptop, it’s a MacBook.</p> \n<h3>2. <a href=\"https://youtu.be/FHtvDA0W34I\">Red Bull</a></h3> \n<div class=\"hs-responsive-embed-wrapper hs-responsive-embed\" style=\"position: relative; top: 0; left: 0; width: 100%; height: auto; border: none; overflow: hidden; padding: 0; max-width: 650px; max-height: 365px; min-width: 256px; margin: 0px auto; display: block;\"> \n <div class=\"hs-responsive-embed-inner-wrapper\" style=\"position: relative; overflow: hidden; max-width: 100%; padding-bottom: 56.15%; margin: 0;\">\n  <iframe class=\"hs-responsive-embed-iframe\" style=\"position: absolute; top: 0; left: 0; width: 100%; height: 100%; border: none;\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/FHtvDA0W34I\" width=\"650\" height=\"365\" frameborder=\"0\"></iframe>\n </div> \n</div> \n<p>&nbsp;</p> \n<p>In 2012, the company went all-in on its tagline “Red Bull gives you wings by sending skydiver Alex Baumgartner 24 miles above the Earth’s surface to pull off the highest skydive ever recorded and become the first person to break the sound barrier during freefall.</p> \n<p>While his record was broken two years later by an executive from Google, it doesn’t change the fact that Red Bull did something no one had ever done before and created a unique brand experience that aligned with its core marketing message.</p> \n<h3>3. <a href=\"https://youtu.be/RrftWVessAw\">Cadbury India</a></h3> \n<div class=\"hs-responsive-embed-wrapper hs-responsive-embed\" style=\"position: relative; top: 0px; left: 0px; width: 100%; height: auto; border: none; overflow: hidden; padding: 0; max-width: 650px; max-height: 365px; min-width: 256px; margin: 0px auto; display: block;\"> \n <div class=\"hs-responsive-embed-inner-wrapper\" style=\"position: relative; overflow: hidden; max-width: 100%; padding-bottom: 56.15%; margin: 0;\">\n  <iframe class=\"hs-responsive-embed-iframe\" style=\"position: absolute; top: 0; left: 0; width: 100%; height: 100%; border: none;\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/RrftWVessAw\" width=\"650\" height=\"365\" frameborder=\"0\"></iframe>\n </div> \n</div> \n<p>Cadbury India opted for consumer suggestions in creating their new chocolate bar flavor. Customers were encouraged to visit the company’s dedicated chocolate bar platform that let them select ingredients and create a recipe. Cadbury then tried all suggested recipes and selected the best of those submitted.</p> \n<p>By prioritizing interaction over simple reaction, Cadbury facilitated consumer connection and encouraged customers to view chocolate bar making as a collaborative effort rather than a corporate endeavor, in turn creating a community-based brand experience.</p> \n<h3>4. <a href=\"https://www.nike.com/\">Nike</a></h3> \n<div class=\"hs-responsive-embed-wrapper hs-responsive-embed\" style=\"position: relative; top: 0px; left: 0px; width: 100%; height: auto; border: none; overflow: hidden; padding: 0; max-width: 650px; max-height: 365px; min-width: 256px; margin: 0px auto; display: block;\"> \n <div class=\"hs-responsive-embed-inner-wrapper\" style=\"position: relative; overflow: hidden; max-width: 100%; padding-bottom: 56.15%; margin: 0;\">\n  <iframe class=\"hs-responsive-embed-iframe\" style=\"position: absolute; top: 0; left: 0; width: 100%; height: 100%; border: none;\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/fUldMpGbBdA\" width=\"650\" height=\"365\" frameborder=\"0\"></iframe>\n </div> \n</div> \n<p>Similarly to Cadbury, Nike found that giving customers more control over their products was a win. <a href=\"https://www.nike.com/nike-by-you\">Nike By You</a> allows customers to customize their favorite Nike kicks online using various color and style combinations.</p> \n<p>Their flagship store in NYC’s SoHo boasts a sneaker bar where customers can customize their shoes in person with dip-dyeing, patches, and accessories. This emphasis on customization and personalization allows Nike to fully integrate into their customers' lives, creating a brand experience that lasts long after they’ve made a purchase.</p> \n<h3>5. <a href=\"https://youtu.be/eaB8XkpHd64\">Lean Cuisine</a></h3> \n<div class=\"hs-responsive-embed-wrapper hs-responsive-embed\" style=\"position: relative; top: 0px; left: 0px; width: 100%; height: auto; border: none; overflow: hidden; padding: 0; max-width: 650px; max-height: 365px; min-width: 256px; margin: 0px auto; display: block;\"> \n <div class=\"hs-responsive-embed-inner-wrapper\" style=\"position: relative; overflow: hidden; max-width: 100%; padding-bottom: 56.15%; margin: 0;\">\n  <iframe class=\"hs-responsive-embed-iframe\" style=\"position: absolute; top: 0; left: 0; width: 100%; height: 100%; border: none;\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/eaB8XkpHd64\" width=\"650\" height=\"365\" frameborder=\"0\"></iframe>\n </div> \n</div> \n<p>While healthy eating has taken off in recent years, messaging around this effort is often the opposite. With a focus on weight loss instead of overall health, many brands find themselves reinforcing harmful stereotypes that equate weight loss with personal worth.</p> \n<p>Lean Cuisine’s #WeighThis campaign looked to change the narrative by placing “scales” around New York’s Grand Central Station that encouraged women to “weigh in”.</p> \n<p>The catch? These scales were actually boards that let women write down how they would prefer to be measured — such as by their own persistence, accomplishments or efforts.</p> \n<p>Even better? Lean Cuisine marketers were smart enough to stay out of the way. There were no samples on offer, no surveys to fill out; women simply saw the scales and interacted with them, in turn boosting Lean Cuisine’s overall brand experience.</p> \n<h3>6. <a href=\"https://youtu.be/wpM499XhMJQ\">Dove</a></h3> \n<div class=\"hs-responsive-embed-wrapper hs-responsive-embed\" style=\"position: relative; top: 0px; left: 0px; width: 100%; height: auto; border: none; overflow: hidden; padding: 0; max-width: 650px; max-height: 488px; min-width: 256px; margin: 0px auto; display: block;\"> \n <div class=\"hs-responsive-embed-inner-wrapper\" style=\"position: relative; overflow: hidden; max-width: 100%; padding-bottom: 75.08%; margin: 0;\">\n  <iframe class=\"hs-responsive-embed-iframe\" style=\"position: absolute; top: 0; left: 0; width: 100%; height: 100%; border: none;\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/wpM499XhMJQ\" width=\"650\" height=\"488\" frameborder=\"0\" allowfullscreen></iframe>\n </div> \n</div> \n<p>Dove’s Campaign for Real Beauty took a similar approach to Lean Cuisine but opted for the use of viral video that highlighted beauty of all types — beauty that goes beyond photoshoots and photoshop. The campaign earned praise for both its authenticity and efforts to help boost self-esteem among young girls.</p> \n<p>By choosing emotional experience over a simple sales effort, Dove was able to better connect with its target customer base and boost overall customer loyalty.</p> \n<h3>7. <a href=\"https://www.zillow.com/\">Zillow</a></h3> \n<div class=\"hs-responsive-embed-wrapper hs-responsive-embed\" style=\"position: relative; top: 0px; left: 0px; width: 100%; height: auto; border: none; overflow: hidden; padding: 0; max-width: 650px; max-height: 365px; min-width: 256px; margin: 0px auto; display: block;\"> \n <div class=\"hs-responsive-embed-inner-wrapper\" style=\"position: relative; overflow: hidden; max-width: 100%; padding-bottom: 56.15%; margin: 0;\">\n  <iframe class=\"hs-responsive-embed-iframe\" style=\"position: absolute; top: 0; left: 0; width: 100%; height: 100%; border: none;\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/fWOY9-X5mSg\" width=\"650\" height=\"365\" frameborder=\"0\"></iframe>\n </div> \n</div> \n<p>Zillow’s “To Move is to Grow” campaign tapped into 2021’s pandemic house hunting frenzy. As people started remote work, folks realized that they didn’t need to live in crowded cities, and browsing the home search site quickly became a common pastime, which <a href=\"https://youtu.be/yEfsaXDX0UQ\">Saturday Night Live</a> hilariously highlighted in one of its skits that year.</p> \n<p>Tugging at our heartstrings, Zillow tackled the emotional rollercoaster of moving. Using an aesthetic reminiscent of <a href=\"https://www.warnerbros.com/movies/where-wild-things-are\"><em>Where the Wild Things Are</em></a>, the first commercial showcases a child unsure about what her moving adventure will bring. The second one hones in on a seller’s perspective. Susan, the main character, is faced with a host of doppelgangers that try to influence her decision.</p> \n<p>With many across the globe feeling like their lives were in flux, Zillow was able to create a brand experience that showed empathy with their customers as they navigated their new normal during a pandemic. It also positioned the brand as a reliable guide to assist with their transition, whether buying or selling.</p> \n<h3>8.<a href=\"https://youtu.be/OSYhPIAIU9o\"> WestJet</a></h3> \n<div class=\"hs-responsive-embed-wrapper hs-responsive-embed\" style=\"position: relative; top: 0px; left: 0px; width: 100%; height: auto; border: none; overflow: hidden; padding: 0; max-width: 650px; max-height: 367px; min-width: 256px; margin: 0px auto; display: block;\"> \n <div class=\"hs-responsive-embed-inner-wrapper\" style=\"position: relative; overflow: hidden; max-width: 100%; padding-bottom: 56.46%; margin: 0;\">\n  <iframe class=\"hs-responsive-embed-iframe\" style=\"position: absolute; top: 0; left: 0; width: 100%; height: 100%; border: none;\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/OSYhPIAIU9o\" width=\"650\" height=\"367\" frameborder=\"0\" allowfullscreen></iframe>\n </div> \n</div> \n<p>Canadian commercial airline WestJet has been running its “Christmas Miracle” campaign since 2013. Its 2021 version sees the company asking people what they miss the most during the holidays — not surprisingly, many mention absent family members. WestJet staff then provide plane tickets to help loved ones reconnect, and the end of the video features a tearful reunion in progress.</p> \n<p>Overall, it’s a feel-good experience designed to bring out emotions already close to the surface for many customers and in turn, boost the overall brand experience.</p> \n<h2>Building a Better Brand Experience</h2> \n<p>The right brand experience makes all the difference when it comes to cultivating long-term customer relationships. By understanding where current efforts don’t deliver, prioritizing areas for improvement, and tracking engagement metrics over time, it’s possible to build a brand experience that boosts customer connection and encourages long-term loyalty.</p> \n<p><em>Editor's note: This post was originally published in February 2016 and has been updated for comprehensiveness.</em></p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=ddbf2eb7-04e8-44b2-9e05-b21264e09b65&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; \" alt=\"brand consistency\" src=\"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/ddbf2eb7-04e8-44b2-9e05-b21264e09b65.png\"></a></p> \n<p></p>  \n<img src=\"https://track.hubspot.com/__ptq.gif?a=53&amp;k=14&amp;r=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.hubspot.com%2Fmarketing%2Fbrand-experience&amp;bu=https%253A%252F%252Fblog.hubspot.com%252Fmarketing&amp;bvt=rss\" alt=\"\" width=\"1\" height=\"1\" style=\"min-height:1px!important;width:1px!important;border-width:0!important;margin-top:0!important;margin-bottom:0!important;margin-right:0!important;margin-left:0!important;padding-top:0!important;padding-bottom:0!important;padding-right:0!important;padding-left:0!important; \">","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Thu, 10 Mar 2022 12:00:00 +0000","feedId":54,"bgimg":"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/814dd420-0d49-40e0-b59c-f01066e186c1.png","linkMd5":"25b8724829410ff484ff4f980aa01943","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn34@2020_3/2022/03/14/08-15-06-083_eac7fa40866dc905.webp","destWidth":382,"destHeight":59,"sourceBytes":4555,"destBytes":6088,"author":"Doug Bonderud","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/814dd420-0d49-40e0-b59c-f01066e186c1.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn34@2020_3/2022/03/14/08-15-06-083_eac7fa40866dc905.webp","https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Everything%20You%20Need%20to%20Know%20about%20Brand%20Experience.jpg?width=650&name=Everything%20You%20Need%20to%20Know%20about%20Brand%20Experience.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx33/cdn96@2020_4/2022/03/14/08-15-13-546_e3b7fe945edb1991.webp","https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/ddbf2eb7-04e8-44b2-9e05-b21264e09b65.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx27/cdn34@2020_2/2022/03/14/08-15-09-474_f4156d3bc1379fd0.webp","https://track.hubspot.com/__ptq.gif?a=53&k=14&r=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.hubspot.com%2Fmarketing%2Fbrand-experience&bu=https%253A%252F%252Fblog.hubspot.com%252Fmarketing&bvt=rss":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn21@2020_4/2022/03/14/08-15-15-028_7523cd1b4a8ce620.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1647245705072},{"createdTime":"2022-03-14 16:15:05","updatedTime":"2022-03-14 16:15:05","title":"What is Context Marketing? Why It Matters in 2022 [+Examples]","link":"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/33894/what-s-the-deal-with-this-whole-context-marketing-thing.aspx","description":"<p>While it's fair to say most marketers are on-board with the importance of <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/content-marketing\">content marketing</a>, there's still an aspect of marketing that doesn't get as much love: context marketing.</p>  \n<p>Whether you know what context marketing means or not, I'm willing to bet you want to deliver the right campaigns to the right customers at the right time. That’s what context marketing is all about.</p> \n<p>Here, we're going to introduce the concept of context marketing and dive into strategies you can use to implement it into your overall marketing strategy.</p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=a145a75e-59f6-4b51-a482-4f3ea486e740&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; margin: 0 auto; display: block; margin-top: 20px; margin-bottom: 20px\" alt=\"Free Resource: Content Marketing Planning Template\" src=\"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/a145a75e-59f6-4b51-a482-4f3ea486e740.png\" align=\"middle\"></a></p> \n<p></p> \n<p>My favorite context marketing definition is delivering the right content, to the right people, at the right time.</p> \n<p>Let me explain what I mean by context a little more, though. When you have context around something, you have a larger, more telling picture — you know, those little details that lend more clarity to things that would otherwise be pretty general, unspecific, and, well, uninteresting.</p> \n<p>The best marketers leverage context about their audience, leads, and customers in their content marketing. They create <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/audience-profile\">audience profiles</a> and <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/buyer-persona-research\">buyer personas</a> and use that information to create more effective marketing and advertising campaigns.</p> \n<p>Now that we have a basic understanding of context marketing, you might be wondering what the difference is between content marketing and context marketing. Let’s take a look below.</p> \n<p>A marketer using context would know more about a lead than her first name. They might also know what industry she works in, what kind of content she likes best, through which channel she prefers to consume content, whether she's currently using another solution to meet her needs, and whether her company has budget at this time of year.</p> \n<p>As a marketer, if you were asked to \"market\" to someone, and all you were given was a first name and the type of company your lead works at, wouldn't your first question be ... what else do we know about her? Probably, if you want to do your job way better.</p> \n<p>That's the idea behind context marketing: Using what you know about your contacts to provide supremely relevant, targeted, and <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/data-personalize-marketing-li\">personalized marketing</a>.</p> \n<h2>Why is context marketing important?</h2> \n<p>Context marketing is important for many reasons, but there are two top ones that make its importance even more salient. Let’s go over them below.</p> \n<h3>Context marketing converts better.</h3> \n<p>When you're creating marketing that's targeted at people's point of need, it stands to reason that marketing will perform much better for you, because you aren't delivering marketing content that's misaligned with their interests or stage in the <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/sales/what-is-the-buyers-journey\">buyer’s journey</a>.</p> \n<p>Think about it: If you know that a B2B lead is getting a new budget in January and it's December, you're able to send her insanely targeted content that addresses her needs — like, say, an offer for a custom demo of your product with a rep that specializes in the finance industry. That's content that she's pretty likely to convert on, especially if she's downloaded a buying guide and visited your product pages.</p> \n<p><strong>Hot tip</strong>: Keeping track of your prospect’s activity using <a href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/products/marketing/marketing-automation\">marketing automation software</a> will make context marketing easier. You’ll know which products your prospect is most interested in and how many times they’ve visited your website.</p> \n<h3>Context marketing increases retention.</h3> \n<p>When you have context around your relationship with a contact, you're able to provide more personalized and relevant marketing content that's targeted to their needs.</p> \n<p>This is great for two reasons: Personalized and relevant marketing is the foundation for <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/content-creation\">creating content</a> people love and engage with. What's more, personalized and relevant marketing is typically not the kind of marketing that annoys people into clicking \"unsubscribe\". If they feel like you’re out to solve their problems specifically, customers are much more likely to stay with you.</p> \n<p>Why not use the context around your relationships with your contacts to create marketing that they love and convert on? Let’s take a look at how you can get started.</p> \n<h2>How to Start Context Marketing</h2> \n<p>Alright, how does this \"context marketing\" theory manifest itself? What would it look like for you, as a marketer? With the help of <a href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/products?hubs_post=blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/33894/what-s-the-deal-with-this-whole-context-marketing-thing.aspx&amp;hubs_post-cta=integrated%20marketing%20software\">marketing automation software</a>, here are some examples of where you'd actually use the principle of \"context\" in your marketing.</p> \n<h3>1. Create specific offers for specific posts and pages.</h3> \n<p>One easy way you can start context marketing? Create offers that extend the value of your website. Bonus points if these offers answer a specific pain point or problem that a customer is trying to solve for when visiting that page.</p> \n<p>Most blog posts in HubSpot’s library feature an offer that’s directly related to the topic of the article. For instance, in our <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/marketing-plan-template-generator?hubs_post-cta=blognavcard-marketing\">blog post about creating a marketing plan</a>, you can download a marketing plan template — which is something that someone wanting to create a marketing plan might need.</p> \n<h3><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/context-marketing-example-offer.jpeg?width=650&amp;name=context-marketing-example-offer.jpeg\" alt=\"context marketing example: specific offer on HubSpot blog post\" width=\"650\" style=\"width: 650px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\"></h3> \n<p>Come up with content offers that will benefit your readers and website visitors depending on the page they’re visiting. For instance, if you sell hiking shoes and you’re writing a blog post about going on a solo hiking trip, you might feature an offer for downloading a solo hiking checklist.</p> \n<h3>2. Add smart calls-to-action (CTAs) to your website.</h3> \n<p>You can take personalized offers to the next level by featuring smart <a href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/products/marketing/calls-to-action?hubs_post=blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/33894/what-s-the-deal-with-this-whole-context-marketing-thing.aspx&amp;hubs_post-cta=dynamic%20CTAs\">calls-to-action</a>. Let’s say you have a variety of offers you want to use to convert traffic into leads, leads into qualified leads, and qualified leads into customers.</p> \n<p>To <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/how-to-increase-conversion-rate\">increase your lead conversion rates</a>, you probably don't want leads visiting a case study webpage (typically an action you'd perform further along in your buyer's journey), and finding a CTA leading them to a blog post (which is meant for people earlier in the buyer's journey).</p> \n<p>However, not everyone who visits a case study page on your website is necessarily ready to talk to a salesperson. You don't want to turn them away, either, by offering a CTA that's too pushy.</p> \n<p>Fortunately, with smart CTAs, you can actually surface a CTA that automatically aligns with the visitor's stage in the sales cycle ... or any other host of criteria you want to set. Think industry, business type, location, and past activity/behaviors.</p> \n<p>For instance, if you have already downloaded an offer from HubSpot, you might see this CTA on certain social-media-related posts:</p> \n<p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/context-marketing-example-smart-cta.jpeg?width=650&amp;name=context-marketing-example-smart-cta.jpeg\" alt=\"context marketing example: smart cta\" width=\"650\" style=\"width: 650px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\"></p> \n<p>But if you haven’t downloaded an offer before, you’ll see the default CTA:</p> \n<p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/context-marketing-example-default-cta.jpeg?width=650&amp;name=context-marketing-example-default-cta.jpeg\" alt=\"context marketing example: default cta\" width=\"650\" style=\"width: 650px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\"></p> \n<p>This type of smart content can help you capture your audience’s information at all stages of their buyer’s journey.</p> \n<p><strong>Hot tip</strong>: HubSpot’s marketing automation software lets you <a href=\"https://knowledge.hubspot.com/ctas/create-smart-calls-to-action-cta\">easily create a smart calls-to-action</a> with little technical knowledge.</p> \n<h3>3. Create smart forms that shorten the conversion cycle.</h3> \n<p>Smart forms know if someone has already filled out the form fields you're asking for. If you use smart forms, for instance, your site visitors won't see \"First Name\" and \"Last Name\" every time they fill out a form — instead, they'll answer those questions once, and then never again.</p> \n<p>This will help you glean new information about your leads each time they fill out a form, instead of just more of the same stuff. It also helps you create a more seamless, personalized user experience that leverages prior interactions with your website as context.</p> \n<p>Here’s one example from HubSpot Academy. This is what I see when I’m logged into the HubSpot CRM:</p> \n<p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/context-marketing-example-smart-form.jpeg?width=650&amp;name=context-marketing-example-smart-form.jpeg\" alt=\"context marketing example: smart form\" width=\"650\" style=\"width: 650px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\"></p> \n<p>The form knows I’m a current HubSpot customer and doesn’t require me to create a new account. I only have to click one button: “Start the Course.”</p> \n<p>But this is what I see when I’m not logged in:</p> \n<p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/context-marketing-example-default-form.jpeg?width=650&amp;name=context-marketing-example-default-form.jpeg\" alt=\"context marketing example: default form\" width=\"650\" style=\"width: 650px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\"></p> \n<p>Ultimately, smart forms will help you gather even more context about your visitors, leads, and customers, and help increase conversion rates over time.</p> \n<p><strong>Hot tip</strong>: You can easily <a href=\"https://knowledge.hubspot.com/cos-general/create-smart-forms?hubs_post=blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/33894/what-s-the-deal-with-this-whole-context-marketing-thing.aspx&amp;hubs_post-cta=smart%20forms\">create smart forms</a> inside HubSpot’s marketing automation software.</p> \n<h3>4. Leverage dynamic email content and workflows.</h3> \n<p>Your forms and offers aren't the only things that need to be smart. Your email database — especially if you want to maintain your space in people's coveted inboxes — <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/email-list-segmentation\">needs to be segmented</a> into highly targeted lists, as well.</p> \n<p>I happen to be subscribed to Grammarly emails on both my work and personal emails. Because I only use the Grammarly Chrome extension at work, I receive emails like this:</p> \n<p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/context-marketing-example-segmented-email-example.jpeg?width=650&amp;name=context-marketing-example-segmented-email-example.jpeg\" alt=\"context marketing example: grammarly segmented email\" width=\"650\" style=\"width: 650px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\">In my personal account, however, I use Grammarly’s web app regularly and review thousands of words for a personal project. Here’s the email I get:</p> \n<p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/context-marketing-example-segmented-email-grammarly.jpeg?width=650&amp;name=context-marketing-example-segmented-email-grammarly.jpeg\" alt=\"context marketing example: grammarly second segmented email\" width=\"650\" style=\"width: 650px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\">Throughout the email, Grammarly prompts you to upgrade to the premium version and take advantage of its other tools. Because I don’t use the Chrome extension in my personal email account, it includes a call-to-action to install the extension. It’s delightful to receive an email that uses my account activity as context.</p> \n<p>Beyond email segmentation, your email lists need to be smart enough to know when to pull in a contact, and certain information you have in your database about that contact, into your email marketing campaigns.</p> \n<p>Remember, a great context marketer delivers the right content, to the right person, at the right time. So to send emails that are contextually relevant, you need to use their activity and background to deliver personalized content that delights them and prompts them to convert.</p> \n<h2>Context Marketing Examples</h2> \n<p>While context marketing may sound complicated, it’s actually quite simple in practice. In fact, as a customer, you may have seen or enjoyed context marketing yourself. Let’s take a look at some examples.</p> \n<h3>1. Google’s Product Ads Carousel</h3> \n<p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/context-marketing-example-google.jpeg?width=650&amp;name=context-marketing-example-google.jpeg\" alt=\"context marketing example: google product carousel ads\" width=\"650\" style=\"width: 650px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\"></p> \n<p>Have you ever looked up a product on Google and see a carousel at the top (as opposed to just the plain search results)? The products you see are typically ads for the exact same thing you searched for.</p> \n<p>This is a prime contextual marketing example. Google uses your behavior and search query to deliver ads that are contextually relevant. Imagine if, when searching for instant coffee, Google delivers ads for french presses instead. While you might be interested in French presses and even searched for them before, you’re looking for instant coffee right now.</p> \n<p>That’s why it’s important to answer for your customer’s specific pain points and queries, and to do so at the right time. And you don’t have to be a highly sophisticated search engine to do so. Remember those offers we spoke about in the previous sections? That can function in the same way as Google’s product carousels.</p> \n<h3>2. Asana’s New Feature Pop-Up</h3> \n<p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/context-marketing-example-asana.jpeg?width=650&amp;name=context-marketing-example-asana.jpeg\" alt=\"context marketing example: asana feature popup\" width=\"650\" style=\"width: 650px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\"></p> \n<p>There’s no more powerful place to carry out contextual marketing than right within your own product, website, or store. Asana’s example shows that you can upsell customers easily by marketing a new feature and prompting them to try it for free.</p> \n<p>This is an excellent example of contextual marketing because you wouldn’t be interested in trying this new feature unless you were a current Asana user. For instance, if Asana had placed this pop-up on their homepage, they likely wouldn’t have much success with it. But because it pops up after you log in, you’re more likely to say, “Sure, I’ll try it.”</p> \n<p>You can achieve something similar by instituting a <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/website/website-personalization-examples-dynamic\">website personalization campaign</a>. When people visit your product page, for instance, they might see a popup to schedule a meeting with a salesperson. But when they’re on the blog, they might see a popup to subscribe. These simple changes can help you capture more leads and use the context from their activity to deliver an offer they won’t resist.</p> \n<h3>3. LinkedIn Company Page Sidebar Ad</h3> \n<p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/context-marketing-example-linkedin.jpeg?width=650&amp;name=context-marketing-example-linkedin.jpeg\" alt=\"context marketing example: linkedin sidebar ad on company page\" width=\"650\" style=\"width: 650px; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\"></p> \n<p>When you visit a company page on LinkedIn, it provides a little sidebar ad that prompts you to find roles at that company that match your skills.</p> \n<p>LinkedIn does this because it knows that you might be open to opportunities even if you don’t list it on your profile. And if you’re looking at a company page, you might be interested in working at that firm. LinkedIn uses this context to deliver a relevant ad that you can’t help but click on.</p> \n<p>Another reason this is such a great example is that it also lists a job title that relates to yours. So if you’re a financial advisor and are looking at JP Morgan Chase’s company page, LinkedIn will automatically advertise financial advisor roles at the firm.</p> \n<h2>Context Marketing is the Next Evolution of Content Marketing</h2> \n<p>Without context, you risk reaching the wrong people at the wrong time. Begin using context in all of your marketing and advertising campaigns, and you’ll see an exponential increase in conversions, helping you exceed your lead acquisition goals and increase revenue at your company.</p> \n<p><em>Editor's note: This post was originally published in March 2013 and has been updated for comprehensiveness. &nbsp;</em></p> \n<p></p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" 16:15:05","updatedTime":"2022-03-14 16:15:05","title":"Does Your Company Need An Employee Referral Program? [Examples + Best Practices]","link":"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/employee-referral-program","description":"<p>Finding qualified candidates to fill your open positions can be challenging. Job posting sites claim to make the process easy by connecting you with hundreds if not thousands of potential employees. But having such a large pool of candidates can be overwhelming.</p>  \n<p>Just thinking about the sheer volume of work involved in reviewing applications, narrowing them down to good fits, and then vetting those potential candidates is enough to make anyone’s head explode.</p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=3f403048-fd8e-426f-bddd-4fce020ae24b&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; margin: 0 auto; display: block; margin-top: 20px; margin-bottom: 20px\" alt=\"Download Now: Free Company Culture Code Template&nbsp;\" src=\"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/3f403048-fd8e-426f-bddd-4fce020ae24b.png\" align=\"middle\"></a></p> \n<p>You work with or run a solid organization with wonderful employees. How do you make sure that you don’t get a bevy of potential candidates, but rather the <em>right</em> candidate?</p> \n<p>Look at this like finding the perfect place to take your significant other on a special occasion. Sure, you could do a Google search for random restaurants in your neighborhood. You could even check a review site for recommendations.</p> \n<p>However, you don’t know any of those people, so how much weight does their opinion really carry? Instead of taking a risk on a very special evening, why not reach out to the people you trust? Asking friends and family for a recommendation is a much safer avenue to finding the perfect date night experience.</p> \n<p>What if we applied this type of thinking to your search for the perfect employee? Rather than leave it up to a random internet search, ask the people you already know, like, and trust… your employees.</p> \n<h2>What is an employee referral program?</h2> \n<p>An employee referral program is a structured system by which you ask existing employees to recommend people they know for open positions within your organization. Employees often receive some sort of incentive for their assistance.</p> \n<p>An employee referral program leverages the power of your employees’ networks and can save you time, money, and a huge headache when it comes to hiring the best talent for your business.</p> \n<h2>Benefits of an Employee Referral Program</h2> \n<p>There are many benefits to utilizing an employee referral program as part of your hiring strategy. These include:</p> \n<h3>1. High Quality Hires</h3> \n<p>Good employees know what skills are necessary to excel in a position and understand the workplace culture. When they recommend someone for the job, there’s a good chance they have the qualifications necessary to successfully perform in the role.</p> \n<h3>2. Decreased Turnover Rates</h3> \n<p>With employee turnover rates <a href=\"https://www.zippia.com/advice/employee-turnover-statistics/\"><span>on the rise</span></a>, you’ll want to keep it front of mind when you’re making hiring decisions. According to <a href=\"https://www.linkedin.com/pulse/employee-referral-statistics-you-need-know-2020-mike-stafiej/?articleId=6622562177335336961\"><span>ERIN</span></a>, 45% of referred employees stay with a company longer compared to 22% from job boards and 33% from career sites.</p> \n<h3>3. Less Time and Lower Cost Per Hire</h3> \n<p>According to <a href=\"https://business.linkedin.com/content/dam/me/business/en-us/talent-solutions/resources/pdfs/new_employee_referral_programs_FINAL.pdf\"><span>LinkedIn</span></a>, employees hired through referrals take an average of 29 days to hire and onboard, whereas job boards can take 39 days and a career site can take upwards of 55 days. The less time it takes to hire and onboard means less revenue lost, fewer employees stressed because they are handling multiple jobs, and more productivity from your new hire.</p> \n<p>Using a headhunter? According to <a href=\"https://www.jobvite.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/10/Jobvite-RecruiterNation-Report-Final.pdf\"><span>Jobvite</span></a>, you can expect to pay between 15% and 25% of the gross annual salary of the candidate. If you’re hiring an employee at $100k per year, that’s $15k to $25k in headhunting fees. The cost to reward an employee for an amazing referral? Around $2,000.</p> \n<h3>4. Increase Employee Satisfaction and Loyalty</h3> \n<p>Doesn’t it feel nice when you have a hand in the decision-making process? Employees that refer candidates feel like they’ve contributed to the company, making them more engaged and more likely to stay.</p> \n<h2>Employee Referral Program Ideas</h2> \n<p>Now that you see the benefit to you as the employer or hiring manager, how do you create an employee referral program that encourages your existing employees to introduce you to their quality contacts? There are a number of ways to do this and best practices that you can adopt to get the most out of your program.</p> \n<h3>Make it Clear What You’re Looking For</h3> \n<p>In a mid-sized to a large company, one department may have no idea what another one is working on. In order for employees to make connections, they need to know what your expectations are for the new position. When you reach out to employees looking for suggestions, provide them with all the details you can. This should include:</p> \n<ul> \n <li><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/marketing-job-descriptions\"><span>Job descriptions</span></a></li> \n <li>Desired experience</li> \n <li>Necessary skills</li> \n</ul> \n<h3>Make it Easy for Employees to Refer</h3> \n<p>Consider the referral experience from your employees’ point of view. Is there a simple form for them to submit when they recommend someone, or do they have to jump through a variety of complicated hoops to pass along their referrals? Some companies even host recruitment happy hours where existing employees can invite friends who might be a good fit.</p> \n<p>The easier you make it for your employees to refer their contacts, the more quality candidates will be presented to you.</p> \n<h3>Keep Your Employees Updated on Referral Status</h3> \n<p>It’s frustrating to make a suggestion or an introduction and not know if it’s been acted upon. When your employee recommends a colleague, keep them updated as to the steps of the hiring process. Some times to check-in include:</p> \n<ul> \n <li>When you receive an application</li> \n <li>When you make contact</li> \n <li>When an interview is scheduled</li> \n <li>When a position has been offered to their contact</li> \n <li>When the position has been given to someone else (after the candidate has been contacted)</li> \n</ul> \n<h3>Provide a Juicy Incentive</h3> \n<p>Surprisingly, this may not always be a monetary reward. While money is always appreciated, you can offer a combination of \"cash\" and experiences, time off, gifts, etc. For some, these may be even more desired than a financial incentive. One great option is to give your employees the choice. That way, you know they’ll be motivated to help. A few employee referral incentive ideas to get your creative juices flowing:</p> \n<ul> \n <li>Cash bonuses</li> \n <li>Gift certificates to their favorite restaurants and local establishments</li> \n <li>Weekend getaways or week-long excursions for frequent referrers</li> \n <li>VIP parking</li> \n <li>Show tickets</li> \n <li>Physical gifts (it’s important to let them choose so they don’t end up with something they can’t use)</li> \n <li>Perks like a gym membership or massage</li> \n</ul> \n<p>The sky's the limit when it comes to thanking your employees for their referrals. You can also consider using a platform like <a href=\"https://www.xoxoday.com/\">XoxoDay</a> to make distributing employee referral perks as easy and streamlined as possible.</p> \n<h3>Show Appreciation for \"Frequent Referrers\"</h3> \n<p>If you’ve got employees that consistently send you quality employee candidates, acknowledge them publicly. This shows your amazing team members that they are appreciated and motivates other employees to step up their referral game.</p> \n<h2>Employee Referral Program Examples</h2> \n<p>Looking for real-world examples of these programs in action? We’ve compiled a few employee referral program samples to introduce you to some of the possibilities.</p> \n<ol> \n <li><a href=\"https://www.inmobi.com/\"><span>Inmobi</span></a>, a mobile advertising company offers referring employees the choice of a bike or a trip to Bali. They park the vehicles in front of the company headquarters to motivate employees to participate.</li> \n <li><a href=\"https://www.accenture.com/us-en\"><span>Accenture</span></a>, a consulting and IT company encourages philanthropy and community involvement by letting their employees donate a part of their referral bonus to a charity of their choice.</li> \n <li><a href=\"https://distillery.com/\"><span>Distillery</span></a>, an American software development company gifts their employees new tech gadgets for every referral they make.</li> \n <li><a href=\"https://www.atlassian.com/\"><span>Atlassian</span></a> software company encourages employees to \"Refer-a-Mate\" and offers them $2,000 in cash bonuses.</li> \n <li><a href=\"https://www.intel.com/content/www/us/en/homepage.html\"><span>Intel</span></a> tech company takes financial incentives one step further by doubling their employee referral reward for women, minorities, and veterans that are referred to the company.</li> \n</ol> \n<p>If you’d like to tap into a pool of qualified, trustworthy, easy-to-hire (and onboard) candidates, an employee referral program can help. Instituting this type of hiring process in your organization can save you money, time, headaches, and the pain of having to repeatedly hire for the same position when your first employee doesn’t work out well. In addition, you’ll improve your workplace culture and enhance your brand.</p> \n<p>An employee referral program is the best thing you can do to improve the quality of your incoming employees. Choose your incentives wisely and then watch the quality candidates roll on in.</p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=4bbcf7f8-3c11-4d5b-b284-c5f6a9d419c9&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; \" alt=\"company culture template\" src=\"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/4bbcf7f8-3c11-4d5b-b284-c5f6a9d419c9.png\"></a></p> \n<p></p>  \n<img src=\"https://track.hubspot.com/__ptq.gif?a=53&amp;k=14&amp;r=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.hubspot.com%2Fmarketing%2Femployee-referral-program&amp;bu=https%253A%252F%252Fblog.hubspot.com%252Fmarketing&amp;bvt=rss\" alt=\"\" width=\"1\" height=\"1\" style=\"min-height:1px!important;width:1px!important;border-width:0!important;margin-top:0!important;margin-bottom:0!important;margin-right:0!important;margin-left:0!important;padding-top:0!important;padding-bottom:0!important;padding-right:0!important;padding-left:0!important; \">","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Wed, 09 Mar 2022 12:00:00 +0000","feedId":54,"bgimg":"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/3f403048-fd8e-426f-bddd-4fce020ae24b.png","linkMd5":"ad7181ffe31559a408a75af9a3fd7bc0","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn91@2020_2/2022/03/14/08-15-05-733_af47b0cd123e84fb.webp","destWidth":489,"destHeight":59,"sourceBytes":5237,"destBytes":7504,"author":"Sheryl Green","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/3f403048-fd8e-426f-bddd-4fce020ae24b.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn91@2020_2/2022/03/14/08-15-05-733_af47b0cd123e84fb.webp","https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/4bbcf7f8-3c11-4d5b-b284-c5f6a9d419c9.png":null,"https://track.hubspot.com/__ptq.gif?a=53&k=14&r=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.hubspot.com%2Fmarketing%2Femployee-referral-program&bu=https%253A%252F%252Fblog.hubspot.com%252Fmarketing&bvt=rss":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn75@2020_3/2022/03/14/08-15-21-265_aa77a0f97e109ceb.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1647245705115},{"createdTime":"2022-03-14 16:15:05","updatedTime":"2022-03-14 16:15:05","title":"The Plain-English Guide to Conjoint Analysis","link":"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/conjoint-analysis","description":"<p>Sometimes, commercials <em>really</em> get me.</p>  \n<p><a href=\"https://www.cbssports.com/nfl/video/2019-super-bowl-commercials-sprint/\">T-Mobile</a>'s Super Bowl commercial this year is a prime example — \"What's for Dinner?\" demonstrates the infuriating process of choosing what to do for dinner for a young couple, and it's<em> gold</em>.</p> \n<p>The reason T-Mobile's ad was so relatable is because of their market research. They looked at what their target audiences wanted — including their thought processes, what informs their decisions, and the trade-offs they're willing to make for their products.</p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=6ba52ce7-bb69-4b63-965b-4ea21ba905da&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; margin: 0 auto; display: block; margin-top: 20px; margin-bottom: 20px\" alt=\"→ Download Now: Market Research Templates [Free Kit]\" src=\"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/6ba52ce7-bb69-4b63-965b-4ea21ba905da.png\" align=\"middle\"></a></p> \n<p>To accomplish all of these important factors in one go, many companies use conjoint analysis.</p> \n<p>Think about buying a new phone. Attributes you might consider are color, size, and model. The reason phone companies include these specs in their marketing is due to research such as conjoint analysis.</p> \n<p><em>Would consumers purchase this product or service if brought to market?</em> That's the question conjoint analysis strives to answer. It's a quantitative measure in marketing research, meaning it measures numbers rather than open-ended questions. Questions on the phone company survey would include price points, color preference, and camera quality.</p> \n<p>Surveys intended for conjoint analysis are formatted to reflect the buyer's journey.</p> \n<p>For instance, notice in this example for televisions, the specs are the options and the consumer picks what best reflects their lifestyle:</p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/conjoint%20analysis%20example.png?width=706&amp;name=conjoint%20analysis%20example.png\" alt=\"conjoint analysis example\" width=\"706\" style=\"width: 706px; display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;\"><em><span style=\"font-size: 10px;\"><strong><a href=\"https://www.surveygizmo.com/resources/blog/conjoint-analysis/\">Image Source</a></strong></span></em></p> \n<p>This direct method of giving consumers multiple profiles to then analyze is how conjoint analysis got its name. These answers are helpful when determining how to market a new product.</p> \n<p>If answers on the phone company survey proved that their target audience of adults ages 18-25 wanted a green phone from $400-600 and a camera with portrait mode, advertisements can cater directly to that.</p> \n<p>The conjoint analysis shows what consumers are willing to give up in order to get what they need. For instance, some might be willing to pay a little more money for a larger model of a phone if their preference is larger text.</p> \n<h2>Types of Conjoint Analysis</h2> \n<p>Choice-based conjoint (CBC) and Adaptive Conjoint Analysis (ACA) are the two main types of conjoint analysis.</p> \n<blockquote> \n <p>Choice-based is the most common form because it asks consumers to mimic their buying habits. ACA is helpful for product design, offering more questions about specs of a product.</p> \n</blockquote> \n<p>Choice-based conjoint analysis questions are usually presented in a \"Would you rather?\" format. For example, \"Would you rather take a ride-share service to a location 10 minutes away for $13 or walk 30 minutes for free?\" The marketer for the ride-share service could use answers from this question to think of the upsides to show off in different campaigns.</p> \n<p>ACA leans towards a Likert-scale format (most likely to least likely) for its attribute-based questions. Respondents can base their preference on specs by showing how likely they are to buy a product with slight differences — for example, similar cars with different doors and manufacturers.</p> \n<h2>How To Do A Conjoint Analysis</h2> \n<p>To create a conjoint analysis, you'll first need to define a list of attributes about your product. Attributes are usually four to five items that describe your product or service. Consider color, size, price, and market-specific attributes, such as lenses if you're selling cameras.</p> \n<p>Additionally, try to keep in mind your ideal respondents. Who do you want to answer your survey? A group of adult men? A group of working mothers? Identify your respondent base and ask specific questions catered to that target market.</p> \n<p>The next step is to organize your questionnaire depending on the type of conjoint analysis you want to conduct. For instance, to run an adaptive conjoint analysis, you will present questions with a Likert-scale.</p> \n<p>You can use a conjoint analysis tool to create and modify your survey. Then, you can distribute your questionnaire through multiple channels, including email, SMS, and social media.</p> \n<p>For more ways to introduce product marketing into your company, check out our <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/product-marketing?_ga=2.125836493.1138478006.1643301254-748143700.1643301254\"><span>ultimate guide here</span></a>.</p> \n<h2>Examples of Conjoint Analysis</h2> \n<p>Sawtooth Software offers a great example of conjoint analysis for a phone company:</p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/conjoint%20analysis%20example%202.png?width=752&amp;name=conjoint%20analysis%20example%202.png\" alt=\"conjoint analysis example\" width=\"752\" style=\"width: 752px;\"><span style=\"font-size: 12px;\"><em><a href=\"http://www.sawtooth.com/index.php/consulting/conjoint-analysis-example/\">Image Source</a></em></span></p> \n<p>The analysis puts three different phone services next to each other. The horizontal column of the model identifies which service is offering a certain program, described by the vertical values. The bottom row shows a percent value of consumers' preferences.</p> \n<p>QuestionPro offers this <a href=\"https://www.questionpro.com/survey-templates/conjoint-analysis-retirement-housing/\">fun, interactive conjoint analysis template</a> about retirement home options. The survey gives you a scenario and asks your course of action. For instance, it asks if you would sign a rental agreement for retirement home housing immediately, and considers specs like rent, meals, size, etc.</p> \n<p>Conjoint analysis isn't limited to existing products. They're also very helpful for figuring out if a brand-new product is worth developing. For instance, if surveys show that audiences would be into the idea of an app that chooses clothes for consumers, that could be a new venture for clothing companies in the future.</p> \n<p>Looking to create a conjoint analysis of your own? Check out our top four conjoint analysis tools below.</p> \n<h2>Conjoint Analysis Tools</h2> \n<h3>1. <a href=\"https://www.qualtrics.com/research-core/conjoint-analysis/\">Qualtrics</a></h3> \n<p><img src=\"https://lh4.googleusercontent.com/dljE-fHFAUmTCRVjNx4YBrVtf_4f8piYKenWCKviyQso8_Vq1n60EkyKyE9VW5mVCSuxCoKNZh38TCz-U8yRWf5H8jU83bg59YC_3t-kMjiTqnfs-hkhNeokMs5GNzqffBO8yqqN\" width=\"650\" style=\"width: 650px;\" alt=\"Conjoint Analysis from Qualtrics\"></p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><a href=\"https://www.qualtrics.com/design-xm/conjoint-analysis/\" style=\"font-size: 10px;\"><em><span>Image Source</span></em></a></p> \n<p>Qualtrics is an easy-to-use survey tool that offers comprehensive product insights. You can create, modify, distribute, and analyze a conjoint analysis in one place. All it takes is four steps — define your attributes, build and modify your questions in the survey editor, distribute the survey, and analyze the results.&nbsp;</p> \n<p><strong>What We Like:</strong> Qualtrics goes beyond product insights — this powerful software also captures customer, brand, and employee experience insights.</p> \n<p><strong>Pro Tip:</strong> Leverage email to invite respondents to take your survey. With Qualtrics, you can embed a survey question directly in your email survey invite.&nbsp;</p> \n<h3>2. <a href=\"https://conjointly.com/\">Cojoint.ly</a></h3> \n<p><img src=\"https://lh4.googleusercontent.com/xHegCVzbKTJooNMiaKLoYCmdJ0qH55gOULr3GyYLtZyStm9GFSLI-igefEQITCuzMUMRE_2zpFBWoOZxd-L8ZqOE54jpZNQQRiZ_UoYfvlMOtCiBjJp_CEgB4xcRKdnREZfXeaeH\" width=\"650\" style=\"width: 650px;\" alt=\"Conjoint Analysis from Conjoint.ly\"></p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><a href=\"https://conjointly.com/products/generic-conjoint/\" style=\"font-size: 10px;\"><em><span>Image Source</span></em></a></p> \n<p>Conjoint.ly offers a complete toolbox for product and pricing research — including a Product Description test, an A/B test, and a Price Sensitivity test. You can also source your own respondents for your survey or buy quality-assured respondents from Conjoint.ly.</p> \n<p><strong>What We Like:</strong> Users can simply choose a tool that best fits their research question. These tools are organized under four main categories: pricing research, features and claims, range optimization, and concept testing.</p> \n<p><strong>Pro Tip:</strong> If you want to \"try before you buy,\" you can use Conjoint.ly's Quick Feedback tool. For a small price, you get around 50 respondents to provide feedback within a 6-hour window.</p> \n<h3>3. <a href=\"https://www.1000minds.com/\">1000minds</a></h3> \n<p><img src=\"https://lh4.googleusercontent.com/SHXkxL2-sEBDsMBAo_zs29VcUFCeNDq2jpGMrkCPZVQb30LE60lSIPWu1-GYYSaNb6kJWfUxxly-LQ-L0yaIGUfYLad0yh5npnqeADQz1wQm81i10rWfeBU6uQQE4oOmOxp_NHUu\" width=\"650\" style=\"width: 650px;\" alt=\"Conjoint Analysis from 1000minds\"></p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><a href=\"https://www.1000minds.com/conjoint-analysis\" style=\"font-size: 10px;\"><em><span>Image Source</span></em></a></p> \n<p>1000minds offers an adaptive conjoint analysis tool. Meaning, each time a choice is made, it adapts by formulating a new question to ask based on all previous choices. This makes the survey feel more like a conversation.</p> \n<p><strong>What We Like:</strong> We're impressed by the scalability of 1000minds. The tool allows you to include as many participants as you like, potentially in the thousands.</p> \n<p><strong>Pro Tip:</strong> You can use their conjoint analysis templates or build your own model from scratch.&nbsp;</p> \n<h3>4. <a href=\"https://www.qresearchsoftware.com/\">Q Research Software</a></h3> \n<p><img src=\"https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/rNDE1aPqKGAzfWfp76ksB6QOQQ_L023X5JAswfwCGghnqPfd9fhcZT6PS1KwWz3OGkA_pv6lobAg2x49XshiWQnLCFYx_FqQJGEp_ibFlZXpjE4nA-Ok5Z0yvHqaQSgaPnh6gCba\" width=\"624\" height=\"412\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\" alt=\"Conjoint Analysis from Q Research Software\"></p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\"><a href=\"https://www.qresearchsoftware.com/\" style=\"font-size: 10px;\"><em><span>Image Source</span></em></a></p> \n<p>Q is analysis software that is specifically designed by market researchers. Its conjoint analysis tool is ideal for choice-based analyses. Users can create experimental designs, analyze the data, and generate reports.&nbsp;</p> \n<p><strong>What We Like:</strong> Q cuts through the grunt work with automation — including cleaning and formatting data, updating surveys, and producing reports.</p> \n<p><strong>Pro Tip:</strong> With just a few clicks, you can export any reports or visualizations from Q to PowerPoint and Excel.</p> \n<p>A conjoint analysis requires a solid survey design and analysis, but the extra effort is often worth it. By going the extra mile, you can access insights into your audience's preferences and buying decisions — which is invaluable when determining how to market a new product or service.</p> \n<p><a
