\">","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Mon, 07 Mar 2022 20:22:17 +0000","feedId":54,"bgimg":"","linkMd5":"8f9f3f5b9dc74df42ff958ced2d79a9e","bgimgJsdelivr":"","metaImg":"","author":"Andréa Hudson","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/chimamanda%20quote.png?width=1600&name=chimamanda%20quote.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn20@2020_5/2022/03/14/08-15-12-591_3febf051b384b019.webp","https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/payal%20quote.png?width=1600&name=payal%20quote.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn9@2020_5/2022/03/14/08-15-16-172_dbc5aa55ac4476ea.webp","https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/6e386943-0655-4288-9829-0962158157f4.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn44@2020_5/2022/03/14/08-15-13-168_3a697e214feb5beb.webp","https://track.hubspot.com/__ptq.gif?a=53&k=14&r=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.hubspot.com%2Fmarketing%2Finbound-women-quotes&bu=https%253A%252F%252Fblog.hubspot.com%252Fmarketing&bvt=rss":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx29/cdn69@2020_5/2022/03/14/08-15-09-536_21af4481054dbf03.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1647245705114},{"createdTime":"2022-03-14 16:15:05","updatedTime":"2022-03-14 16:15:05","title":"Ad Tracking: What It Is & How to Do It","link":"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/7249/a-marketer-s-guide-to-tracking-online-campaigns.aspx","description":"<p>Tracking ad engagement and impact has been historically hit-or-miss. There wasn't a universal standard for measuring the success of an ad campaign. In fact, the term ROI (return on investment) wasn't even widely used <a href=\"https://mashable.com/2013/04/27/roi-definition/\">until the mid-1960s</a>.</p> \n<p>A lot has changed since then. Advertisers now have access to a wealth of granular ad tracking data for every single campaign they run. Ad tracking lets marketing teams leverage this data to more accurately measure, test, and revise ads based on how users interact with their online campaigns.</p> \n<a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=da1bfbbd-7ee9-4bf1-89d1-6d7a833deb08&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; margin: 0 auto; display: block; margin-top: 20px; margin-bottom: 20px\" alt=\"Download Now: Free Ad Campaign Planning Kit\" src=\"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/da1bfbbd-7ee9-4bf1-89d1-6d7a833deb08.png\" align=\"middle\"></a> \n<p></p> \n<p>If you're new to running online ads, it's important to spend some time thinking about the specific metrics that will determine the success of your campaign. Ad tracking today exists across a number of different tools and platforms, and advertisers have the ability to collect data on everything from views and clicks, to impressions and behavior across multiple sessions and websites.</p> \n<p>The sheer amount of data available can be overwhelming (not to mention distracting from your goals), so deciding on one or two key performance indicators (KPIs) will help focus your efforts and make reporting more straightforward and effective.</p> \n<blockquote> \n <p>\"Good key performance indicators are simple, timely, critical to the success of a project, and not financial in nature. But you also need to add in one thing if you want it to be a successful marketing metric -- <strong>it must represent a key behavior you wanted to see</strong>. Look at your campaign and ask yourself: What’s the behavior I want to influence, not just something I can measure?\"</p> \n</blockquote> \n<p style=\"text-align: center;\">— <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/agency/measure-kpi?_ga=2.55325803.159970128.1644874104-345458440.1644874104\">William Stentz, Director of Marketing Analytics at Carmichael Lynch</a></p> \n<p><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/analyze-performance-display-ads\">We wrote an article here</a> that can help you determine the right metrics to track based on the goals of your ad campaign.</p> \n<p>Once you've determined the metrics you want to track for your ad, it's time to find the best ad tracking method for your purposes. The exact ad tracking methods available to you will vary based on where you run your ads and which tools you're using, but here are a few basic types to keep in mind. It's important to note that the following ad tracking methods aren't mutually exclusive -- in fact, when used together they can provide even more powerful insights.</p> \n<h2>Technical Tracking Tools</h2> \n<p>When it comes to ad tracking, technical tools are a good place to start. These include options for tracking URLs from your website, ads placed in emails or sidebar displays or webpages and cookie-based tracking to unpack user behavior and fine-tune your <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/marketing-plan-template-generator\">marketing plan</a>. Let’s explore each in more detail.</p> \n<h3>Tracking URLs</h3> \n<p>A tracking URL is a normal page URL from your website with a tracking token added to the end of it. Here's an example landing page URL by itself, and with a tracking token (in bold).</p> \n<p>Regular old landing page URL:</p> \n<p><code>http://www.yourwebsite.com/your-landing-page/</code></p> \n<p>Landing page URL with a tracking token:</p> \n<p><code>http://www.yourwebsite.com/your-landing-page/<strong>?utm_campaign=test-campaign&amp;utm_source=email</strong></code></p> \n<p>As you can see, the page URL is the same in both cases, but in the second case, there's some extra stuff added to the end. This extra stuff is your tracking token, also called a UTM parameter.</p> \n<p>So how does this \"extra stuff\" help you track things, exactly?</p> \n<p>When a user clicks on a URL with a UTM parameter added to the end, it essentially sends a signal back to your ad tracking tool that the URL was clicked. The \"<span style=\"font-weight: bold;\">source=_____</span>\" bit of the tracking token can provide information about where the user clicked the link. Similarly, the \"<span style=\"font-weight: bold;\">campaign=_____</span>\" bit can be used to signal to your tracking tool that the link should be bucketed as part of a campaign.</p> \n<p>For example, if you were to run the same ad on multiple websites and wanted to know which one generated the most clicks, you could define the two different websites as sources in the UTM parameters of your links.</p> \n<p>You can learn more about tracking parameters and how they work in <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/what-are-utm-tracking-codes-ht\">this article</a>.</p> \n<h4>When to use tracking URLs:</h4> \n<p>If you're running a PPC campaign, sending an email, or putting an advertisement on another website, tracking URLs are ideal for calculating the number of visits, leads, and conversions you've generated from your hard work.</p> \n<h3>Tracking Pixels</h3> \n<p>A tracking pixel is a tiny, often transparent, 1px by 1px image that can be placed in an email, display ad, or simply on a webpage. When it loads, it sends a signal back to your tracking tool that a user has viewed the page.</p> \n<p>Tracking pixels are also capable of collecting pretty comprehensive data about a user's activity and browser configuration -- but you should only ever track information that is directly useful to your buyer's journey and will provide a better, more personalized experience for your target users.</p> \n<p>When used correctly, tracking pixels can help optimize your ads and get them in front of a receptive audience. For example, using banner ad tracking with a pixel lets you gather information about how many people just view versus actually click on your ad, which will help you determine whether or not an ad was actually successful (and worth running again).</p> \n<p>For context, here's how big a tracking pixel appears (no, that's not just a speck of dust on your screen):</p> \n<p><img alt=\"Google tracking pixel\" src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Google%20Drive%20Integration/Ad%20Tracking%20What%20It%20Is%20%26%20How%20to%20Do%20It.png?width=400&amp;name=Ad%20Tracking%20What%20It%20Is%20%26%20How%20to%20Do%20It.png\" title=\"\" width=\"400\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block; width: 400px;\"></p> \n<h4>When to use tracking pixels:</h4> \n<p>Tracking pixels are incredibly useful for tracking the success of your online campaigns through every step of your conversion path. They can give you insight into how users are interacting with your ads, and help you optimize each stage of your user journey from initial touch through final purchase.</p> \n<h3>Cookies</h3> \n<p>Cookies can help you gain insight into user behavior on your website across multiple sessions of activity. Marketers need to gain explicit consent from users before using cookies to track their activity. When explicit consent is given, cookies can be used to customize a user's experience. Here's a <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/customers/what-is-cookie-tracking\">deeper dive on cookies</a> if you want to learn more about the technical aspects of how they function.</p> \n<p>From an ad tracking perspective, cookies are the driving force behind most ad retargeting campaigns. Cookies can be used to essentially build a user profile based on someone's web activity and habits, and advertisers can leverage this profile to serve ads that align with a user's observed interests. They can also capture information about a user's browser configuration, location, and preferred language.</p> \n<h4>When to use cookies:</h4> \n<p>Cookies are ideal when you want to serve a user ads aligned with their web browsing activity, or retarget them with ads for products they've demonstrated an interest in. Cookies can also be used to create a personalized experience for users on your website based on their previous interactions with you -- for example, you could create an abandoned cart email when users put items in their cart and then leave your website.</p> \n<p>Now that we've gone over a few core solutions related to ad targeting, let's take a deeper look at how ad targeting functions on a few of the biggest ad tracking platforms, and how you can use it to make your own ad campaigns stronger and more effective.</p> \n<h2>Search and Social Ad Tracking Solutions</h2> \n<p>Brands can also boost their ad tracking ability by using tools that integrate with search tools such as Google or social media sites such as Facebook and Instagram. This type of ad tracking provides more in-depth information about user behaviors and preferences to help companies fine-tune their marketing efforts.</p> \n<h3>DoubleClick Ad Tracking</h3> \n<p>If you've ever noticed an ad for a product you viewed weeks ago following you around on the internet, it's likely the result of DoubleClick ad tracking. <a href=\"https://support.google.com/faqs/answer/2727482?hl=en\">DoubleClick</a>, which was acquired by Google in 2008, is an ad management and ad serving platform that enables marketers to run ad campaigns across multiple channels.</p> \n<p>Online publishers use DoubleClick to essentially rent out ad space on their websites, and agencies and advertisers use the product to place ads on websites where their target audiences are spending time.</p> \n<p>In 2012, Google <a href=\"https://adexchanger.com/platforms/doubleclick-no-more-google-renames-its-ad-stack/\">rebranded</a> their DoubleClick products as Google Marketing Platform (formerly DoubleClick), Google Ads (formerly Google AdWords), and Google Ad Manager (formerly DoubleClick for Publishers and DoubleClick Ad Exchange).</p> \n<p>Google ad tracking offers advertisers a number of different options when they create campaigns on the platform -- most of which rely on the use of cookies.</p> \n<p><a href=\"https://support.google.com/admanager/answer/2839090?hl=en\">According to Google</a>, \"Cookies themselves contain no personally identifiable information. Depending on the publisher’s and user’s settings, information associated with cookies used in advertising may be added to the user’s Google Account.\"</p> \n<p>These generic cookies can collect information on the time and date you viewed particular ads, the specific web pages you were on when you viewed an ad, and your IP address -- which can help the cookie infer where you're located.</p> \n<p>Although the cookies contain no personally identifiable information, <a href=\"https://thenextweb.com/google/2019/02/05/google-has-quietly-dropped-ban-on-personally-identifiable-web-tracking/\">Google can combine</a> the information it obtains via cookies with the personally identifiable information associated with your Google Account (which includes your browsing and search activity when you're logged into Google -- which, for most of us, is pretty much always).</p> \n<p>Google leverages two main types of cookies: first-party and third-party.</p> \n<p>First-party cookies are dropped (i.e., assigned to a specific user) by the owner of the website you're visiting. Information collected via first-party cookies can help publishers better understand your activity on their site and how ads are performing.</p> \n<p>Third-party cookies are dropped by an advertiser on a website where their ads are being displayed. These cookies send information back to advertisers about how their ad campaigns are performing across all the websites where their DoubleClick ads are being displayed.</p> \n<p>Over <a href=\"https://trends.builtwith.com/websitelist/Google-Adsense\">11.1 million websites</a> currently run ads as part of Google's AdSense network. If you visit a website within the network, the information collected via a DoubleClick ad tracking cookie will be pooled and leveraged by other websites and advertisers using AdSense.</p> \n<p>This consolidation of cookie information results in an extremely rich pool of data for Google advertisers, as they can keep track of what ads you're served across millions of different websites.</p> \n<p>To get started tracking ads with Google, you'll need to <a href=\"https://marketingplatform.google.com/about/\">get a Google Marketing Platform account</a>. Depending on the size of your business and your particular needs, you'll choose either an enterprise account -- which can accommodate large ad campaigns across multiple websites and mediums -- or a small business account -- with ad tracking tools more focused and specialized for early company growth.</p> \n<h3>Facebook Pixel</h3> \n<p>Advertisers on Facebook can leverage a number of different ad tracking strategies to optimize ads for their audience. Facebook's <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/facebook-pixel\">ad tracking pixel</a> is one of the more common methods for both desktop and mobile ad tracking. It functions similarly to the basic tracking pixel we outlined above, and can be used to track the path someone takes from viewing an ad, to visiting your website, to purchasing a product.</p> \n<p>When an action takes place on a page where a tracking pixel has been set up, the pixel will \"fire\" and send that information back to your Facebook Events Manager account. Information collected via the tracking pixel can also be used in the creation of custom audiences for future ad campaigns.</p> \n<p>For example, you could use data collected via a tracking pixel to create a custom ad audience targeting users who viewed a particular page on your website that implies purchase intent -- like a pricing page. We wrote an article that goes <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/facebook-pixel\">deeper into how the tracking pixel functions</a> if you want to learn more about different uses and how to set it up.</p> \n<p>Worth noting? Because Facebook owns Instagram, pixel works the same way on the photo-sharing site and will deliver the same type of insights. Collecting data from both Facebook and Instagram in tandem is a great way to pinpoint strategies that may work well on one platform but under-perform on the other. For example, longer text-driven ads may drive click-throughs on your Facebook page but fall flat on Instagram, where images drive interaction.</p> \n<h3>Additional Ad Tracking Options</h3> \n<p>While the Facebook pixel can offer advertisers valuable insights into how ads are influencing specific actions on their websites, it's not the only way to track ads on the social network.</p> \n<p>Another ad tracking option available to help improve <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/ad-management-tools\">ad management</a> is adding UTM parameters to links that appear on your ads. As we discussed above, tracking parameters use extra code on a URL to \"fire\" when a user loads the link. On Facebook, they can <a href=\"https://www.facebook.com/business/help/1016122818401732\">be used</a> in Ads Manager to better understand which ads you're running are driving which types of traffic.</p> \n<h2>It All Adds Up: Improving Impact with Ad Tracking</h2> \n<p>Competitive Ad tracking can help your business see how your marketing efforts and campaigns are performing at scale. This starts with URL, pixel, and cookie tracking to explore how users are interacting with your brand. It’s bolstered by search-focused and social-focused tools that help your brand discover where ads are working, where they come up short, and where they need to improve to increase user engagement and drive sales conversions.</p> \n<p><em>Editor's note: This post was originally published in July 2019 and has been updated for comprehensiveness.</em></p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=46d72524-f4a7-44e9-9af0-935be9bb3891&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; \" alt=\"Improve your website with effective technical SEO. href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/blog/tabid/6307/bid/33924/how-to-develop-a-website-redesign-strategy-that-guarantees-results-free-template.aspx\">website redesign</a> to improve lead generation, and you're responsible for managing the project.</p> \n<p></p> \n<p>Naturally, one of the first questions you ask is, \"How much is this website redesign <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/website/how-much-website-cost\">going to cost</a>?\"</p> \n<p>The answer, of course, is \"it depends.\" Are you simply switching to a new template and adding some new CTAs, or are you migrating your entire website to a new platform?</p> \n<p>If only there were a way to organize your answers to all of these questions — a place where you could enter in estimated costs for all of your line items, and then compare your projected marketing budget to what you actually end up spending. Good news: Marketing budget templates can help.</p> \n<a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=3e2abb94-93d9-4cf5-bd8e-6a96ecc14270&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; margin: 0 auto; display: block; margin-top: 20px; margin-bottom: 20px\" alt=\"Click here to download 8 free marketing budget templates.\" src=\"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/3e2abb94-93d9-4cf5-bd8e-6a96ecc14270.png\" align=\"middle\"></a> \n<p>Included in our <a href=\"https://offers.hubspot.com/marketing-budget-templates\">eight marketing budget templates bundle</a> is a template to manage your website redesign ... as well as templates for both Excel and Google Sheets to help you track your content budget, paid advertising budget, event budget, and more.</p> \n<p>Additionally, in this guide, we discuss how to manage your entire marketing budget from start to finish.</p> \n<p></p> \n<a></a> \n<p></p> \n<h3>Marketing Budget for Small Business</h3> \n<p>Marketing budgets are especially important for small businesses. Small business owners may lack the experience drawing up budgets; moreover, it's critical that these companies keep costs as low and lean as possible as they scale.</p> \n<p>Ironically, you need marketing to scale. Without it, it's hard to sell your products and services. In addition to the budgeting templates provided below, check out some of our <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/free-content-creation-templates\">free offers</a> and <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/free-online-marketing-classes\">courses</a> to mitigate your company's marketing costs.</p> \n<p>Yet marketing budgets can be difficult to establish for companies of all sizes.</p> \n<h3>How much should a company spend on marketing?</h3> \n<p>Well, <a href=\"https://insights.digitalmediasolutions.com/articles/digital-spending-2020\">digital media makes up more than half</a> of both U.S. and global advertising spend. This includes initiatives that cater to audiences on desktop computers, search engines, video streaming platforms, social media, and mobile devices.</p> \n<p>Given the success marketers have seen in it, you might consider planning to spend at least half of your marketing budget on some of these digital channels.</p> \n<p>Let's talk about other ways to allocate your marketing budget.</p> \n<p></p> \n<a></a> \n<p></p> \n<p>As you build a budget, there are a few items you'll want to keep in mind when planning your marketing budget allocation.</p> \n<h3>Marketing Cost Examples</h3> \n<h4>1. Software</h4> \n<p>When it comes to digital and even print media, you may need software to create your marketing campaigns or handle your daily processes. There’s a <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/marketing-tools\">marketing tool</a> for just about any task you can think of, but they are generally broken down into the following categories:</p> \n<ul> \n <li><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/sales/benefits-of-crm\">Customer relationship management </a>(CRM)</li> \n <li><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/online-marketing-tools\">Online advertising</a></li> \n <li><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/best-social-media-management-tools\">Social media</a></li> \n <li><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/content-creation\">Content creation</a> and <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/website/free-web-design-tools-2020\">design</a></li> \n <li><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/event-marketing\">Event marketing</a></li> \n <li><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/lead-generation-tools\">Lead capture and lead generation</a></li> \n <li><a href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/marketing-automation-information\">Marketing automation</a></li> \n <li><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/content-marketing-analytics\">Data reporting and analytics</a></li> \n <li><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/website/digital-asset-management\">Digital asset management</a></li> \n <li><a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/collaboration-tools\">Team collaboration</a></li> \n</ul> \n<p>The costs of these tools can quickly add up, so it’s worth it to try out the <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/marketing-tools\">free options</a> until you’re ready to commit to a tool your team loves.</p> \n<h4>2. Freelancers</h4> \n<p>If you have a temporary campaign or want to test out a new marketing strategy, you might want to <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/find-manage-freelancers\">hire a short-term freelancer</a> before bringing on a full-timer.</p> \n<p>Reach out to your network for recommendations or consider using a site like UpWork. Freelancers typically charge an hourly rate, so be sure to examine your budget before hiring.</p> \n<h4>3. New Personnel</h4> \n<p>When you do hire full-time employees, you'll want to budget costs including their computer, technology, benefits, and onboarding-related needs. According to research from <a href=\"https://www.zippia.com/advice/cost-of-hiring-statistics-average-cost-per-hire/#Cost_Per_Hire_Demographic_Statistics\">Zippia</a>, the average cost of hiring a new employee is $4,425.</p> \n<h4>4. Advertising</h4> \n<p>Budget how much money you'll spend on paid opportunities such as physical ads, native ads, sponsored content, search engine ads, and social media promotions.</p> Most businesses will benefit from some form of online advertising whether via social media platforms, search engine, or native ads. \n<a href=\"https://www.statista.com/statistics/273018/number-of-internet-users-worldwide/\">Statista</a> estimates there were an estimated 4.9 billion internet users worldwide as of 2021. If you’re not advertising online, you're missing out.\n<br> \n<h4>5. Content Creation</h4> \n<p>When you create content such as videos, photos, or even blog posts, you'll need to put paid time into it.</p> \n<p>Content marketing brings in <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/content-creation\">3X </a>as many leads as traditional options, so it’s worth dedicating funds to this area. Budget how much money will go into creating this content so you can adjust accordingly based on its return on investment.</p> \n<p>Now that you know more about what to include in your budget, let’s look at how to those funds are spent.</p> \n<p></p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center; font-style: italic; font-size: 12px;\"><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Marketing%20budget%20breakdown.jpg?width=650&amp;name=Marketing%20budget%20breakdown.jpg\" alt=\"Marketing budget breakdown\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\" width=\"650\"><a href=\"https://www.gartner.com/en/marketing/research/annual-cmo-spend-survey-research\">Image Source</a></p> \n<p>If you’re not sure where to start with budget allocation, a good guideline to follow is the 70-20-10 rule. Using this as a benchmark:</p> \n<ul> \n <li>70% of your budget is allocated toward strategies you know work well</li> \n <li>20% of your budget is allocated toward new strategies aimed at helping you grow</li> \n <li>10% of your budget is allocated toward experimental strategies</li> \n</ul> \n<h3>Marketing Cost Example</h3> \n<p>Let’s say your business has a marketing budget of $10,000. The budget allocation may look like this:</p> \n<ul> \n <li>$7,000 towards a CRM or other software you love, successful paid search campaigns, social media marketing</li> \n <li>$2,000 towards marketing a new product, feature, or service you’re testing</li> \n <li>$1,000 towards testing sponsored content</li> \n</ul> \n<h3>Allocation by Channel</h3> \n<p>How you allocate your budget per channel depends on your company’s particular goals, so there is no hard and fast rule. However, the chart below from <a href=\"https://www.statista.com/statistics/1222784/marketing-budget-share-channel/\">Statista</a> can give you a ballpark idea as it illustrates the share of marketing budgets from large companies across North America, the UK, Germany, and France.</p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center; font-style: italic; font-size: 12px;\"><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Marketing%20budget%20by%20channel%20Statista.jpg?width=650&amp;name=Marketing%20budget%20by%20channel%20Statista.jpg\" alt=\"Marketing budget cost by channel \" width=\"650\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\"><a href=\"https://www.statista.com/statistics/1222784/marketing-budget-share-channel/\">Image Source</a></p> \n<p>Organized by channel, you can see that the top spots belong to social marketing, digital advertising, and search engine optimization (SEO).</p> \n<p>By 2023, it's estimated that marketers will spend more than <a href=\"https://www.emarketer.com/content/digital-ad-spending-outlook-blows-past-previous-forecasts\">$52 billion</a> on ads across websites or apps that are mainly eCommerce-focused. Let’s look at some examples of how these digital marketing costs apply to your budget.</p> \n<h4>Paid Search Advertising</h4> \n<p>You’re probably familiar with the ads at the top of a Google results page that show up above the list of search results. Those are a form of paid advertising called <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/ppc\">pay-per-click (PPC)</a>. You can <a href=\"https://ads.google.com/home/campaigns/search-ads/\">create and run ads on Google</a>, and each time someone clicks, you pay. The cost-per-click (CPC) can range anywhere from a few cents to a few dollars. You can use Google’s <a href=\"https://support.google.com/google-ads/answer/7337243\">keyword planner</a> to help estimate costs.</p> \n<p>With this method, you only pay for clicks you receive. So even if you’ve set aside a budget of $2,000, your campaign may only generate $1,500 worth of clicks.</p> \n<h4>Social Media</h4> \n<p>Like Google Ads, social media platforms have advertising programs based on the PPC model, but also charge by impressions. The CPC of running a paid social campaign varies depending on the platform of choice, but ranges from a few cents to a several dollars.</p> \n<p>Some companies may opt to hire an agency to run their campaigns and to create a social media strategy. Outsourcing this function is more expensive and can cost anywhere from <a href=\"https://www.digitalstand.com/blog/social-media-agency-charges\">$2,000 to $20,000</a> per month.</p> \n<h4>Content Marketing</h4> \n<p>Having a brand blog is a great way to get into content marketing, especially if you have in-house staff tasked with keeping it updated. Instead of a blog, you may be more interested in creating case studies, eBooks, videos or guides. They’re all designed to promote your brand and attract new customers.</p> \n<p>Content marketing costs vary widely based on what your goals are and area of focus. Hiring outside consultants or agencies to handle content marketing for you can range from <a href=\"https://www.webfx.com/content-marketing/pricing/\">$2,000 to $10,000</a> per month for small to medium-sized businesses. While it isn’t cheap, paying an agency to handle this task will free up your team’s time to work on other projects and may yield better results than going solo.</p> \n<h4>Email Marketing</h4> \n<p>Email marketing is a must-have for businesses, especially online retailers. With a customer acquisition rate <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/email-marketing-guide\">40X more effective</a> than Facebook and Twitter combined, it’s no surprise why this tried and true method is a staple in most marketing budgets. Email marketing also provides higher ROI as you’re connecting with people already interested in your brand.</p> \n<p>Email marketing costs depend on the size of your business, your goals, and chosen software or platform. Hiring an outside firm to handle these efforts will cost significantly more than doing it yourself.</p> \n<h4>Search Engine Optimization</h4> \n<p>SEO aids marketing efforts by improving your webpages so that they show up in search engines like Google. The more often your website comes up in search, the more potential customers will see it and hopefully visit your website.</p> \n<p>If you don’t have staff to handle your SEO needs in-house you may need to work with an agency. Depending on what your business needs are, this can cost thousands per month.</p> \n<p>While the marketing channel choices can seem endless, don't feel pressured to use all of them. Every business is different and you should prioritize putting funds toward the methods that best suit your needs.</p> \n<a></a> \n<p></p> \n<p>Spreadsheet knowledge <em>alone</em> won't help you understand how you'll spend your marketing money this year. Creating a sound marketing budget starts with knowing what purpose this budget will serve and which marketing teams it will represent.</p> \n<h3>1. Know your buyer's journey.</h3> \n<p>Your <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/sales/what-is-the-buyers-journey\">buyer's journey</a> is the steps your audience takes as they 'journey' from prospect to paying customer. Knowing your buyer's journey allows you to understand how your audience interacts with your marketing — and where to set your goals <em>and</em> budget to better reach your customers.</p> \n<p>Ask yourself these questions as you define your buyer's journey:</p> \n<ul> \n <li>How do your leads and customers typically discover your products?</li> \n <li>What do they need to know before they make a purchase?</li> \n <li>How many site visits do you see per month?</li> \n <li>How many leads are you generating per month, and how many of these convert to paying customers?</li> \n <li>What is the cost of generating new leads and then converting them to customers?</li> \n <li>What's the typical value/revenue of each lead?</li> \n</ul> \n<p>This process should point out what marketing tactics are (and aren't working), where you should alter your marketing goals, and where you can focus your marketing budget.</p> \n<h3>2. Align your budget with your marketing goals.</h3> \n<p>What you spend and where you spend it will depend on what you're trying to accomplish.</p> \n<p>So, when starting to create your marketing budget, make sure you're only spending money on the things required by your current marketing goals — goals set based on your audience and their journey from prospect to customer. These could include:</p> \n<ul> \n <li>Display ads <strong>to promote a new product</strong> you're launching this year.</li> \n <li>Sponsored social media posts <strong>to generate followers</strong> on your new Facebook page.</li> \n <li>Paid search engine ads <strong>to drive traffic (and purchases)</strong> to a specific product page.</li> \n <li>Contract bloggers <strong>to get more organic search traffic</strong> to your company's website.</li> \n</ul> \n<p>Former Demand Generation Marketer at HubSpot and current Head of Marketing at Tailscale, <a href=\"https://www.linkedin.com/in/jessicacwebb\">Jessica Webb Kennedy</a>, says this about how your costs can change when focusing on lead generation vs. lead conversion: \"The majority of the money you spend on paid efforts is usually calculated based on the volume of clicks or impressions. Because of this, you'll often want to put more budget toward campaigns with higher-volume offers and audiences.\"</p> \n<p>\"For example, a tweet or Facebook ad promoting a lead generation offer that leans more top of the funnel will likely receive more clicks than something that falls more toward the middle or bottom of the funnel,\" she explains.</p> \n<p>Your paid advertising costs will also change depending on how wide of an audience you are attempting to reach.</p> \n<p>\"You can look at Twitter advertising as an example,\" Webb says. \"You have to option to target your campaigns based on users' interests or keywords searched for. Interests are a much broader category, whereas smaller pockets of users are searching for any given keyword, therefore your interests-based audience is going to be much larger and require a larger budget.\"</p> \n<h3>3. Beware of hidden marketing costs.</h3> \n<p>One of the great advantages to having and maintaining a budget spreadsheet is that it helps you avoid those end-of-the-quarter or end-of-the-year freak-outs when you realize, \"Whoa … what did I spend all that money on?\"</p> \n<p>In many cases, unanticipated costs can force marketers to fork over cash that they didn't plan on spending. Product marketing offers a perfect example. According to former HubSpot VP of Marketing and current CMO at The Wanderlust Group, <a href=\"https://www.linkedin.com/in/meghankeaney\">Meghan Keaney Anderson</a>, it's easy to forget that successfully marketing your products and services requires more than just promotion.</p> \n<p>\"When people allocate budget for product marketing, they tend to think in terms of product launches and promotional activities,\" Anderson explains.</p> \n<p>\"That's certainly an important part of it, but another area of focus to remember is setting aside resources to conduct research and message testing long before the product ever goes to market. Having conversations with customers about the pain points your product will ultimately address is critical to shaping the messaging and having a successful launch.\"</p> \n<h3>4. Remember where your priorities lie.</h3> \n<p>Marketing is overflowing with add-ons and extras, upsells, and \"premium\" versions. One of the best ways to assess what's nice to have versus what's absolutely necessary is to (you guessed it) organize all of your expenses.</p> \n<p>By keeping tabs on where your budget is being allocated, and cross-checking that spending with the results you're getting, it will be much easier to figure out what should keep getting budget and what should get kicked to the curb.</p> \n<p>For example, let's look to the world of public relations. In PR, there are countless tools to which you can allocate budget, which could leave you overspending where it doesn't matter — and underspending where it does.</p> \n<p>\"Tools abound to help PR practitioners not only create and distribute great content and find and target key stakeholders, but to ultimately measure reach and effectiveness,\" says <a href=\"https://www.linkedin.com/in/nathanieleberle\">Nathaniel Eberle</a>, HubSpot's former Director of PR &amp; Brand and GoTo’s current VP of Global Brand &amp; Creative Management.</p> \n<p>\"The key is making sure you're laser-focused on who you're setting out to reach and influence, then ensuring that your budget supports how they'll most likely want to receive (and share) your key messages.</p> \n<p>\"As the media and digital landscape evolves at breakneck speed, continually reassessing the tools, services, and programs you're employing is a great way to determine real-time ROI of your overall spend. Today's measurement tool may be worthless to you tomorrow.\"</p> \n<h3>5. Spend your budget smartly.</h3> \n<p>When you open up these budget templates and check out all the various expenses detailed in them, don't fret if you can't tick every box. I'm not advocating for an \"always spend more\" approach to marketing.</p> \n<p>I'm advocating for an \"always spend smart\" approach. The expenses listed out aren't mandatory — they're just meant to guide your thinking and to help ensure that you haven't overlooked any hidden costs.</p> \n<h3>6. Prepare to measure ROI.</h3> \n<p>When you put a certain amount of money into a certain area, you'll want to determine if your budgeting helped you or hurt you as you plan out future budgets. The best way to do this is by measuring ROI — or return on investment.</p> \n<p>If the money you spend on one item results in your company making more in return, you may want to increase budget in the next year. If your money went nowhere, you should examine your budget.</p> \n<a></a> \n<h2>8 Marketing Budget Templates You Need to Manage Your Marketing Spend</h2> \n<p>With the <em>8 Free Budget Planner Templates to Manage Your Marketing Spend</em><em>,</em> you'll be able to manage all of the moving pieces of your budget at a monthly and quarterly level.</p> \n<p>Use the Excel version of the templates to keep all of your budgets in one place. When you download the zip file, you'll find a separate file for each marketing team, as well as a <em>Master Budget Template</em> to maintain a high-level view of your overall expenses.</p> \n<p>Interested in sharing your marketing budget across a larger team? Try the<strong> Google Sheets version of our templates</strong> to share access with other Gmail users. For the Google Sheets templates, each team budget is found in a separate tab of the same Google Sheet.</p> \n<p>No matter which version you choose, each budget is optimized with the same line items, tips, and graphs. Read on to learn how to use each budget template.</p> \n<h3>1. Master Marketing Budget Template</h3> \n<p><em><a href=\"https://offers.hubspot.com/marketing-budget-templates\"><strong>Download the Master Marketing Budget Template here.</strong></a></em></p> \n<p>While it's helpful to have individual budget templates for specific marketing departments and activities, it's also nice to be able to take a step back and see the bigger picture.</p> \n<p>The <em>Master Marketing Budget Template</em> lets you do just that: It's the place where you can collect the totals from the other seven templates in the bundle and see all of your expenses in one place.</p> \n<h3><a href=\"https://offers.hubspot.com/marketing-budget-templates\"><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Screen%20Shot%202021-05-18%20at%2010.12.17%20AM.png?width=650&amp;name=Screen%20Shot%202021-05-18%20at%2010.12.17%20AM.png\" alt=\"master marketing budget template\" width=\"650\" style=\"display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;\"></a></h3> \n<h3>2. Product Marketing Budget Template</h3> \n<p><em><a href=\"https://offers.hubspot.com/marketing-budget-templates\"><strong>Download the Product Marketing Budget Template here.</strong></a></em></p> \n<p>This template will guide you step-by-step through the process of budgeting for a product launch. From determining product/market fit, to running user testing sessions, to promoting your finished product, our <em>Product Marketing Budget Template</em> will help ensure you don't overlook any important expenses.</p> \n<p><a href=\"https://offers.hubspot.com/marketing-budget-templates\"><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Screen%20Shot%202021-05-18%20at%2010.03.53%20AM.png?width=650&amp;name=Screen%20Shot%202021-05-18%20at%2010.03.53%20AM.png\" alt=\"product marketing budget template\" width=\"650\" style=\"display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;\"></a></p> \n<h3>3. Content Budget Template</h3> \n<p><em><a href=\"https://offers.hubspot.com/marketing-budget-templates\"><strong>Download the Content Budget Template here.</strong></a></em></p> \n<p>The budget required for creating and promoting content can vary greatly from organization to organization. For example, while some organizations keep most of their content operations in-house, others rely more heavily on freelancers and contractors. And while some use many different software products, publishing tools, and services, others take a much simpler approach.</p> \n<p>Our <em>Content Budget Template </em>is designed to cover as many content-related bases as possible. So, if you see any expenses listed that don't apply to <em>your</em> organization, go ahead and delete them. (That's the beauty of Excel spreadsheets: You can customize them to your specific needs.)</p> \n<h3><a href=\"https://offers.hubspot.com/marketing-budget-templates\"><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Screen%20Shot%202021-05-18%20at%2010.03.40%20AM-1.png?width=650&amp;name=Screen%20Shot%202021-05-18%20at%2010.03.40%20AM-1.png\" alt=\"content budget template\" width=\"650\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\"></a>4. Paid Advertising Budget Template</h3> \n<p><em><a href=\"https://offers.hubspot.com/marketing-budget-templates\"><strong>Download the Paid Advertising Budget Template here.</strong></a></em></p> \n<p>Paid advertising: Does it <em>really</em> qualify as an inbound marketing tactic/channel? That is a loaded question, my friends, and one that I don't have room to answer in-depth in this post.</p> \n<p>What I can tell you for sure is that <a href=\"https://offers.hubspot.com/inboundy-outbound-how-to-do-traditional-marketing-inbound-way\">you can do paid advertising in an \"inboundy\" way</a> — i.e. by targeting specific buyer personas and using paid advertising as a supplement to your organic efforts to help drive awareness and conversion opportunities.</p> \n<p>Measuring the effectiveness of your paid advertising campaigns is also paramount to doing things the inbound way. Using our <em>Paid Advertising Budget Template</em>, you can keep tabs on your monthly (and quarterly) ad spending, and then cross-reference the amounts with your lead-generation metrics to determine your cost-per-lead.</p> \n<p><a href=\"https://offers.hubspot.com/marketing-budget-templates\"><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Screen%20Shot%202021-05-18%20at%2010.02.44%20AM.png?width=650&amp;name=Screen%20Shot%202021-05-18%20at%2010.02.44%20AM.png\" alt=\"advertising budget template\" width=\"650\" style=\"display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;\"></a></p> \n<h3>5. Public Relations Budget Template</h3> \n<p><em><a href=\"https://offers.hubspot.com/marketing-budget-templates\"><strong>Download the Public Relations Budget Template here.</strong></a></em></p> \n<p>Public relations expenses amount to more than just paying for press releases. From reputation monitoring software, to traveling (e.g., to events and trade shows), to applying for awards, there are many PR costs that can be all too easy to overlook.</p> \n<p>To ensure you're accounting for all of your organization's PR-related expenses, check out our <em>Public Relations Budget Template</em>.</p> \n<h3>6. Branding &amp; Creative Budget Template</h3> \n<p><em><a href=\"https://offers.hubspot.com/marketing-budget-templates\"><strong>Download the Creative Budget Template here.</strong></a></em></p> \n<p>In order to produce high-quality, innovative graphics, videos, and other content, the branding and creative teams of today need more than just Photoshop ... a lot more. One of the largest — and often most overlooked — expenses is storage.</p> \n<p>If your organization is producing a lot of video, storage is especially important. Because as it turns out, when budgeting for video storage, you shouldn't be thinking on a megabyte (MB) or even a gigabyte (GB) scale, but on a terabyte (TB) scale. FYI: 1 terabyte = 1 trillion bytes. You can keep track of all your storage costs (and other branding and creative costs) using our free template.</p> \n<p><a href=\"https://offers.hubspot.com/marketing-budget-templates\"><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Screen%20Shot%202021-05-18%20at%2010.01.58%20AM.png?width=650&amp;name=Screen%20Shot%202021-05-18%20at%2010.01.58%20AM.png\" alt=\"branding creative budget template\" width=\"650\" style=\"display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;\"></a></p> \n<h3>7. Website Redesign Budget Template</h3> \n<p><em><a href=\"https://offers.hubspot.com/marketing-budget-templates\"><strong>Download the Website Redesign Budget Template here.</strong></a></em></p> \n<p>Budgeting for a website redesign can be seriously tricky. With so many moving pieces to consider, there is a lot of room for underestimating or miscalculating costs. We created our <em>Website Redesign Budget Template</em> so you can keep all of your redesign-related expenses in one convenient location.</p> \n<p>Unsure if your current website is right for a redesign? Check out this HubSpot research report: <em><a href=\"https://offers.hubspot.com/does-your-website-make-the-grade\">Does Your Website Make the Grade? Chances Are, It's Barely Passing</a></em>.</p> \n<p><a href=\"https://offers.hubspot.com/marketing-budget-templates\"><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Screen%20Shot%202021-05-18%20at%2010.01.11%20AM.png?width=650&amp;name=Screen%20Shot%202021-05-18%20at%2010.01.11%20AM.png\" alt=\"budget for website redesign\" width=\"650\" style=\"display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;\"></a></p> \n<h3>8. Event Budget Template</h3> \n<p><em><a href=\"https://offers.hubspot.com/marketing-budget-templates\"><strong>Download the Event Budget Template here.</strong></a></em></p> \n<p>When planning an event, the associated costs can seem obvious at first. There's the venue to consider, of course. And the P.A. system and microphones. And then the costs associated with booking and bringing in presenters/performers. That's pretty much it, right?</p> \n<p>Wrong.</p> \n<p>For example, does the venue come with tables/chairs, or will you have to rent those separately? Do you want your attendees to wear name tags, and if so, will you be printing out the name tags ahead of time or will attendees be writing their own names on blank tags?</p> \n<p>If the latter, have you factored in the pens or markers you'll need to accommodate that? As you can see, planning for an event can lead you down many rabbit holes.</p> \n<p>Use our <em>Event Budget Template</em> to stay organized.</p> \n<p><a href=\"https://offers.hubspot.com/marketing-budget-templates\"><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Screen%20Shot%202021-05-18%20at%2010.01.01%20AM.png?width=650&amp;name=Screen%20Shot%202021-05-18%20at%2010.01.01%20AM.png\" alt=\"event budget templates\" width=\"650\" style=\"display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;\"></a></p> \n<a></a> \n<h2>Sample Marketing Budget</h2> \n<p>With your chosen template downloaded, it's time to consider which digital channels to allot a budget for. Hint: There's no right answer — it'll depend on the market research you do to figure out where your specific audience spends most of its time.</p> \n<p>If you find your buyer prefers learning and consuming content in the form of video, for example, you might invest more of your money in <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/youtube-video-advertising-guide\">YouTube advertising</a>.</p> \n<h3>Advertising Budget Example</h3> \n<p>Here's a small sample budget for a quarter's worth of expenses by a hypothetical company that has decided to invest heavily in video marketing. This template was created using the Master Budget Template, the first template listed in the section above.</p> \n<p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/sample-marketing-budget-1.jpg?width=650&amp;name=sample-marketing-budget-1.jpg\" alt=\"Sample marketing budget showing a video advertising investment that exceeds budget by $2,420.\" width=\"650\" style=\"width: 650px; display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;\"></p> \n<p>Based on the figures above, video advertising's total expenses for the quarter exceeded budget by $20, while full-time recruitment's total expenses exceeded budget by $2,400. This means the company is trending over budget for the first three months of the year.</p> \n<p>Why might this happen? Perhaps a pay-per-click (PPC) campaign on YouTube received more clicks by viewers than expected, and a sharp video-savvy job candidate negotiated a higher salary.</p> \n<p>Based on the difference between this company's planned spend and actual spend, their budget template produced the following graph:<br><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/sample-marketing-budget-graph.jpg?width=650&amp;name=sample-marketing-budget-graph.jpg\" alt=\"sample marketing budget graph\" width=\"650\" style=\"display: block; margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto;\"></p> \n<h2>Create a Marketing Budget That Prioritizes Your Goals</h2> \n<p>A well-thought out marketing budget serves as roadmap to your team's success. Revisit the buyer’s journey, flesh out your goals, and stay away from tempting add-ons that are not in line with your marketing priorities.</p> \n<p>Go now, and plan wisely — your marketing staff is counting on you.</p> \n<p><em>Editor's Note: This blog post was originally published in December 2015 and has been updated for comprehensiveness.</em></p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" /blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Screen%20Shot%202021-05-18%20at%2010.01.11%20AM.png?width=650&name=Screen%20Shot%202021-05-18%20at%2010.01.11%20AM.png":null,"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Screen%20Shot%202021-05-18%20at%2010.01.01%20AM.png?width=650&name=Screen%20Shot%202021-05-18%20at%2010.01.01%20AM.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn55@2020_4/2022/03/14/08-15-10-955_d7bac4e403dece73.webp","https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/sample-marketing-budget-1.jpg?width=650&name=sample-marketing-budget-1.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn86@2020_5/2022/03/14/08-15-10-090_77d357d064f65fd1.webp","https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/sample-marketing-budget-graph.jpg?width=650&name=sample-marketing-budget-graph.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx5oss/cdn10@2020_4/2022/03/14/08-15-15-413_d8c995adb665e7c2.webp","https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/fec839c8-058f-4d11-8943-c7e0c554fa27.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx12/cdn18@2020_3/2022/03/14/08-15-13-433_af961930029e625f.webp","https://track.hubspot.com/__ptq.gif?a=53&k=14&r=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.hubspot.com%2Fmarketing%2Fhow-to-manage-marketing-budget-free-budget-templates&bu=https%253A%252F%252Fblog.hubspot.com%252Fmarketing&bvt=rss":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn14@2020_4/2022/03/14/08-15-10-897_5c67a242a5ff4c0e.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1647245705115},{"createdTime":"2022-03-14 16:15:05","updatedTime":"2022-03-14 16:15:05","title":"How to Run an Effective Vetting Process for Candidates in 2022","link":"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/vetting-process","description":"<p>Imagine you're a hiring manager and put up an ad for a role. After a lengthy process, you hire someone you think is a great fit.</p> \n<p>Except, reality sets in a few weeks later when you realize they were a bad hire and you have the start all over again. A robust vetting process would help you avoid this costly mistake.</p> \n<p>However, it's not enough to come up with a process, you have to make sure it's inclusive, fair, and efficient. Let's show you how.</p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=c42148d7-13dd-4c38-b907-cff1602ee62f&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; margin: 0 auto; display: block; margin-top: 20px; margin-bottom: 20px\" alt=\"→ Click here to download our free guide to hiring and training a team of  all-stars [Free Ebook].\" src=\"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/c42148d7-13dd-4c38-b907-cff1602ee62f.png\" align=\"middle\"></a></p> \n<p></p> \n<p>Hiring the wrong employee can cost companies hundreds of thousands of dollars. Back in 2016, The U.S. Department of Labor estimated this cost was close to 30% of the former employee's first-year earnings.</p> \n<p>Today, that figure could be even higher.</p> \n<p>Undoubtedly, recruiting and hiring candidates is an expensive and time-consuming process. This is on top of figuring out which candidates are <em>most</em> qualified to succeed at your company for the long haul.</p> \n<p>A vetting process should include a few critical elements. Let's cover how to run an effective vetting process that's efficient and free of bias as possible.</p> \n<h2>How long does the vetting process take?</h2> \n<p>The vetting process can take anywhere from a few days to a few weeks depending on what your process looks like, the seniority level for the role, and the industry.</p> \n<p>For instance, a role at the Federal Bureau of Investigation likely has a much longer vetting process than one at a SaaS company. The FBI likely conducts in-depth background checks beyond a candidate's criminal background whereas a SaaS company may focus the bulk of its vetting process on technical proficiency.</p> \n<p>Over time, your company will start compiling data on how long the process takes based on the factors mentioned above and build its strategy based on that.</p> \n<p></p> \n<h3>1. Write an accurate job description.</h3> \n<p>Your vetting process will be easier start-to-finish if you take the time to write an accurate and compelling job description.</p> \n<p>I spoke to <a href=\"https://ie.linkedin.com/in/clairebmccarthy\">Claire McCarthy</a>, team lead in sales recruiting, who told me the job description can help both you and the candidate ensure a mutually beneficial fit from the start.</p> \n<p>\"We have pretty comprehensive job descriptions and we want candidates to take the time to read them and ensure the role is a good match for their background and skillset, as well as their long-term goals,\" she said.</p> \n<p>McCarthy adds that it's valuable to focus on attributes when creating your job description.</p> \n<p>\"For instance, for a sales role, we might list 'customer-first mentality' as a requirement,\" she said.</p> \n<p>In addition, craft your description to attract a wide pool of diverse applicants, since diverse teams perform better, and come up with more innovative ideas.</p> \n<p>This is important because a<a href=\"https://hbr.org/2014/08/why-women-dont-apply-for-jobs-unless-theyre-100-qualified\"> </a><a href=\"https://hbr.org/2014/08/why-women-dont-apply-for-jobs-unless-theyre-100-qualified\">Hewlett Packard internal report found</a> that women historically won't apply for a job unless they meet all the qualifications, while most men will apply if they meet only 60% of them.</p> \n<p>However, it doesn't only affect candidates from a gender perspective. Racism, ableism, and ageism can also impact the hiring process – and it all starts with your job description.</p> \n<p>To do so, you can rely on tools like <a href=\"https://textio.com/\">Textio</a>, which help you identify and remove implicit and explicit biased language from your job description.</p> \n<p>The goal is to use inclusive language that welcomes and attracts a diverse range of talent.</p> \n<p>Take a look at the <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/marketing-job-descriptions\">marketing job descriptions</a> you should recruit and hire to have an all-star team.</p> \n<h3>2. Leverage software to review candidates' application materials.</h3> \n<p>A vetting process should allow you to filter out candidates who don't have the skills necessary to succeed in the role. To do this, start by vetting the applicant's <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/how-to-write-a-resume\">resume</a>, cover letter, and other application materials they've submitted for review.</p> \n<p>Additionally, a vetting process can support your diversity and inclusion initiative by ensuring your HR team remains fair and unbiased when evaluating potential candidates.</p> \n<p>For instance, you might implement a blind search system in which resumes are scanned by software, such as <a href=\"https://www.greenhouse.io/\">Greenhouse</a>.</p> \n<p>By ensuring your resumes are automatically sorted based on skill, you're circumventing some of the unintentional biases that might lead your HR employees to make unfair judgments.</p> \n<h3>3. Use video interviews prior to phone calls.</h3> \n<p>There are certain questions you can ask to decipher whether or not a candidate has the correct skills for the role.</p> \n<p>You don't want your recruiters spending valuable time on phone calls when you can just as easily collect that information another way.</p> \n<p>At HubSpot, our hiring process includes video interviews, in which candidates must answer a series of questions and submit their recorded responses. The caveat here is that they must answer each question within a minute and they won't know what the questions are ahead of time.</p> \n<p>\"We do this for high volume roles, and use the video interview as a qualifier for whether or not the candidate moves forward with a phone interview,\" said McCarthy.</p> \n<p>Consider using video interviews to limit the amount of phone calls your HR team needs to make each day.</p> \n<h3>4. Evaluate candidates' qualifications using additional assessment tools.</h3> \n<p>To evaluate whether your candidate will succeed in the role, consider offering initial assessments.</p> \n<p>As a HubSpot writer, I was asked to write a blog post from scratch using one of HubSpot's prompt topics before being invited for an interview. This makes sense – why waste your time, and your candidate's time, if they don't have the skills you're looking for?</p> \n<p>From the candidate's perspective, it allows them to get a taste of what the role requires and show off why they're right for it.</p> \n<p>You might consider offering role plays for customer-facing positions, case studies for functional roles, or coding assessments for engineering positions.</p> \n<h3>5. Trust the process.</h3> \n<p>The point of having a process is to ensure consistency and promote fairness.</p> \n<p>This means across all tools and software you utilize just as much as the steps you follow.</p> \n<p>Ultimately, a vetting process is only effective if it's consistent and replicable.</p> \n<p>\"A vetting process is about establishing a process at the beginning and sticking to it,\" said McCarthy. \"Additionally, it's important to use a vetting process to operationalize how we review candidates and decide which ones are most qualified to move forward to next steps.\"</p> \n<p>Using these five tactics will mitigate the time and money your HR team spends on recruitment in 2022 while ensuring you hire the best applicants – a win all around.</p> \n<em>Editor's Note: This post was originally published in January 2019 and has been updated for comprehensiveness.&nbsp;</em>\n<br> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=20fe7a4f-8bfb-4924-9046-ef5a2f3f3c33&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; \" alt=\"New Call-to-action\" src=\"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/20fe7a4f-8bfb-4924-9046-ef5a2f3f3c33.png\"></a> </p>  \n<img src=\"https://track.hubspot.com/__ptq.gif?a=53&amp;k=14&amp;r=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.hubspot.com%2Fmarketing%2Fvetting-process&amp;bu=https%253A%252F%252Fblog.hubspot.com%252Fmarketing&amp;bvt=rss\" alt=\"\" width=\"1\" height=\"1\" style=\"min-height:1px!important;width:1px!important;border-width:0!important;margin-top:0!important;margin-bottom:0!important;margin-right:0!important;margin-left:0!important;padding-top:0!important;padding-bottom:0!important;padding-right:0!important;padding-left:0!important; \">","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Wed, 23 Feb 2022 12:00:00 +0000","feedId":54,"bgimg":"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/c42148d7-13dd-4c38-b907-cff1602ee62f.png","linkMd5":"30588118e842c8415a4177c0c867f8ca","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn44@2020_5/2022/03/14/08-15-05-897_83b23746ffd9fffb.webp","destWidth":840,"destHeight":59,"sourceBytes":8139,"destBytes":13774,"author":"Caroline Forsey","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/c42148d7-13dd-4c38-b907-cff1602ee62f.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn44@2020_5/2022/03/14/08-15-05-897_83b23746ffd9fffb.webp","https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/20fe7a4f-8bfb-4924-9046-ef5a2f3f3c33.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx11/cdn28@2020_2/2022/03/14/08-15-10-558_e4e09f6d3d81a2f6.webp","https://track.hubspot.com/__ptq.gif?a=53&k=14&r=https%3A%2F%2Fblog.hubspot.com%2Fmarketing%2Fvetting-process&bu=https%253A%252F%252Fblog.hubspot.com%252Fmarketing&bvt=rss":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx5oss/cdn94@2020_3/2022/03/14/08-15-10-346_cc5c7e20b7a48857.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1647245705083},{"createdTime":"2022-03-14 16:15:05","updatedTime":"2022-03-14 16:15:05","title":"What Is Brand Perception? How to Measure It and 4 Examples","link":"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/what-is-brand-perception","description":"<p>If you take a second to think about your shopping habits, you'll probably realize that a majority of the products you buy are influenced by brand perception. You're not the only one — <a href=\"https://learn.g2.com/branding-statistics\"><span>77% of B2C consumers</span></a> make purchasing decisions based solely on the brand name.</p>  \n<p>Brand perception, or the thoughts and feelings associated with a company, impacts why people wear a certain brand of clothing or pick one pasta sauce over another at the grocery store. Once consumers adopt an attitude about a brand, it's tough to change. That's why brands work hard to create positive associations in people's minds, rather than negative or neutral perceptions.</p> \n<p>When you know how people perceive your brand, it's easier to shape its reputation, help consumers understand what sets it apart, and develop brand equity. You do this by measuring brand perception and tracking customer sentiment over time.</p> \n<p>But before diving into the metrics, it's important to understand what creates brand perception and how it informs company and consumer decision-making.</p> \n<p><a class=\"cta_button\" href=\"https://www.hubspot.com/cs/ci/?pg=814dd420-0d49-40e0-b59c-f01066e186c1&amp;pid=53&amp;ecid=&amp;hseid=&amp;hsic=\"><img class=\"hs-cta-img \" style=\"border-width: 0px; /*hs-extra-styles*/; margin: 0 auto; display: block; margin-top: 20px; margin-bottom: 20px\" alt=\"Download Now: Free Brand Building Guide\" src=\"https://no-cache.hubspot.com/cta/default/53/814dd420-0d49-40e0-b59c-f01066e186c1.png\" align=\"middle\"></a></p> \n<h2>What is brand perception?</h2> \n<p>Brand perception is the sum of a consumer's feelings, experiences, and thoughts about a product or service. It's what people believe a brand represents, rather than what a brand says it represents.</p> \n<p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/brand%20perception-v1.jpg?width=1794&amp;name=brand%20perception-v1.jpg\" alt=\"How to Understand the Value of Brand perception\" width=\"1794\" style=\"width: 1794px;\"></p> \n<p>Although brand perception is a mental association, it plays an essential role in creating emotional connections with consumers. People consider their attitude toward brands when choosing between competing products. They read reviews, chat with customer support, compare options with friends, or sign up for a free trial. All of these touchpoints affect brand perception and impact a company's success.</p> \n<p>If consumers think highly of a brand, they become more loyal to it. Consider how this dynamic plays out in everyday life. People get in meme wars over <a href=\"https://www.google.com/search?q=apple+vs+android+meme&amp;client=firefox-b-1-d&amp;source=lnms&amp;tbm=isch&amp;sa=X&amp;ved=2ahUKEwiT_ryuu_r0AhVKaM0KHf2QAxcQ_AUoAXoECAEQAw&amp;biw=1423&amp;bih=741&amp;dpr=2#imgrc=QFWJsh5kwFIW0M\"><span>Apple versus Android</span></a> products. A person who wears Nike shoes usually won't be caught in Adidas kicks. And you probably won't find Coca-Cola and Pepsi in the same fridge.</p> \n<p>Companies that understand brand perception use this information to develop <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/marketing/brand-equity\"><span>brand equity</span></a>. While brand perception can be narrowed down to what one customer thinks about your brand, brand equity is the combination of people's perceptions, experiences, and opinions that creates your reputation. A company with high brand equity attracts loyal customers who pick your product or service when given the choice between competitors.</p> \n<p>When a customer is <a href=\"https://home.kpmg/xx/en/home/insights/2019/11/customer-loyalty-survey.html\"><span>loyal to a brand</span></a>, 86% will recommend it to friends or family and 66% are likely to write a positive review. Those actions drive company growth and improve brand perception, which only helps your business.</p> \n<p>Although it may seem that brand perception is out of your hands, you can take steps to measure it and improve people's attitudes.</p> \n<h2>How to Measure Brand Perception</h2> \n<p>Data can help you understand how consumers, employees, stakeholders, and competitors perceive your brand. Since brand perception is a combination of reviews, reputation, experience, functionality, advertising, social engagement, and customer use, you should gather metrics from multiple sources.</p> \n<p>Here's how to measure brand perception:</p> \n<ul> \n <li><strong>Conduct brand perception surveys</strong> to learn what people think of your business and how it stacks up against competitors. Ask questions that touch on emotional, cognitive, and action-oriented factors, such as these examples from <a href=\"https://www.qualtrics.com/uk/experience-management/brand/perception-surveys/\"><span>Qualtrics</span></a>: \n  <ul> \n   <li>When you think of [the brand], what comes to mind first?</li> \n   <li>Which of the following words describe [the brand]?</li> \n   <li>What kind of feelings do you experience when you think of [the brand]?</li> \n   <li>How would you describe your level of emotional attachment to [the brand]?</li> \n   <li>How would you describe [the brand] to a friend?</li> \n   <li>How would you describe your last experience with [the brand]?</li> \n   <li>On a scale of 1-10, how likely are you to recommend [the brand] to a friend or colleague?</li> \n  </ul> </li> \n <li><strong>Track online mentions</strong> using <a href=\"https://info.campussonar.com/social-listening-basics\">social listening</a> tools or Google alerts. You want to monitor social media comments, online reviews, relevant hashtags, forums (i.e. Reddit and Quora), and news mentions. As the brand grows, so will this dataset. I recommend creating a system to handle negative mentions as soon as possible and stay on top of talk about your brand, products, and marketing campaigns.</li> \n <li><strong>Do a brand audit</strong> to evaluate how your brand perception compares to competitors'. This should include research on primary and secondary target audiences, a competitive analysis of your products or services, a thorough evaluation of your communications strategy, and a deep dive into your <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/sales/brand-positioning-strategy\"><span>brand positioning</span></a>. (I recommend referencing this brand audit guide from <a href=\"https://visme.co/blog/brand-audit/\"><span>Visme</span></a>).</li> \n <li><strong>Collect data from customers</strong> at each point of the <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/sales/what-is-the-buyers-journey\"><span>buyer's journey</span></a>. This can include how buyers research information, evaluate products, compare between competitors, interact with customer support, make a purchase decision, onboard, and interact with the brand post-purchase.</li> \n</ul> \n<p>Once you have enough data to measure brand perception, you can evaluate if consumer sentiment aligns with your brand identity. If so, stay the course. If not, you can learn how to improve <a href=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/service/improve-customer-perception\"><span>consumer brand perception</span></a>.</p> \n<h2>Brand Perception Examples</h2> \n<p>From PR campaigns to packaging, brand perception is influenced by every touchpoint people have with a company. The following brand perception examples show how businesses can shape consumer sentiments so the inner identity matches the outer image.</p> \n<h3>1. Snickers</h3> \n<p>Candy lovers can choose between dozens of chocolate-covered bars, so what makes someone grab a Snickers instead of a Kit Kat? Yes, it may be taste or preference, but the brand has designed clever campaigns to make people believe that eating Snickers will transform you from hangry and unfocused to sharp and satisfied.</p> \n<div class=\"hs-embed-wrapper\" style=\"position: relative; overflow: hidden; width: 100%; height: auto; padding: 0; max-width: 560px; max-height: 315px; min-width: 256px; display: block; margin: auto;\">\n <div class=\"hs-embed-content-wrapper\">\n  <div style=\"position: relative; overflow: hidden; max-width: 100%; padding-bottom: 56.25%; margin: 0px;\">\n   <iframe width=\"560\" height=\"315\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/DZdvFTgmeo0\" frameborder=\"0\" allowfullscreen style=\"position: absolute; top: 0px; left: 0px; width: 100%; height: 100%; border: none;\"></iframe>\n  </div>\n </div>\n</div> \n<h3>2. Orangetheory</h3> \n<p>You may have driven past one of these orange-hued workout studios on your daily commute or taken an online class during the pandemic. And while fitness crazes come and go, Orangetheory has carved out a brand perception that's kept the company going strong since 2010. The community-oriented classes make it the right fit for people looking to connect and compete with neighbors while working up a sweat. It's more casual than Crossfit but kicks up the intensity compared to group classes at national gyms, like Planet Fitness and LA Fitness.<img src=\"https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/ME__19BmV3Gala0b9NqcYZWJKV0IlAbLZL9yAnJuGUhHivg3UmUYK1DhiqTHmySWmdOhbnQ4STomwJRFff8Pxigjmpi6HvcWyAR3WY7kYZnpUMAswU3pCECqqMobzxwCeP76S2gA\" width=\"455\" height=\"546\" style=\"margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; display: block;\" alt=\"Orange Theory Fitness Brand Perception\"></p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center; font-size: 12px;\"><a href=\"https://tombras.com/campaign/orangetheory-fitness\">Image Source</a></p> \n<h3>3. Zoom</h3> \n<p>An innovative and beloved video platform at the start of the pandemic, Zoom quickly became the cause of remote workers' burnout. People loved how it kept them connected to teams, families, and friends.</p> \n<p>But the constant connection led to \"Zoom fatigue,\" an informal diagnosis that's been covered by Healthline, <a href=\"https://news.stanford.edu/2021/02/23/four-causes-zoom-fatigue-solutions/\"><span>Stanford</span></a>, the New York Times, and more. While companies still rely on Zoom for virtual meetings, the brand has had to adjust from its original \"Video conferencing that doesn't suck\" vibe to \"How the world connects\" as <a href=\"https://adage.com/article/marketing-news-strategy/zoom-launches-ad-campaign-aiming-keep-growing-beyond-pandemic/2364921\"><span>consumers shifted their perceptions</span></a>.</p> \n<p><img src=\"https://blog.hubspot.com/hs-fs/hubfs/Zoom-Meetings.jpg?width=624&amp;name=Zoom-Meetings.jpg\" alt=\"Zoom fatigue meme: 1st day of Zoom meetings vs. 14th day of Zoom meetings\" width=\"624\" style=\"width: 624px;\"></p> \n<p style=\"text-align: center; font-size: 12px;\"><a href=\"https://www.remote.tools/memes/zoom-memes\"><span>Image Source</span></a></p> \n<h3>4. Patagonia</h3> \n<p>The outdoor gear brand became famous for its innovative clothing and focus on responsible manufacturing, but a change in consumer perception caused the company to double down on its sustainability-driven identity.</p> \n<p>In the early 2010s, people began referring to the company as Patagucci — a satirical name that poked fun at the brand's high prices and its adoption among high-income workers. To sway consumers from placing Patagonia in the fast-fashion category, the company has launched a number of sustainability-focused initiatives, like its Worn Wear line of recycled clothing.</p> \n<div class=\"hs-embed-wrapper\" style=\"position: relative; overflow: hidden; width: 100%; height: auto; padding: 0; max-width: 560px; max-height: 315px; min-width: 256px; display: block; margin: auto;\">\n <div class=\"hs-embed-content-wrapper\">\n  <div style=\"position: relative; overflow: hidden; max-width: 100%; padding-bottom: 56.25%; margin: 0px;\">\n   <iframe width=\"560\" height=\"315\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/cMgfVenLRSI\" frameborder=\"0\" allowfullscreen style=\"position: absolute; top: 0px; left: 0px; width: 100%; height: 100%; border: none;\"></iframe>\n  </div>\n </div>\n</div> \n<p>&nbsp;</p> \n<p>Knowing what people think of your brand is an important part of developing a successful business. It gives you the information you need to shape your brand identity, create impactful marketing campaigns, and make changes when consumer perception shifts.</p> \n<p>Now that you know how to measure
